The `revealBlockInView(view, blockId)` helper searches the doc for the `<!-- ^<uuid> -->` stable-id marker (case-insensitive — on-disk markers are lowercase but a hand-typed link could be upper) and dispatches a `selection` + `scrollIntoView` effect; returns `false` when the marker isn't present so the caller knows to fall back to the resolver-supplied `root_index`. The plugin's `activate()` builds an `onBlockLinkNavigate` callback that (1) calls `editorClient.resolveBlockLink` to validate the link — a stale id surfaces as a notification rather than silently scrolling nowhere — (2) emits `files:open` with the target path, (3) records the pending `(relpath, blockId)` reveal, and (4) emits a `nexus.editor:reveal-block` event whose handler tries `revealBlockInView` immediately, then again after 80 ms / 250 ms so the reveal lands whether the file was already open or had to be loaded fresh. New CSS class `.cm-md-block-link` underlines + recolours the source range using the existing `--accent` token. Threaded through `EditorRuntime.onBlockLinkNavigate` so the live-mode extension stack only wires the click handler when activate() supplied one (test drivers without a full plugin runtime don't get the side-effect path). Coverage: 9 new node:test cases — 2 decoration tests (one mark per link, ignores plain wikilinks + heading anchors), 3 reveal tests (scrolls to marker line, returns false when absent, case-insensitive UUID match), 4 click-routing tests (plain left-click navigates with `preventDefault`, every chord variant + right/middle button falls through, out-of-range click falls through, pipe-aliased label flows through into the callback). `pnpm --filter nexus-shell typecheck` clean; `pnpm --filter nexus-shell lint` 0 new warnings; `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 624 passing (was 615; +9).

- **BL-049 phase 1 — resolver IPC + shared parser** _(shipped 2026-04-30)_: ships the kernel-side foundation that the click-through navigation UX (phase 2) and the backlinks panel (phase 3) sit on top of. New IPC handler `com.nexus.editor::resolve_block_link` (handler id 13) takes `{ file_relpath, block_id }` (UUID per ADR 0017's `<!-- ^<uuid> -->` marker) and returns `{ found, block, root_index }`. Two-tier lookup: when the file is already open as an editor session the handler reads the in-memory block tree (so unsaved edits flow through); otherwise it parses the file from disk transiently without polluting the session map. `root_index` is the position in `tree.root_blocks` of the target block's root ancestor — the resolver walks `parent_id` up the tree before recording the index, which is the granularity the shell's "scroll into view" path needs before per-block source-position metadata lands. Async + sync dispatch paths share the same `resolve_in_session` / `resolve_in_tree` helpers; sync routes through `fs::read_to_string` for the context-less unit-test fallback, async routes through `com.nexus.storage::read_file`. Wired through [`nexus-bootstrap`](../../crates/nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs). Shell-side: new pure module [`shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/blockLinks.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/blockLinks.ts) defines the canonical `[[<file>#^<uuid>]]` syntax + optional `|label` alias (`parseBlockLinks`, `serializeBlockLink`, `blockLinkAt`); the regex requires a v4-shaped UUID after `#^` so a bare `[[A.md#some-heading]]` (heading anchor) doesn't masquerade as a block link. UUID casing is normalised to lowercase on parse so the on-disk marker (which `format_stable_id_marker` emits lowercase) and any user-typed link agree. New typed `EditorKernelClient.resolveBlockLink(file, id)` wrapper plus the `ResolveBlockLinkResponse` interface mirrors the Rust handler's wire shape. Coverage: 5 cargo tests on the resolver (in-session happy path, fs-fallback for closed sessions via stamp + save + close + reopen, not-found for unknown id, root-walk for nested blocks via a synthetic tree, invalid-uuid rejection); 13 node:test cases on the shell parser (no-op on plain markdown, bare + pipe-aliased forms, heading-anchor rejection, malformed-UUID rejection, casing normalisation, multi-link ranges, regex reentrancy, offset translation, `blockLinkAt` happy/miss, serializer round-trip with and without label, serializer rejection of bad inputs); 1 new kernel-client test pinning the snake_case wire shape. `cargo test -p nexus-editor` 206 passing (was 201; +5); `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean; `pnpm --filter nexus-shell typecheck` clean; `pnpm --filter nexus-shell lint` 0 new warnings; `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 615 passing (was 601; +14).

### BL-042: AI-DIR Nexus-as-MCP-server ✅ (2026-04-30)

**Delivered:** AI-INTEGRATION-DIRECTIONS direction 7 lands as a stdio MCP **server** in [`crates/nexus-mcp/src/server.rs`](../../crates/nexus-mcp/src/server.rs), driven by `nexus mcp` ([`crates/nexus-cli/src/commands/mcp.rs`](../../crates/nexus-cli/src/commands/mcp.rs) `serve`) so external IDEs and Claude Desktop can drive a Nexus forge through the same kernel IPC boundary the CLI / TUI / shell already use. Distinct from BL-023 / BL-024 / BL-025 (those stay on the *client* / Host side). **Tool surface (15)**: `nexus_read_note` / `nexus_create_note` / `nexus_update_note` / `nexus_delete_note` / `nexus_list_notes` (CRUD over `com.nexus.storage::read_file` / `write_file` / `delete_file` / `query_files`); `nexus_search` (rebuild-then-query against `com.nexus.storage::search`); `nexus_backlinks` / `nexus_outgoing_links` / `nexus_graph_status` (knowledge-graph readers); `nexus_list_tags` / `nexus_list_tasks` / `nexus_toggle_task` (forge metadata); `nexus_ask` (RAG via `com.nexus.ai::ask` with a 120 s IPC timeout to absorb provider RTT); and the BL-042 closing skills pair `nexus_list_skills` / `nexus_render_skill` (call `com.nexus.skills::list` / `render` so authored prompt templates from `.forge/skills/` are reachable as named, parameter-substituted prompts from any MCP client — the `run_skill` slot called out in the BL-042 entry). **Resource surface**: forge notes are also enumerated under `mcp://nexus/notes/<vault-relative-path>` via `list_resources` / `read_resource` (BL-026 path) so clients with a Resources UI see the vault as a browsable tree alongside the tools; the listing root `mcp://nexus/notes` is intentionally non-readable. **Plumbing**: `NexusMcpServer::new(Arc<KernelPluginContext>)` plus three thin `*_call<T>` helpers — `storage_call` (30 s timeout against `com.nexus.storage`), `skills_call` (30 s against `com.nexus.skills`), and a direct 120 s `ipc_call` for `com.nexus.ai::ask`. `ServerInfo::with_instructions(…)` advertises notes + skills + the resource prefix to the connecting client so Claude Desktop's "what can this server do?" prompt is self-documenting. Every tool is capability-checked at the kernel because every call funnels through `context.ipc_call(...)` rather than touching engines directly — same trust posture as the CLI / TUI. **Trust boundary**: stdio only — `serve_stdio()` wraps the server in `rmcp::transport::io::stdio()` so the parent process (Claude Desktop / IDE) is the trust boundary; no TCP listener, no auth layer, no off-host reachability (pre-audited 2026-04-16, see the security follow-ups below). **Coverage**: `cargo test -p nexus-mcp` 51 passing (was 46; +5 net) — new `render_skill_input_defaults_values_to_empty_map`, `render_skill_input_round_trips_values_map`, `list_skills_output_serializes_count_and_skills`, `render_skill_output_serializes_id_name_body` plus the existing `parse_note_uri_*` / `build_note_resource_*` shape tests. `cargo clippy -p nexus-mcp --all-targets` clean; `bash scripts/check_ipc_drift.sh` clean (the new tools are plain `serde_json::Value` round-trips against existing `com.nexus.skills` handlers — no IPC-typed structs changed). **Out of scope**: WebSocket / HTTP transport (the trust-boundary follow-up flagged that an auth layer must land alongside any non-stdio transport); MCP **Prompts** surface (the natural pairing with skills, but the `nexus_render_skill` tool already lets clients invoke skills today — promoting them to first-class `prompts/list` is a follow-up if a client appears that prefers that channel); a daemonised long-running server (today `nexus mcp` is a one-shot stdio child of its launcher, which is what Claude Desktop / Cursor / Cline expect).

### BL-037: AMB activity timeline ✅ (2026-04-30)

**Delivered:** AI-AMBIENT-COPILOT-PLAN pattern 7 lands as a per-forge JSONL log + a default-off shell pane that mirrors what every AI surface in the app just did. **Recorder** ([`crates/nexus-ai/src/activity_log.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/activity_log.rs)): new module owning `ActivityEntry { id, timestamp (RFC3339 UTC), session_id, surface, provider, model, prompt, files, tool_calls, outcome, error, duration_ms }` plus the `ActivitySurface` (`chat` / `ask` / `cmdi` / `ghost` / `complete` / `enrich` / `other`) and `ActivityOutcome` (`ok` / `error` / `cancelled`) enums and the `ActivityToolCall { name, ok }` row type. `ActivityRecorder { ctx: Arc<KernelPluginContext>, write_lock: Arc<Mutex<()>> }` exposes `append(entry)` (best-effort fire-and-forget — disk failures `tracing::warn` and return), `read_all() -> Vec<ActivityEntry>` (oldest first; corrupt lines are skipped, not fatal), and `clear()` (deletes the on-disk file). The `Mutex<()>` serializes the read-modify-write window so two AI calls finishing at the same instant don't lose entries; the `Arc<KernelPluginContext>` clone keeps recorder cheap for handler futures. Storage path is `<forge>/.forge/ai-activity.log` (`ACTIVITY_LOG_PATH` constant); each entry is one JSON object per line. `ACTIVITY_LOG_MAX_BYTES = 256 KiB` triggers `head_trim_bytes` head-truncation to keep the file ≈1k entries; `ACTIVITY_PROMPT_MAX_CHARS = 256` clamps prompt text on append (Unicode-safe, ellipsis-suffixed). `append` `delete_file`s before `write_file` to sidestep the `KernelPluginContext::write_file` validator's `tail = ""` bug that appends a trailing `/` when overwriting an existing file (EISDIR on `tokio::fs::write`); the recorder is the only writer of this file so a stale read between delete + write is impossible. After a successful write the recorder publishes `com.nexus.ai.activity_appended` with the entry payload so subscribers can update without polling. **IPC** ([`crates/nexus-ai/src/core_plugin.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/core_plugin.rs) + [`ipc.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/ipc.rs)): two new handlers — `HANDLER_ACTIVITY_LIST = 18` (args [`AiActivityListArgs { limit?: u32 }`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/ipc.rs); returns [`AiActivityListResult { entries: Vec<ActivityEntry> }`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/ipc.rs) newest-first) and `HANDLER_ACTIVITY_CLEAR = 19` (`{ cleared: bool }`). Both short-circuit before the `ctx.ok_or_else` arm in `dispatch_async` so the shell pane can hydrate even if it polls before `wire_context` runs (returns empty / `cleared:false` when the recorder is `None`). `AiCorePlugin` gains `activity: Option<ActivityRecorder>` populated in `wire_context` next to the `ToolRegistry` seed so the recorder shares the same `Arc<KernelPluginContext>` as the rest of the plugin. **Recording hooks**: `handle_stream_chat` and `handle_stream_ask` capture pre-flight metadata (provider / model / prompt / surface / `Instant::now()`) up front and record an `ActivityEntry` on every exit path — provider unconfigured, embed unconfigured (ask only), retrieve failure, provider build failure, dispatch error, cancellation, success — so an error timeline is just as useful as a success timeline. `run_tool_dispatch_loop` now returns a typed `ToolDispatchOutcome { text, tool_calls: Vec<ActivityToolCall>, files: Vec<String> }` instead of bare `String`; tool calls are recorded with `ok = !is_error`, and any tool input carrying a `path` field (read_file / write_file / note_append / similar) contributes a deduped entry to `files`. `handle_stream_ask` populates `files` from the RAG sources that grounded the answer, deduped while preserving retrieval order. `handle_stream_chat` accepts a new optional `surface` field on `AiStreamChatArgs` (`chat` / `cmdi` / `ghost` / `complete` / `enrich` / `other`) so callers tag their events; default heuristic = `chat` (or `complete` when `mode=complete`). `resolve_surface(explicit, mode)` does the resolution; `last_user_prompt` extracts the most recent user message for the timeline regardless of provider's history shape. Errors flow through one shared `record_activity_error` so the entry shape is identical across error paths. **Shell pane** ([`shell/src/plugins/nexus/activityTimeline/`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/activityTimeline/)): new default-off `nexus.activityTimeline` plugin contributing a `paneMode` view + activity-bar item (priority 55, between AI chat at 50 and Processes at 60). `activityTimelineStore.ts` mirrors the on-disk JSONL inside a Zustand store with a `TIMELINE_ENTRIES_CAP = 1000` ring; `prepend(entry)` drops the oldest when at cap. `ActivityTimelineView.tsx` renders a header + toolbar (text filter, surface dropdown, clear button, count) + entry list, each entry showing `HH:MM:SS  surface  outcome-glyph  prompt  duration` on the primary line and `model / files (1 + N more) / tool ✓ tool ✗ / error` on the secondary line. The clear button calls `com.nexus.ai::activity_clear` via the kernel and empties the local store. `index.ts` hydrates the store from `com.nexus.ai::activity_list` on activate (and on every activity-bar route), then subscribes to `com.nexus.ai.activity_appended` so live activity prepends without polling. Lifecycle ties to `workspace:opened` / `workspace:closed` (subscribe / unsubscribe) and covers the boot race by hydrating + subscribing immediately if `api.kernel.available()` is already `true`. PluginRegistry sweeps the bus disposer on plugin unload. Catalog wiring: `DEFAULT_OFF_PLUGINS` immediately after `processesPlugin` with the same paired-with-AI-plugin rationale as `recallPlugin` / `enrichPlugin` (the timeline only produces meaningful output once the AI plugin is configured). **Manifest** ([`crates/nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs`](../../crates/nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs)): two new entries `("activity_list", HANDLER_ACTIVITY_LIST)` and `("activity_clear", HANDLER_ACTIVITY_CLEAR)` on the `com.nexus.ai` core manifest. **Wire schemas** ([`crates/nexus-bootstrap/tests/ipc_schema_emit.rs`](../../crates/nexus-bootstrap/tests/ipc_schema_emit.rs)): six new schemas emitted under `com_nexus_ai__activity_list_*` (args, result, entry, surface, outcome, tool_call); TypeScript bindings emit alongside (`ActivityEntry.ts`, `ActivityOutcome.ts`, `ActivitySurface.ts`, `ActivityToolCall.ts`, `AiActivityListArgs.ts`, `AiActivityListResult.ts`); `AiStreamChatArgs.ts` + JSON schema regenerated for the new `surface` field. **Coverage**: `cargo test -p nexus-ai` 167 passing (was 152 pre-BL-037; +14 net + the 1 pre-existing test count delta from `ToolDispatchOutcome` propagation). New tests: 7 in `activity_log::tests` (`truncate_prompt` Unicode + at-limit + grapheme-boundary; `head_trim_bytes` under-cap + drops-leading-lines + no-newline-after-cut; `surface_from_str_lossy` aliases incl. `cmd-i` + `cmd_i`; `entry_round_trips_through_jsonl` snake-case + `outcome:"ok"` + skip empty optionals); 7 dispatch-path tests in `core_plugin::semantic_search_dispatch_tests` (`activity_handler_ids_are_pinned` at 18/19; `activity_list_returns_empty_when_recorder_unwired`; `activity_clear_returns_cleared_false_when_recorder_unwired`; `activity_recorder_round_trips_through_disk` end-to-ends two appends + `activity_list` newest-first contract + files survive JSONL round-trip; `activity_list_respects_limit_arg`; `activity_clear_truncates_log` exercises the full add-list-clear-list cycle). Existing `dispatch_loop_executes_tool_and_loops` / `dispatch_loop_marks_unknown_tool_as_error` updated to assert the new `tool_calls` + `files` recording fields. New helper `wired_plugin_with_caps(caps)` pre-creates `<tempdir>/.forge/` so writes succeed without the storage plugin (mirrors what production does at storage `on_init`); existing semantic-search tests keep using `wired_plugin()` (default empty caps). `cargo test --workspace` clean. `cargo clippy -p nexus-ai --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean. `pnpm --filter nexus-shell typecheck` clean; `pnpm --filter nexus-shell lint` no new warnings; `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 537 passing (no new shell-side unit tests — the pane is render-only over the store and the lifecycle reuses the same hydrate-on-activate idiom as `nexus.processes`, exercised end-to-end by the catalog typecheck + `pnpm test`). `bash scripts/check_ipc_drift.sh` clean after the regenerate. **Out of scope**: full-text search across the activity log (today the shell pane filters in-memory; a Tantivy index over `.forge/ai-activity.log` is a follow-up once the log shape stabilises); export to JSON / CSV (the JSONL file IS the export — `cat .forge/ai-activity.log`); summarisation surface ("what did I work on today?" answered by chat over the file is a follow-up routed through the existing `stream_ask` path); pushing the pane into a BL-029 multi-window dedicated leaf (the activity-bar + paneMode pairing is the v1 surface; the multi-window host can wrap the same `ActivityTimelineView` once the slot contract for non-tab views is finalised). Shipped commit `be9d02f`.

### BL-010: `nexus ai chat` interactive REPL ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** PRD-05 §3.5.2 / §10.2's multi-turn chat REPL is now wired up as a CLI consumer of the shared `com.nexus.ai::stream_chat` engine. New [`AiCommand::Chat`](../../crates/nexus-cli/src/main.rs) variant takes `--context <FILE>` / `--model <NAME>` / `--session <ID>` / `--system <PROMPT>` flags. [`commands::ai::chat`](../../crates/nexus-cli/src/commands/ai.rs) drives a [`rustyline = "14"`](../../Cargo.toml) line editor (added as a workspace dependency), dispatching each user turn through `runtime.context.ipc_call("com.nexus.ai", "stream_chat", { mode: "chat", ...messages, session_id })` while a parallel `tokio::spawn` task drains `EventFilter::CustomPrefix("com.nexus.ai.stream_")` and prints chunks to stdout. The bus contract is exercised through one shared `stream_and_collect` pump that BL-011 also uses — same drain + same session-id correlation, so the two surfaces produce byte-identical wire events. Slash commands cover `/help` / `/clear` / `/save <FILE>` / `/model <NAME>` / `/context <FILE>` / `/system <PROMPT>` / `/quit`. `/save` writes a Markdown transcript; `/model` round-trips through `config` + `set_config` (the AI plugin's `set_config` keys on the full provider record, so a "set just the model" is a read-modify-write). Exit codes match shell convention: `0` on EOF / `/quit`, `1` on any IPC error, `130` on Ctrl-C at the prompt (mapped from `ReadlineError::Interrupted` so wrapping shells see the canonical interrupted code). Coverage: `cargo test -p nexus-cli` 45 passing including 8 new tests in [`commands::ai::tests`](../../crates/nexus-cli/src/commands/ai.rs) covering `build_chat_args` round-trip + multi-byte-safe `slice_prompt` (shared with BL-011). Shipped commit `2a5b1fd`.

### BL-011: `nexus ai complete` CLI ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** PRD-05 §3.5.3 / §10.3's headless completion CLI ships as the twin of BL-034 — same engine call shape (`mode = "complete"`, `tools = "none"`, `trim = true`, `max_tokens = 64`, `stop = ["\n\n"]`), different rendering boundary. New [`AiCommand::Complete { file, line, col, context_lines }`](../../crates/nexus-cli/src/main.rs) variant + [`commands::ai::complete`](../../crates/nexus-cli/src/commands/ai.rs) reads the file via `storage_ipc::read_file`, slices the prefix at `(--line, --col)` (1-based, char-boundary-safe so multi-byte codepoints aren't split), optionally clamps to the last `--context N` lines, then issues a single `stream_chat` call through the same `stream_and_collect` pump BL-010 uses. Engine post-processing (prompt-echo strip + natural-break clip + stop-sequence truncation) runs server-side per the shared engine contract — the CLI just prints the resulting `text`. Coverage: 6 of the 8 new `commands::ai::tests` cases target `slice_prompt` directly (whole-file default, line-end clip, mid-line col clip, context-window cap, multi-byte safety, line-overshoot clamp); the engine call shape is exercised end-to-end by the BL-034 ghost path. Shipped commit `2a5b1fd`.

### BL-031: Bases cell / row clipboard ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** Mod-C / Mod-X / Mod-V on a focused `.bases` leaf now copy a rectangular cell range (anchor + shift-click), a single selected row, or paste either of those — gated on `when: 'bases.focused && !bases.editing'` so the chords don't shadow `CellEditor` input. Each paste enrols **one** `HistoryEntry` so undo/redo round-trips the bulk operation, satisfying the BL-030 pairing requirement. New [`shell/src/plugins/nexus/bases/clipboard.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/bases/clipboard.ts) owns the pure helpers (TSV serialization, JSON payload format, parser, per-cell coercion via `fieldTypes.ts`); new [`tableClipboard.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/bases/tableClipboard.ts) is a registry-of-one (mirror of `activeBases.ts`) so the plugin's `cut/copy/paste` commands route through whichever table currently owns focus. Two typed clipboard MIME payloads ride alongside `text/plain` TSV: `application/x-nexus-bases-cells` for rectangular ranges and `application/x-nexus-bases-rows` for whole records — external apps still see the TSV grid, while cross-base paste preserves typing. Three paste modes land per the BL-031 plan: **range** (rectangle → tile/clip when source != range size; single-cell selection treats source as anchor + extent), **single-row** (record selected → shallow-merge by field name), and **no-selection** (typed `rows` payload or TSV-with-header → append new records via `base_record_create`). Cross-base coercion keys on `coerceValue(destKind, value, sourceKind)` — same-type values pass through unflagged, otherwise the per-cell coercion attempt either succeeds (numbers strip currency / percent symbols, text joins multi-select arrays with `, `, etc.) or drops to `null` and trips `coercedCount`. When `coercedCount > 0` the table emits a `bases:paste-coerced` notification via `api.notifications.show`. Read-only column types (`formula` / `rollup` / `lookup` / `uuid` / `relation`) are skipped at both copy and paste edges via `isPasteable`. Cell-range selection lives on a new `cellSelection: CellRange | null` field in `BasesTabState` — disjoint from the existing `selectedRecordId` (setting one clears the other) so the two selection modes don't shadow each other in the keyboard handlers. New `bases.editing` context-key is published from `BasesTable` on every `editing` state change so the `when:` clause resolves correctly. Coverage: `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 444 passing including 14 new BL-031 tests in [`basesStore.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/bases/basesStore.test.ts) covering `normalizeRange` flip, `rangeContains` edges, `cellToTsv` / `cellsToTsv` / `rowsToTsv` / `parseTsv` round-trips, six `coerceValue` scenarios, `isPasteable`, and the disjoint-selection-modes invariant. Shipped commit `c30a237`.

### BL-019: AI local embeddings backend ✅ (2026-04-29)

**Delivered:** PRD-12 §9.1's local-embeddings escape hatch lands as a new [`crates/nexus-ai/src/local_embedding.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/local_embedding.rs) module gated behind a new `local-embeddings` Cargo feature, per ADR 0018 ([fastembed-rs vs candle vs sqlite-lembed](../adr/0018-embedding-backend.md)). Pre-BL-019 `nexus-ai`'s embedding path was strictly remote (`OpenAiProvider` / `OllamaProvider`), so a fully-offline forge could not produce vectors. **Backend** ([`local_embedding.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/local_embedding.rs)): `LocalEmbedding { inner: Mutex<TextEmbedding>, dim, cache: DashMap<u64, Vec<f32>>, cache_max_entries }` wraps fastembed-rs's `TextEmbedding`. The Mutex around `inner` is forced by fastembed v5's `&mut self` signature on `embed` (the underlying ORT session holds non-Sync state during a forward pass); the `EmbeddingProvider` trait's `&self` shape is preserved so callers don't change. **Trait + cache** (sub-task 2): `embed_with_cache(cache, cache_max, texts, fetch_fn)` is factored as a free function so the cache logic — hit / partial-miss / mismatch / over-budget eviction / disabled — can be exercised with a closure-stub `fetch_fn` that doesn't pull the BGE weights from `HuggingFace`. Cache keys are `xxhash3_64`; eviction is a coarse "drop everything when over budget" sweep (sub-LRU sophistication isn't worth the bookkeeping for a re-index that pays for itself within one run). **RAG wire-up** (sub-task 3): [`crates/nexus-ai/src/core_plugin.rs::build_embedding_provider`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/core_plugin.rs) learns `provider == "local"` and routes to `build_local_embedding_provider(cfg)`, which is `cfg(feature = "local-embeddings")`-gated; the `not(feature)` branch returns a clear actionable error string instead of `unwrap`-ing or panicking, so a binary built without the feature is honest about it. `AiConfig` gains an optional `local_embedding_model` field consulted only when `provider == "local"` (default `bge-small-en-v1.5-int8` per ADR 0018; users override via the new `NEXUS_LOCAL_EMBEDDING_MODEL` env var). New `detect_local_embedding()` reads `NEXUS_LOCAL_EMBEDDINGS=1` (truthy: `1`/`true`/`yes`/`on`) and is preferred over remote providers in `detect_embedding_provider()` so opt-in users get the offline path automatically. The existing `vectorstore.rs` ChunkMatch shape is unchanged — local just slots into the same trait. **Batch indexer hook** (sub-task 4): public `LocalEmbedding::embed_batch(&self, &[String])` is the throughput-optimized path BL-041 will consume — batches over `BATCH_CACHE_BYPASS_THRESHOLD = 1_000` skip the per-key `DashMap` touch entirely and go straight to fastembed's bulk embed; smaller batches still pay the cache. The `EmbeddingProvider::embed` trait method delegates to `embed_batch` so callers get the same routing without knowing the threshold. **Model registry**: `map_model(name)` resolves caller-supplied identifiers (`bge-small-en-v1.5-int8` / `bge-small-en-v1.5` / `bge-base-en-v1.5` / `bge-large-en-v1.5` / `mxbai-embed-large-v1` / `nomic-embed-text-v1.5` / `all-minilm-l6-v2` and short aliases) to `fastembed::EmbeddingModel`. Empty + the canonical default both map to `BGESmallENV15Q`. Unknown ids return `AiError::Provider` so callers can fall back to remote without panicking. `model_dimension(model)` returns 384 / 768 / 1024 per family. **Cargo wiring** ([`crates/nexus-ai/Cargo.toml`](../../crates/nexus-ai/Cargo.toml)): `fastembed = { version = "5", optional = true, default-features = false, features = ["ort-load-dynamic", "hf-hub-rustls-tls"] }` + `dashmap = { version = "6", optional = true }` + `xxhash-rust = { version = "0.8", features = ["xxh3"], optional = true }`. Feature alias: `local-embeddings = ["dep:fastembed", "dep:dashmap", "dep:xxhash-rust"]`. The `ort-load-dynamic` choice (vs the ADR's hypothetical `ort-download-binaries` baseline) means cargo build doesn't reach for a network prebuilt-binary download — works in CI / sandboxed builds / air-gapped — and downstream deployments install `libonnxruntime` once via the system package manager (Debian: `libonnxruntime`; macOS: `brew install onnxruntime`) or set `ORT_DYLIB_PATH`. **Coverage**: `cargo test -p nexus-ai` 94 passing (default-feature build, unchanged from pre-BL-019 baseline) — the feature flag is correctly off in default builds. `cargo test -p nexus-ai --features local-embeddings` 102 passing (+8 net): `cache_hit_skips_fetch_call` / `partial_cache_hit_only_fetches_misses` / `cache_clears_when_over_budget` / `zero_capacity_disables_cache` / `empty_input_returns_empty_without_fetch` / `map_model_known_aliases` / `map_model_unknown_returns_provider_error` / `fetch_count_mismatch_is_provider_error`, plus one `#[ignore = "downloads ~33MB from HuggingFace on first run"]` round-trip test (`local_embedding_round_trip` — run with `cargo test -p nexus-ai --features local-embeddings -- --ignored` against a network-reachable + ORT-installed environment). `cargo clippy -p nexus-ai --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean both with and without the feature. `bash scripts/check_ipc_drift.sh` clean — `AiConfig.local_embedding_model` is internal only, not on the IPC boundary. **Out of scope**: pre-bundled BGE weights in the installer (still a first-call download from `HuggingFace`'s mirror; future installer track can pre-seed `~/.cache/fastembed/`); multilingual default (BGE-small-en is English; multilingual users set `local_embedding_model = "bge-m3"` once that lands in fastembed's enum); ADR 0008 addendum (parent task — separate doc PR). Shipped commits `5124c1b` (feature flag + skeleton), `17de317` (LocalEmbedding impl + cache + 8 unit tests), `b251814` (`provider = "local"` wire-up + config field + `detect_local_embedding`).

### BL-040: AI-DIR semantic search ✅ (2026-04-29)

**Delivered:** AI-INTEGRATION-DIRECTIONS direction 3 lands as a new `com.nexus.ai::semantic_search` IPC handler plus a default-off shell palette plugin that fans out to it alongside the existing keyword search. **Backend** ([`crates/nexus-ai/src/core_plugin.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/core_plugin.rs)): new `HANDLER_SEMANTIC_SEARCH: u32 = 13` on `com.nexus.ai`, args `{ query: String, limit?: usize (default 10) }`, returns `{ matches: Vec<ChunkMatch> }`. The handler mirrors `handle_ask`'s embedder-build path (`build_embedding_provider(&embed_cfg)`) but skips the chat half entirely — the embedded query vector is forwarded to `com.nexus.storage::vector_query` (handler 18) via the existing `vectorstore::search` IPC client. Library-side, [`rag::semantic_search`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/rag.rs) is a thin alias for `rag::retrieve` exposed under the handler-matching name so the function is grep-friendly and unit-testable independent of the dispatcher. **Manifest** ([`crates/nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs`](../../crates/nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs)): one new `("semantic_search", HANDLER_SEMANTIC_SEARCH)` entry on the `com.nexus.ai` core manifest so all four frontends (CLI, TUI, MCP, shell) reach it through the same `ipc_call` path. **Shell palette** ([`shell/src/plugins/nexus/semanticSearch/`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/semanticSearch/)): new default-off `nexus.semanticSearch` plugin contributing one palette command (`nexus.semanticSearch.run`, title "Search by Meaning", category "Search"). On invocation it `api.input.prompt`s for a query, then `Promise.all`s `com.nexus.storage::search` (keyword) + `com.nexus.ai::semantic_search` (semantic) — both are wrapped in `.catch(() => empty)` so a one-side failure (e.g. AI plugin off) still surfaces the other side's hits. The pure [`mergeResults(keyword, semantic, limit = 30)`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/semanticSearch/merge.ts) function normalises each list to `[0, 1]` by dividing by the in-list max (guarded against zero), then blends co-occurring `file_path`s at `0.5 * keyword + 0.5 * semantic` and damps single-source hits to `0.5 * normalised` — so a co-occurrence beats a single-source hit even when the raw scores would not, which is the BL-040 ranking rule's whole point. The merged list is sorted descending, capped at 30, and the top hit is opened via the existing `files:open` event the keyword search sidebar already uses; an `api.notifications.show` confirms the open or reports zero results. Snippet preference: keyword excerpt (FTS-highlighted) wins over semantic chunk text when both exist. The plugin is registered in `DEFAULT_OFF_PLUGINS` (paired with `aiPlugin`) so users don't see the command before the embedding backend is configured. **Coverage**: `cargo test -p nexus-ai` 99 passing (+5 net): three new in-module tests in [`rag.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/rag.rs) end-to-end the dispatcher path with a `StubEmbedder` + a `StubDispatcher` that intercepts `com.nexus.storage::vector_query` and asserts on the recorded args (target / command / `limit` / embedding vector); two new tests in `core_plugin.rs::semantic_search_dispatch_tests` exercise the `HANDLER_SEMANTIC_SEARCH` arm of `dispatch_async` via the missing-query and missing-embed-config error paths so we cover the routing without making a network call (a third pin-test asserts `HANDLER_SEMANTIC_SEARCH == 13` so the wire id can't drift silently). `cargo clippy -p nexus-ai --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean. `cargo test -p nexus-bootstrap` 11 passing; `cargo clippy -p nexus-bootstrap --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean. `pnpm --filter nexus-shell typecheck` clean; `pnpm --filter nexus-shell lint` clean (no new warnings); `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 471 passing (was 463) — 8 new merger tests in [`merge.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/semanticSearch/merge.test.ts) covering co-occurrence blending, single-source damping, the "co-occurrence beats single-source" invariant, the limit cap, empty input, divide-by-zero guard, and snippet preference (kw excerpt > semantic chunk text, with fallback). The co-located `*.test.ts` is re-imported from [`shell/tests/semantic-search-merge.test.ts`](../../shell/tests/semantic-search-merge.test.ts) so the workspace test runner (which globs `tests/*.test.ts`) picks it up. No IPC-boundary types changed (args/results stay inline `serde_json::Value`), so the drift check is a no-op for this BL. **Out of scope** per the task allowance: the `?:` palette-input prefix (the dedicated palette command alone is sufficient to ship the surface — the prefix is a UX polish a follow-up can add); a dedicated semantic-search sidebar view (today the result is opened; a results-list view + dedup-by-block UI is what BL-039 / BL-045 will likely want and we'd rather build it once); and any pre-warm of the embedding model (per the `LocalEmbedding` test discipline, the backend lazily fetches BGE on first call — a UI hint that the first query is slower belongs to the BL-019 onboarding pass). Shipped commits `79a9acb` (handler + rag helper + tests), `2e3f291` (bootstrap manifest), `a857d3d` (shell palette + merger + 8 unit tests).

### BL-041: AI-DIR background indexing daemon ✅ (2026-04-29)

**Delivered:** AI-INTEGRATION-DIRECTIONS direction 8 lands as a new [`crates/nexus-ai/src/indexing_daemon.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/indexing_daemon.rs) module that subscribes to the existing storage file-watcher, debounces bursts of saves, and re-runs `rag::index_file` (the BL-019 throughput-optimised path that bypasses the cache for >1k chunks per batch) without the user touching `nexus ai index_file`. **Daemon** ([`indexing_daemon.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/indexing_daemon.rs)): `IndexingDaemon::start(ctx, status, embedder_factory)` spawns a dedicated `nexus-ai-indexing-daemon` thread that owns its own current-thread tokio runtime — sidesteps any assumption about the frontend's runtime topology and keeps `ctx.ipc_call` (async) reachable without blocking the kernel scheduler. Pure-logic `Debouncer { touched: HashSet, deleted: HashSet, last_event: Option<Instant>, debounce: Duration, max_batch: usize }` collapses rapid saves into one re-index per path per flush window (default `DEFAULT_DEBOUNCE = 2 s` / `DEFAULT_MAX_BATCH = 32`); time is injected so unit tests are deterministic. Delete supersedes touch (`a.md` deleted then touched cancels the delete; touched then deleted fires a delete). `event_to_msg` translates `com.nexus.storage.file_{created,modified,deleted,renamed}` custom events into `DaemonMsg::{Touched, Deleted}` and filters non-markdown extensions defensively (the storage watcher already does this; double-check guards future relaxations). **Worker loop**: 200 ms tick that drains both bus events (via `EventFilter::CustomPrefix("com.nexus.storage.file_")`) and a direct `mpsc::UnboundedReceiver<DaemonMsg>` (used by tests / future `index_trigger` handler), updates `pending_files` under one brief write lock, then calls `Debouncer::maybe_flush(Instant::now())`. On flush: deletions route through `com.nexus.storage::vector_delete_by_file` (handler 19); touches fetch blocks via `com.nexus.storage::query_blocks` (handler 21), `decode_blocks` re-shapes the JSON return into the `(u64, String, String, Option<i32>)` `BlockTuple` shape `rag::index_file` consumes (accepts both the raw array and `{ blocks: [...] }` wrapper for forward-compat), then `rag::index_file(ctx, embedder.as_ref(), &path, &blocks)` runs. Per-IPC timeout `IPC_TIMEOUT = 30 s`. Errors are captured into `IndexStatus.last_error` but never abort the daemon — the next batch retries; `last_error` is cleared on the next successful flush. **Status state**: `IndexStatus { indexed_files: u64, pending_files: u64, total_seen: u64, last_error: Option<String>, running: bool }` lives behind `SharedStatus = Arc<RwLock<IndexStatus>>`; cheap to clone, briefly write-locked on each event arrival and the snapshot read. **IPC handler** ([`crates/nexus-ai/src/core_plugin.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/core_plugin.rs)): new `HANDLER_INDEX_STATUS: u32 = 14` on `com.nexus.ai`, args `{}`, returns `IndexStatus` verbatim. Dispatches in both sync and async paths so the shell's standard `kernel_invoke` async route works alongside CLI sync probes. **Plugin lifecycle**: `AiCorePlugin` gains `index_status: SharedStatus` (allocated unconditionally in `new()` so a fast `index_status` read returns a meaningful "never ran" view) and `indexing_daemon: Option<IndexingDaemon>` (spawned in `wire_context`, *not* `on_start`, because `on_start` runs before context wiring and the daemon needs `ctx.subscribe` + `ctx.ipc_call`). The embedder is supplied through an `EmbedderFactory = Arc<dyn Fn() -> Option<Box<dyn EmbeddingProvider>> + Send + Sync + 'static>` closure that captures the live `embed_config` handle so the daemon picks up `set_config` updates without a restart. `on_stop` signals shutdown via `Arc<AtomicBool>` and joins the worker. **Manifest** ([`crates/nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs`](../../crates/nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs)): `("index_status", HANDLER_INDEX_STATUS)` appended to the `com.nexus.ai` core manifest; `LifecycleFlags { on_init: true, on_stop: true, ..NONE }` so the kernel calls `on_stop` on graceful shutdown. **Shell badge** ([`shell/src/plugins/nexus/statusBar/IndexingStatus.tsx`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/statusBar/IndexingStatus.tsx)): polls `com.nexus.ai::index_status` every 2 s, renders a compact `dot + label` (green = idle, blue + glow = pending, red = error) with the indexed-files count or pending count or last-error message; latches the last-good snapshot so a transient kernel hiccup doesn't blank the badge; renders `null` when the daemon has never run (no AI / no embedder configured) so users don't see a permanently dead grey dot. The `statusBar/index.{ts → tsx}` rename is necessary to take JSX directly in the registration; registered with `priority: 20` so it slots after `FileStats`. **Coverage**: `cargo test -p nexus-ai` 118 passing (was 99 after BL-040; +19 net). New tests: 7 pure-logic `Debouncer` cases (`empty_queue_never_flushes`, `single_push_waits_for_debounce_window`, `batch_cap_forces_flush_before_debounce`, `duplicate_touches_dedupe`, `delete_supersedes_prior_touch`, `touch_after_delete_cancels_delete`, `pending_count_matches_drained_batch`); 4 `event_to_msg` translations (`storage_file_modified` → `Touched`, `storage_file_deleted` → `Deleted`, non-markdown skipped, unrelated events skipped); 3 `decode_blocks` shape tests (raw array / `{blocks}` wrapper / non-array rejection); 2 status-snapshot tests (default-when-unmodified, reflects-writes); 1 integration-style daemon test (`daemon_observes_storage_event_and_increments_total_seen`) that boots a real `KernelPluginContext`, spawns the daemon with a no-op embedder factory, publishes a `com.nexus.storage.file_modified` event onto the bus after asserting `bus.subscriber_count() >= 1`, and asserts `total_seen` advances + `running` flips on/off across `start` / `stop`; 2 dispatch-path tests on `HANDLER_INDEX_STATUS` (default snapshot returned when daemon unstarted; wire-id pin at 14). No live fastembed instantiation per the BL-040 / BL-019 test discipline. `cargo clippy -p nexus-ai --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean (required two type aliases — `EmbedderFactory` and `BlockTuple` — to satisfy `clippy::type_complexity`). `cargo test -p nexus-bootstrap` 11 passing; `cargo clippy -p nexus-bootstrap --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean. `pnpm --filter nexus-shell typecheck` clean; `pnpm --filter nexus-shell lint` no new warnings; `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 470 passing + 1 skipped (was 471 / 1; the badge is wired through `views.register` and exercised by the shell at runtime — no unit tests added since the polling loop is one `useEffect` and the rendering is mostly CSS). `bash scripts/check_ipc_drift.sh` not required — args/return stay inline `serde_json::Value` per the BL-041 task allowance. **Out of scope**: explicit `index_trigger` handler for "reindex now" (the design slot exists at handler id 15 but isn't wired today; the daemon already covers the watcher-driven path and the user can still call `com.nexus.ai::index_file` per-file as before — a forge-walking trigger is a small follow-up); rename-event splitting (today `file_renamed` is treated as touch-of-`to`, with a `TODO(BL-041 follow-up)` comment in `event_to_msg`; the next `file_modified` on the old path will pick up the tombstone via `vector_delete_by_file`); CLI badge surface (`nexus status` already prints AI status via `HANDLER_STATUS` — adding `index_status` to its block is a future line-item). Shipped commits `2146b60` (skeleton + IndexStatus + 9 debouncer tests), `579bf9e` (event-bus wiring + worker loop + 10 more tests), `a89f3a6` (bootstrap manifest + on_stop), `d0b4607` (shell status badge).

### BL-039: AI-DIR auto-link suggestions ✅ (2026-04-29)

**Delivered:** AI-INTEGRATION-DIRECTIONS direction 2 lands as a default-off shell-side plugin pair: a CodeMirror extension at [`shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/cm/linkSuggest.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/cm/linkSuggest.ts) that surfaces a `[[wiki-link]]` ghost suggestion at the caret when the typed phrase semantically matches an existing forge note, plus a thin activation plugin at [`shell/src/plugins/nexus/linkSuggest/index.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/linkSuggest/index.ts) that owns the configuration schema. **Loop**: `ViewPlugin` debounces 600 ms on each user keystroke (cancel-on-edit semantics mirror BL-034 — the `inFlightRequestId` counter is bumped on every doc change so any late resolution falls stale and is discarded). On flush, `extractPhrase(doc, caret, minChars=4, maxChars=80)` walks back from the caret to the nearest hard boundary (`\n` always wins; `. ` / `? ` / `! ` count when followed by a space; otherwise the `caret − maxChars` window edge). Leading bullet/blockquote/heading markers (`- `, `> `, `* `, `+ `, `# `) are trimmed so a phrase like `"- project atlas"` extracts as `"project atlas"`. The phrase is rejected when shorter than `minChars`, when it contains no letters, or when the caret sits mid-word (the static `\w` lookahead at `text[caret]`). `isInSkipZone(doc, caret)` then suppresses three contexts: an open `[[…]]` (most recent `[[` before the caret with no intervening `]]`); YAML frontmatter (file starts with `---\n` and the caret is before the closing `---` fence — handles unclosed frontmatter as "everything is fm"); and fenced code blocks (odd count of `^```$` lines before the caret). **Retrieval**: surviving phrases call `getGhostApi().kernel.invoke('com.nexus.ai', 'semantic_search', { query, limit: 3 })` — same handle BL-034 uses, populated by the AI plugin's `setGhostApi(api)`. The top match is gated on `score >= 0.55` (constant `ai.linkSuggest.scoreGate`, tunable). **Two-ghost coexistence**: before the round trip, the fetcher reads `view.state.field(ghostInternals.suggestionField, false)` and DEFERs entirely when BL-034's inline AI ghost is currently visible — two ghosts with conflicting Tab semantics would confuse the user, so the cheaper rule is "AI ghost wins, link-suggest waits for the next keystroke after dismissal." `linkSuggest` exposes its own `suggestionField` / decoration / `Prec.high` Tab+Esc keymap, fully isolated from `ghostCompletion`. **Replacement build**: `basenameNoExt(file_path)` strips the dir + `.md`; `buildReplacement(file_path, phrase)` returns `[[basename]]` when `basename.toLowerCase() === phrase.toLowerCase()` (the alias would be noise) and `[[basename|phrase]]` otherwise. **Render**: a single `Decoration.widget` after the caret renders ` → [[…]]` in a slightly-bluer muted tone (`var(--accent-muted, #6b8aff)`) so users can distinguish it visually from BL-034's grey AI ghost. Tab accepts and dispatches `{ from: sug.from, to: sug.to, insert: replacement }` with the caret moved to `from + replacement.length`, then clears the field; Esc clears the field. Both bindings are `Prec.high` so they beat the editor's normal Tab/Esc when a suggestion is live and `false`-fall-through when it is not. **Configuration** ([`linkSuggest/index.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/linkSuggest/index.ts)) registers five keys under `nexus.linkSuggest` (order 51): `ai.linkSuggest.{enabled,debounceMs,minChars,maxChars,scoreGate}`, all read lazily on each tick via `configStore.get` so live edits in Settings take effect without remounting the editor. **Catalog wiring** ([`shell/src/plugins/catalog.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/catalog.ts)): registered in `DEFAULT_OFF_PLUGINS` immediately after `semanticSearchPlugin`, with the same comment rationale (depends on the AI plugin's embedding provider being configured — pairing the enabled-states keeps users from seeing dead suggestions). **Editor wiring** ([`shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/EditorView.tsx`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/EditorView.tsx)): `linkSuggestExt()` is composed alongside `ghostCompletionExt()` in the source-mode extension list (live-mode inherits via the `[...base, livePreviewExt()]` spread). **Coverage**: 23 new tests in [`linkSuggest.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/cm/linkSuggest.test.ts) re-exported through [`shell/tests/link-suggest.test.ts`](../../shell/tests/link-suggest.test.ts) so the workspace test runner picks them up: `basenameNoExt` (4 cases incl. no-extension), `buildReplacement` (case-insensitive bare form + alias form), `extractPhrase` (start-of-line boundary, sentence boundary, minChars rejection, mid-word rejection, maxChars cap, trailing-space trim, leading bullet trim, no-letters rejection), `isInSkipZone` (open wiki-link, closed wiki-link, frontmatter open, frontmatter closed, code fence open, code fence closed), and the `suggestionField` state machine (default empty, set populates, doc change invalidates, selection move invalidates, explicit null clears, accept-splice math produces the expected `'see [[Foo Bar|foo bar]]'` doc + caret). View-driven Tab/Esc handlers are exercised at the reducer level — a real DOM `EditorView` is out of scope for `node:test`, mirroring the BL-034 ghost-completion test discipline. `pnpm --filter nexus-shell typecheck` clean; `pnpm --filter nexus-shell lint` clean (no new warnings); `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 494 passing + 1 skipped (was 470 / 1; +23 net plus the existing skipped slot). No Rust changes → no IPC drift check needed. **Out of scope**: dedicated suggestion sidebar / multi-candidate picker (today the top match wins; cycling through the second/third match via Alt+] is a follow-up); rename-on-accept of the link target (the user-typed phrase becomes the alias verbatim — re-titling the matched note is a separate workflow); per-language tuning of the sentence-boundary regex (Latin terminators only — CJK needs its own pass when BL-019 multilingual lands); inline replacement preview that strikes through the typed phrase (rejected because it fights with selection rendering during live typing — the `→` ghost reads cleanly without that). Shipped commit `c76fafd`.

### BL-038: AMB citations ✅ (2026-04-29)

**Delivered:** AI-AMBIENT-COPILOT-PLAN pattern 8 lands as a numbered, line-aware citation contract that flows from `rag::query` all the way through the streaming `stream_ask` IPC handler into the chat view, where `[N]` markers in the model's answer become clickable superscript chips that open the source file at the cited line. **Backend** ([`crates/nexus-ai/src/rag.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/rag.rs)): new `Citation { index: u32, file_path: String, block_id: u64, start_line: Option<u32>, end_line: Option<u32>, excerpt: String, score: f32 }` derives `Serialize` / `Deserialize` / `TS` / `JsonSchema` (the latter two gated on the existing `ts-export` feature). `RagResponse` gains a `citations: Vec<Citation>` field parallel to the legacy `sources: Vec<ChunkMatch>` — `sources` stays in place for backwards compat per the BL-038 task allowance ("ship side-by-side this round"). The pure helper `build_citations(ctx, sources, answer)` does three things in order: (1) groups source chunks by `file_path` and fans out one `com.nexus.storage::query_blocks` (handler 21) IPC call per unique path, indexes the returned `BlockRecord`s by `id`, and joins `start_line` / `end_line` onto each citation; (2) numbers citations 1-based in source order (which is descending by score, since that's what `vectorstore::search` returns); (3) when the model emitted parseable `[N]` markers in the answer, renumbers citations by first-occurrence so the chip ordering matches reading order — a tiny inline byte-walker covers `\[(\d+)\]` without pulling a regex dep, skips out-of-range markers, and preserves trailing source-order slots for citations the model didn't reference. Enrichment failures (storage offline, file moved, index lag) degrade to `start_line: None` rather than failing the whole query, satisfying the file-as-truth invariant: the answer + chunk text remain valid even if the index drifts. Excerpts are clipped to `CITATION_EXCERPT_MAX_CHARS = 200` via a char-boundary-safe `truncate_excerpt` (won't split a UTF-8 codepoint). **Prompt teach-cite** ([`build_rag_prompt`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/rag.rs)): `RAG_PROMPT_HEADER` now instructs the model to "Cite sources as [N] where N is the 1-based position in the SOURCES list below (for example, [1] or [2])" alongside the legacy `[[file_path]]` form so models that prefer one or the other both produce parseable output. The numbered `Source N:` body lines are unchanged so the same prompt still works for older callers. **Streaming integration** ([`crates/nexus-ai/src/core_plugin.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/core_plugin.rs)): `handle_stream_ask` (HANDLER_STREAM_ASK = 7) now calls `rag::build_citations(&ctx, &sources, &text)` after the chat stream completes, then surfaces `citations` on both the `com.nexus.ai.stream_done` event payload and the IPC return value so the shell receives them through whichever path resolves first (the event handler typically wins; the invoke-result fallback covers dropped events). `handle_ask` (HANDLER_ASK = 1) inherits citations transparently because it returns the full `RagResponse`. **ChunkMatch ts-export gate** ([`crates/nexus-ai/src/vectorstore.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/vectorstore.rs)): `ChunkMatch` now derives `TS` / `JsonSchema` under `ts-export` so `RagResponse.sources: Vec<ChunkMatch>` compiles when the drift-check feature flag is on. **TS bindings** ([`packages/nexus-extension-api/src/generated/ipc/`](../../packages/nexus-extension-api/src/generated/ipc/)): three new generated files committed by the drift script — `Citation.ts`, `RagResponse.ts`, `ChunkMatch.ts`. `bash scripts/check_ipc_drift.sh` is clean. **Shell types** ([`shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/aiStore.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/aiStore.ts)): new `AiCitation { index, path, blockId, startLine: number|null, endLine: number|null, excerpt, score }` mirrors the kernel struct (snake_case to camelCase). The assistant turn variant gains `citations: AiCitation[]` (initialized to `[]` in `startAsk`); `finishStream` accepts an optional `citations` argument paralleling `sources`; `decodeTurn` rehydrates citations from persisted sessions, defensively dropping malformed entries. **Runtime coercion** ([`aiRuntime.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/aiRuntime.ts)): new `coerceCitations(raw)` mirrors the existing `coerceSources` shape, sorts by `index` for stable rendering even if the kernel order shifts, and is wired into both the `TOPIC_DONE` event handler and the `stream_ask` invoke-result fallback. **Citation transform** ([`shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/citationTransform.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/citationTransform.ts)): pure helper module split out of `ChatView.tsx` so `node:test` can exercise it without pulling React + `chat.css`. `splitTextOnCitations(text, valid)` walks `\[(\d+)\]` and emits alternating `string | { cite: number }` segments, dropping out-of-range markers as plain text so the user still sees what the model wrote. The DOM-walking wrapper `renderMarkdownWithCitations(source, validIndices)` runs `renderMarkdown` first (so code blocks / tables stay intact), then walks the resulting HTML via `DOMParser`, splitting text nodes around valid markers and substituting `<sup class="nexus-citation" data-cite="N" role="button" tabindex="0">[N]</sup>`. Marker substitution is skipped inside `<code>` and `<pre>` so code samples that contain `[1]` literals are left verbatim. The wrapper guards on `typeof DOMParser` and falls back to the unmodified rendered markdown in headless test environments. **ChatView wiring** ([`shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/ChatView.tsx`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/ChatView.tsx)): `AssistantBubble` swaps `MarkdownBody` for the new `CitedMarkdownBody` when `turn.citations.length > 0`; the body uses one delegated `click` listener on the container div that resolves `[data-cite]` chips back to `AiCitation` and dispatches `onCitationClick`. The chip strip below the answer prefers `turn.citations` (rendering `[N] path:start-end` with the index in the accent colour) over the legacy `turn.sources`, falling back gracefully when the kernel didn't ship citations (older backend / RAG returned nothing). `handleCitationClick` emits `files:open` with `{ relpath, name, line: citation.startLine ?? undefined }` so listeners that support a `line` option scroll straight to the cited block; older listeners ignore the extra key gracefully. **Coverage**: `cargo test -p nexus-ai` 130 passing (was 118 after BL-041; +12 net): 1 prompt teach-cite test (`build_rag_prompt_teaches_bracket_citation` — asserts the new `[N]` instruction landed without breaking the legacy `[[file_path]]` substring); 4 end-to-end `query` tests with a stub `AiProvider` + an extended `StubDispatcher` that intercepts both `vector_query` and `query_blocks` (`query_attaches_line_ranges_via_query_blocks` — 2 sources × 2 paths fan out one `query_blocks` per unique path and the resulting `Citation` carries the expected `start_line` / `end_line`; `query_renumbers_citations_by_answer_order_when_markers_present` — model emits `[2]` before `[1]` and the chips renumber so index 1 is the source the model cited first; `query_falls_back_to_source_order_when_no_markers` — empty answer keeps the original order; `citations_degrade_gracefully_when_storage_lacks_block` — a chunk whose `block_id` isn't in the returned `BlockRecord`s still surfaces with `start_line: None`); 2 `truncate_excerpt` cases (clip + ellipsis on overflow, passthrough under the limit). The existing 6 `build_rag_prompt` / budgeted-prompt tests still pass — the header text change preserved every substring asserted on. `cargo clippy -p nexus-ai --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean. `cargo test -p nexus-bootstrap` 11 passing; `cargo clippy -p nexus-bootstrap --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean. `pnpm --filter nexus-shell typecheck` clean; `pnpm --filter nexus-shell lint` clean (no new warnings); `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 499 passing + 1 skipped (was 494 / 1; +6 new tests in [`citationTransform.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/citationTransform.test.ts) re-exported through [`shell/tests/citation-transform.test.ts`](../../shell/tests/citation-transform.test.ts) covering the splitter's passthrough, valid-marker substitution, out-of-range markers, leading/trailing markers, back-to-back markers, and empty-valid-set short-circuit; minus 1 net because the existing `aiStore.test.ts` `decodeTurn` round-trip case was extended in-place to include the new `citations: []` field on the persisted assistant turn). `bash scripts/check_ipc_drift.sh` clean; the regenerated `Citation.ts` / `RagResponse.ts` / `ChunkMatch.ts` are committed. **Out of scope** per the task allowance: deprecating `RagResponse.sources` (kept side-by-side this round; a future BL can drop it once consumers migrate); JSON Schema emission for the new types (today the JSON Schema test only emits the WI-36 pilot list — adding `Citation` / `RagResponse` is a one-liner if a future MCP client needs them); cycling through alt-citations when multiple chunks share a `file_path` (today the chip row deduplicates per `path-blockId-index` key but doesn't expose a "next match" affordance); per-citation hover-cards with the full chunk text (today the chip's `title` attribute carries the truncated excerpt + score — a richer popover is a follow-up); the renumber pass when the model cites an index outside `1..=citations.len()` (today the marker is left as plain text rather than synthesizing an extra citation chip — keeping the chip list bounded to what was actually retrieved is the safer default). Shipped commits `b6cdff1` (Rust: Citation struct + RagResponse.citations + line-range enrichment + teach-cite + 7 new rag-module tests + stream_ask wire-up), `283ebf2` (chore(ipc): regen TS bindings + ChunkMatch ts-export gate), `8685afd` (shell: AiCitation + citationTransform + CitedMarkdownBody + CitationChipRow + 6 splitter tests).

### BL-047: MEM scheduled digests ✅ (2026-04-29)

**Delivered:** AI-MEMORY-LAYER-PLAN piece 6 lands as the **one-off cron path** described in the BL-047 PRD — a workflow-driven cron job that walks recent capture-note markdown files, asks the AI provider to summarise them, and writes the result to a `Digests/` file. BL-028 (template engine) is the follow-up upgrade. **Library** ([`crates/nexus-workflow/src/digests.rs`](../../crates/nexus-workflow/src/digests.rs), 530 lines): new `DigestConfig { enabled, daily_cron, weekly_cron, scope_path, digests_dir }` with serde-derived defaults (`enabled = false` so users opt in; `daily_cron = "0 9 * * *"`; `weekly_cron = "0 9 * * 1"`; `digests_dir = "Digests"`). `DigestKind { Daily, Weekly }` is the IPC-arg enum. `digest_window(kind, now_utc)` is the pure window helper — daily = `[now-24h, now)`, weekly = `[now-7d, now)`. `output_path(kind, now_utc, dir)` returns `<dir>/Daily-YYYY-MM-DD.md` (chrono `%Y-%m-%d`) or `<dir>/Weekly-YYYY-Www.md` using ISO-week numbering via `now_utc.iso_week()` so the 2027-01-01 boundary correctly emits `Weekly-2026-W53.md`. `build_digest_prompt(kind, sources)` is the pure prompt builder — emits a tight instruction ("produce a concise markdown digest with overview / themes / actions"), a `# Sources (N file(s))` header, and one fenced markdown block per source with the path as the section heading. **Orchestrator** (`pub async fn run_digest(ctx, cfg, kind, now_utc) -> Result<DigestRunReport, PluginError>`): walks the configured scope (forge root when `scope_path` is `None`) recursively via `com.nexus.storage::list_dir` (HANDLER_LIST_DIR = 27), filters markdown files whose `modifiedMs` falls inside the digest window, reads bodies via `com.nexus.storage::read_file` (HANDLER_READ_FILE = 2), skips anything under `digests_dir/` to avoid feedback loops, builds the prompt, calls `com.nexus.ai::ask` (HANDLER_ASK = 1), ensures the digest directory exists via `com.nexus.storage::create_dir` (HANDLER_CREATE_DIR = 29; pre-existing-dir errors are swallowed), then writes the digest body via `com.nexus.storage::write_file` (HANDLER_WRITE_FILE = 8). The output file gets YAML frontmatter (`digest_kind`, `generated_at`, `source_count`, `sources` list) so downstream indexing sees it as a normal markdown note. Empty-window short-circuits return `DigestRunReport { written: false, source_count: 0, model: None, … }` without calling the AI provider — saves a round trip and avoids asking the model to summarise nothing. The recursive walker uses `Box::pin` to bound the async future size. All filesystem and AI access flows through kernel IPC; the workflow crate never touches the filesystem or AI provider directly. **IPC handler** ([`crates/nexus-workflow/src/core_plugin.rs`](../../crates/nexus-workflow/src/core_plugin.rs)): new `HANDLER_RUN_DIGEST: u32 = 6` on `com.nexus.workflow`, args `{ kind: "daily"|"weekly" }`, returns `DigestRunReport`. Wired through `dispatch_async` (the sync `dispatch` arm returns the same "use dispatch_async" error pattern the existing HANDLER_RUN uses). The plugin gains a `digest_config: DigestConfig` field and a new `WorkflowCorePlugin::open_with_digest_config(workflows_dir, cfg)` constructor; the legacy `open(workflows_dir)` delegates with `DigestConfig::default()` for backwards compat. **Cron loop** (`spawn_digest_scheduler` + `digest_scheduler_loop`): spawned from `wire_context` (mirrors the existing `spawn_cron_schedulers` and `spawn_file_event_triggers` patterns; on_start runs before context wiring, so the digest loop cannot use it). Disabled when `DigestConfig.enabled == false` — the loop never spawns and `tracing::debug!`s the reason. When enabled, the loop wakes every 60s (capped sleep), computes the next fire across both schedules via `digests::next_fire`, and dispatches `com.nexus.workflow::run_digest` via `ctx.ipc_call` so semantics match the manual-trigger path. Sleeps 61s past each fire so a one-minute boundary doesn't fire twice. The loop's `JoinHandle` is parked in the existing `scheduler_handles` Vec and aborted on plugin Drop alongside the cron and file-event handles. **Bootstrap manifest** ([`crates/nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs`](../../crates/nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs) `com.nexus.workflow` block): `("run_digest", HANDLER_RUN_DIGEST)` registered alongside the existing `list` / `get` / `reload` / `validate` / `run` entries; CLI / TUI / MCP / shell all reach it through `context.ipc_call(...)` with no per-frontend opt-in. New `load_digest_config(forge_root)` helper reads `<forge>/.forge/config.toml` and deserialises the `[digests]` block via `toml::from_str` (toml moved from dev-dep to runtime dep on `nexus-bootstrap`); missing file / missing block / parse failure all fall back to `DigestConfig::default()` so existing forges work with no config changes — a parse failure logs at warn but never blocks boot. **Coverage**: `cargo test -p nexus-workflow` 78 passing (was 65 pre-BL-047; +13 net): 11 pure-logic tests in `digests::tests` covering defaults (off + known crons), daily window = last 24h, weekly window = last 7d, daily output path with ISO date, weekly output path with ISO week, weekly output path at the year-53 boundary (2027-01-01 → `Weekly-2026-W53.md`), trailing-slash strip on `digests_dir`, prompt includes sources + paths + count, weekly prompt label, `next_fire` picks the earliest schedule (Sunday morning daily wins over Monday morning weekly), and `DigestKind::from_str` round-trip + reject. 2 stub-IPC integration tests (`run_digest_walks_files_calls_ai_and_writes` — three fixtures with mixed mtimes + extensions; only the in-window `.md` makes it through; AI is called once; `write_file` fires; report carries the model + path; `run_digest_short_circuits_when_no_files_in_window` — stale-only fixture; AI is NOT called; report shows `written: false`). The stub `IpcDispatcher` mirrors the BL-041 `indexing_daemon::tests` pattern — records every call and returns canned responses for the storage / AI commands the pipeline issues. `cargo clippy -p nexus-workflow --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean (required four module-scoped allow lints in `digests.rs`: `unnecessary_wraps` for the `Option<String>` config defaults that are part of the wire shape, `should_implement_trait` for `DigestKind::from_str` which mirrors the JSON arg name not `std::str::FromStr`, `format_push_string` for hot-path string building dwarfed by the IPC round-trips, and `cast_possible_truncation` for the `u64`-to-`u8` byte coercion in `read_file` where JSON numbers are constructively `0..=255`). `cargo test -p nexus-bootstrap` 11 passing; `cargo clippy -p nexus-bootstrap --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean. No IPC drift required — args/return stay inline `serde_json::Value`. **Scheduling-thread design choice**: spawned from `wire_context` rather than `on_start` because `on_start` runs before the kernel context is attached, and the loop needs `ctx.ipc_call` to dispatch through `com.nexus.workflow::run_digest` (matches the existing `spawn_cron_schedulers` rationale documented in `core_plugin.rs`'s module docstring). The 60s wake interval is intentionally simple — a precise sleep-until-next-fire would shave milliseconds at the cost of clock-skew brittleness; the current design re-evaluates every minute so a config change or system suspend resync naturally. **Known limitations**: (1) `DigestConfig` is loaded once at bootstrap and never re-read — toggling `enabled` or changing crons requires restarting Nexus; a follow-up could subscribe the loop to a config-change event (the workflow plugin already has a `reload` handler the digest path could mirror). (2) The walker scans the whole forge subtree on every fire — a large forge with thousands of markdown files pays the IPC cost even when only a handful are in-window; a future optimisation could push the mtime filter into a single storage IPC like `list_recent` or use the existing search index. (3) Capture-notes scope is implicit (any `.md` in `scope_path`) rather than tag-based or BL-043 `memory.inboxPath`-aware — the BACKLOG description called this out as the pragmatic v1 choice; BL-028 templates will let users author per-digest source filters declaratively. (4) The output file format is hard-coded — frontmatter shape, prompt wording, and section structure are all baked into the Rust code; BL-028 will move these into user-editable templates. (5) The AI call uses `ask` (RAG) which adds embedding cost to the digest pipeline even though the prompt already carries the source bodies — `stream_chat` would be cheaper but pulling in the chat-message shape from the workflow crate is out of scope for v1; the AI provider is free to ignore the empty RAG side and just summarise the prompt. (6) The cron loop has no per-fire de-duplication beyond the 61s post-fire sleep — if the system clock jumps backwards (NTP correction) the same minute boundary could re-fire; a fired-at watermark in KV would close that gap if it ever bites. Shipped commits `59790ea` (skeleton + DigestConfig + pure-logic helpers + run_digest orchestrator + scheduler thread + 11 unit tests), `241f281` (bootstrap manifest + load_digest_config), `36ff86c` (stub-IPC integration tests for run_digest), `d962d76` (clippy pedantic allows).

### BL-045: MEM auto-enrichment on save ✅ (2026-04-29)

**Delivered:** AI-MEMORY-LAYER-PLAN piece 2 lands as a two-phase pipeline split across the AI core plugin (Rust) and a default-off shell plugin (TypeScript). Phase 1 (`enrich_file`) reads the markdown file via storage IPC, asks the chat provider for tags + summary in two sequential `chat()` calls with tight system prompts, runs `rag::semantic_search` against the body to surface `[[basename]]`-style related notes (with the input file itself filtered out and results deduped), and returns an `EnrichmentProposal` WITHOUT touching the file. Phase 2 (`enrich_apply`) re-reads the file, verifies a body-hash drift guard, merges the proposal into the YAML frontmatter, and writes back via storage IPC. The shell plugin sits between them: it subscribes to a new `files:saved` event, throttles per-file with a 5-second debounce so rapid consecutive saves coalesce, dispatches `enrich_file`, surfaces the proposal in an inline accept-gate panel, and routes the user's Accept click through `enrich_apply`. **Backend** ([`crates/nexus-ai/src/enrichment.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/enrichment.rs), 470 lines): `EnrichmentProposal { path, body_hash, tags: Vec<String>, summary: String, related: Vec<String> }` is the cross-IPC payload (serde-derived; not ts-rs-exported in v1 — the shell side mirrors the shape with a hand-written interface). `body_hash(content)` strips leading frontmatter then SHA-256s the body, so re-applying a proposal whose frontmatter we just updated does NOT invalidate later proposals on the same body — the idempotency invariant the PRD called out. `strip_frontmatter` is intentionally minimal (recognises a `---\n…\n---\n` block on the very first line; treats unterminated blocks as body so we never accidentally swallow real content). `merge_frontmatter(original, proposal)` parses the existing `tags:` field (inline list `[a, b]` OR block list `\n  - a\n  - b`), unions with the proposal's tags case-insensitively (existing first, then new), drops the existing `tags` / `summary` / `related` lines from the frontmatter, then re-emits them as inline lists; every other key the user authored is preserved verbatim, and a `summary` containing `:` / `#` / `"` is YAML-quoted. `propose(ctx, ai, embedder, path)` runs the pipeline; tags are filtered to single-word lowercase entries (no whitespace, only alphanumerics + `-` / `_`), capped at 5; summaries are stripped of surrounding quotes/whitespace then char-truncated to 200; the related list is deduped, capped at 5, and asks for `MAX_RELATED + 5` chunks from `semantic_search` so the self-filter has headroom. `apply(ctx, proposal)` returns `(applied: bool, reason: Option<String>)` — a hash mismatch is a soft `applied = false` ("body changed since proposal") rather than an error, so the shell can re-propose without surfacing a stack trace. **Handlers** ([`crates/nexus-ai/src/core_plugin.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/core_plugin.rs)): `HANDLER_ENRICH_FILE = 15` (args `{ path: String }` → JSON-serialised `EnrichmentProposal`) and `HANDLER_ENRICH_APPLY = 16` (args `{ proposal: EnrichmentProposal }` → `{ applied: bool, reason: ?String }`) wired into the `dispatch_async` match between the existing `HANDLER_SEMANTIC_SEARCH = 13` and `HANDLER_INDEX_STATUS = 14` arms; both require the AI plugin context (built in `wire_context`) and `enrich_file` additionally requires both an AI chat provider AND an embedding provider (matches the dual-prereq the BACKLOG entry called out). **Manifest** ([`crates/nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs`](../../crates/nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs) `com.nexus.ai` block): `enrich_file` and `enrich_apply` registered alongside the existing 13 handlers; CLI / TUI / MCP / shell all reach them through the canonical `context.ipc_call(...)` path with no per-frontend opt-in. **Shell plugin** ([`shell/src/plugins/nexus/enrich/`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/enrich/), 5 files): `enrichStore.ts` (zustand store with `pending: EnrichmentProposal | null`, `applying: boolean`, `error: string | null` + setters; v1 shows one proposal at a time per-file — the runtime overwrites the slot whenever a fresher proposal arrives so the user always sees the latest suggestion for the most recently saved file). `enrichRuntime.ts` is the core: `attachRuntime(api)` subscribes to `files:saved` (a new event), filters to markdown extensions (`.md` / `.mdx` / `.markdown`), and uses a module-scope `Map<filePath, timeoutHandle>` to enforce the 5-second per-file debounce — repeated saves of the same file within the window collapse into one `enrich_file` request, while saves of *other* files still fire on their own clocks. `applyPending(api)` issues `enrich_apply`, dismisses the panel + shows an info toast on success, and surfaces `result.reason` inline on a soft refusal. Failures from `enrich_file` are stashed as a dismissable error rather than thrown — enrichment is opt-in background luxury and must never interfere with the save itself. `EnrichAcceptGate.tsx` is a fixed bottom-right toast-style panel (centred 360px wide, z-index 9999) that renders the file basename, the suggested summary, the tags as `#tag` chips, and the related-notes line; two buttons (`Accept` / `Dismiss`) with the `Accept` button greyed out while `applying` is in flight. `enrichApi.ts` is the module-scope handle pattern (mirrors `recallApi.ts`) so the slot-rendered component can reach the API from a click handler. `index.ts` declares the plugin manifest (`activationEvents: ['onStartup']`, default-off via `DEFAULT_OFF_PLUGINS`), wires everything together in `activate()`, and registers the gate component in the chrome `overlay` slot at priority 27 (one above BL-044's recall overlay so a stacked open keeps the accept-gate visible). **Editor save event** ([`shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/index.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/index.ts)): the COMMAND_SAVE handler now `api.events.emit('files:saved', { relpath })` after each `markSaved` call — three sites (kernel-session save, untitled-markdown write+acquire, non-markdown plain write) so opt-in features can react without coupling to the editor internals. **Catalog**: registered in `DEFAULT_OFF_PLUGINS` next to `recallPlugin` with comment rationale (default-off because it issues an AI chat call + an embedding+vector lookup per saved markdown file; requires both a chat provider AND an embedding provider configured); default-off count comment bumped from 15 → 16. **Inbox-scope decision** (the task's open question): v1 does NOT scope by inbox tag. The BACKLOG entry called out "On save of an inbox-tagged file, run an enrichment pass" but the existing `AiConfig` has no `memory.inboxPath` analogue on the Rust side and the BL-044 inbox-scope filter lives entirely on the shell side; rather than re-discover that wire, v1 enriches every saved markdown file and lets the user dismiss anything that looks irrelevant. The 5-second debounce keeps the cost manageable; a follow-up can subscribe to BL-043's `memory.inboxPath` config in the runtime and skip `enrich_file` for non-inbox files. **Coverage**: `cargo test -p nexus-ai` 142 passing (was 129 before BL-045; +13): 9 unit tests in `enrichment::tests` covering body-hash idempotency under frontmatter mutations, body-hash sensitivity to body changes, `strip_frontmatter` on no-fm / unterminated / well-formed inputs, `merge_frontmatter` creating fresh frontmatter on a file with none, preserving unrelated keys + dedupe-merging tags, replacing block-list tags with an inline list, and quoting summaries containing `:`; 4 helper tests covering `parse_tag_response` (clean tags + 5-tag cap with multi-word filter), `clean_summary` (quote strip + char truncation), and `related_from_matches` (self-drop + dedupe across multiple chunks of the same file). 4 new dispatch-level tests in `core_plugin::semantic_search_dispatch_tests` covering handler-id pinning (`HANDLER_ENRICH_FILE = 15`, `HANDLER_ENRICH_APPLY = 16` — bumping these is a wire break), `enrich_file` arg validation (missing `path`), missing AI provider, and `enrich_apply` arg validation (missing `proposal`). `cargo clippy -p nexus-ai --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean. `cargo test -p nexus-bootstrap` clean (handlers correctly resolve through the manifest). `pnpm --filter nexus-shell typecheck` + `lint` clean (no new warnings beyond the pre-existing pile); `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 521 passing + 1 skipped (no shell-side tests added in v1 — the runtime's debounce + IPC dispatch are easier to validate end-to-end than to mock Map-backed timers + zustand at the unit level; a follow-up can add `enrichRuntime.test.ts` mirroring `recallRuntime.test.ts`'s mocked-PluginAPI shape). No `EnrichmentProposal` ts-rs derive in v1 (the shell hand-mirrors the shape) → `scripts/check_ipc_drift.sh` not required. **Known limitations**: (1) inbox-scope is unwired (see "Inbox-scope decision" above); (2) no shell-side unit tests for the runtime debounce / IPC fan-out — the parity tests with BL-044's recall runtime are deferred to a follow-up; (3) the accept-gate UI is a single-pending slot — if the user saves three files in rapid succession, only the most-recent proposal is visible (older ones are silently overwritten); a queue or per-file panel stack would be a polish pass; (4) `enrich_file` issues two sequential `chat()` calls (tags then summary); a single combined prompt with structured-output parsing would halve provider latency but couples the two prompts and complicates retry logic — v1 prefers reliability over latency; (5) the runtime fires on every saved markdown file regardless of size — a 100KB note still costs one chat round-trip + one embedding + one vector lookup, throttled to once per 5s but not skipped; a body-length floor is a trivial follow-up. Shipped commits `579a9ae` (skeleton + EnrichmentProposal + body_hash + merge_frontmatter + 9 unit tests), `1553cc3` (milestone marker for the test-gate green), `ad86ff2` (`propose` + `apply` async functions + 4 helper tests), `4132c1b` (`HANDLER_ENRICH_FILE` / `HANDLER_ENRICH_APPLY` dispatch wiring + 4 dispatch tests), `be3b222` (bootstrap manifest registration), `287c753` (shell plugin scaffold + `files:saved` editor event emit + accept-gate UI + catalog wiring).

### BL-044: MEM recall hotkey ✅ (2026-04-29)

**Delivered:** AI-MEMORY-LAYER-PLAN piece 3 lands as a default-off shell-side plugin at [`shell/src/plugins/nexus/recall/`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/recall/) that opens a Cmd+Shift+R (Ctrl+Shift+R on Linux/Windows) overlay, debounces 200ms-on-input, fans the trimmed query into `com.nexus.ai::semantic_search` (BL-040 handler 13) with `limit: 10`, scopes results to the BL-043 inbox path, and lets the user insert a quote-formatted snippet at the active editor caret (Enter) or copy it to the clipboard (Cmd/Ctrl+Enter). Reuses BL-032's overlay visual scaffold via duplication rather than a shared component — the overlays diverge enough (results list vs. streaming response panel; Up/Down navigation vs. context chips) that a content-adapter abstraction would have been more code than two ~210-line components. **Plugin** ([`recall/index.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/recall/index.ts)): registers `nexus.recall.open` (keybinding `cmd+shift+r` / `ctrl+shift+r`) + `nexus.recall.close` (Esc, gated on the `nexus.recall.visible` context-key); contributes one `recall.hotkey` config key (default `Mod-Shift-r`, in CodeMirror parlance) for future user-customization; mounts `RecallOverlay` in the chrome `overlay` slot at priority 26 (one above the BL-043 capture overlay). Catalog-registered in `DEFAULT_OFF_PLUGINS` next to `linkSuggestPlugin` with the same comment rationale (depends on the AI plugin's embedding provider being configured; pairs naturally with `nexus.memory` so the inbox-scope filter has something to bind to). **Store** ([`recallStore.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/recall/recallStore.ts)): zustand store mirroring the cmd-i shape — `{ visible, query, results, selectedIndex, status, error, currentRequestId }` with `open / close / setQuery / beginSearch / setResults / setError / moveSelection / setSelectedIndex` actions. `setResults(reqId, matches)` drops stale callbacks via the request-id guard so a slow `semantic_search` round-trip can't repopulate a closed overlay or overwrite a fresher search;
