`moveSelection(±1)` clamps to `[0, results.length-1]` so arrow-key navigation can't fall off either end; `setResults` also reclamps `selectedIndex` when the new list is shorter than the previous selection. `close()` retains query/results so reopening with the hotkey doesn't flicker between empty and prior state — the next `open()` wipes them anyway. **Runtime** ([`recallRuntime.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/recall/recallRuntime.ts)): `searchDebounced(api, query)` collapses keystroke bursts into a single `runSearch` call after `RECALL_DEBOUNCE_MS = 200` of quiet (the trailing edge wins; same value the BL-039 link-suggest poll settled on); empty/whitespace queries short-circuit to a clean state without firing a kernel call (no spinner-then-empty flicker). `runSearch` mints a `recall-<uuid>` request id, calls `semantic_search` with `{ query, limit: 10 }`, decodes the `{ matches: ChunkMatch[] }` response defensively (drops malformed entries lacking `file_path`, same shape as the BL-040 palette plugin's decoder), and applies `filterToInboxScope`. `insertSelectedSnippet()` reaches the active CodeMirror view via `editor/runtime.getActiveCmView()` (a sibling-plugin import — same pattern `editor/cm/linkSuggest.ts` already uses for BL-039) and dispatches a `{ from: head, to: head, insert: snippet }` change with the post-splice caret placed AFTER the inserted snippet so the user can keep typing without manually escaping the quote block; pulls focus back to the editor on success. `copySelectedSnippet()` writes through `navigator.clipboard.writeText` and degrades silently when the platform clipboard is unavailable. **Inbox-scope filter** ([`filterToInboxScope`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/recall/recallRuntime.ts)): v1 reads `memory.inboxPath` via `api.configuration.getValue` (default `Inbox.md` matching BL-043) and keeps only matches whose `file_path === inboxPath`. **Known v1 limitation**: when the filter would zero out a non-empty result list, the runtime degrades to surfacing the unfiltered set — recall with no results is worse UX than recall with out-of-scope results when the user explicitly typed a query that hit the index. The richer "from project" / multi-path / tag-based filter is BL-046 (code-aware capture) territory; the BACKLOG entry for BL-046 already calls this out. **Insert formatter** ([`insertFormat.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/recall/insertFormat.ts)): pure function `formatRecallSnippet(match)` returns ``> {chunk_text trimmed, line-prefixed}\n>\n> — [[basename]]\n``. Strips a single trailing `.md` (case-insensitive) so the produced wiki-link resolves through Nexus's existing link resolver; preserves internal newlines by prefixing every line with `> ` so the snippet stays inside one quote block; trims surrounding whitespace; handles empty `chunk_text` without producing a malformed block (single `>` line + attribution). **Overlay** ([`RecallOverlay.tsx`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/recall/RecallOverlay.tsx)): autofocused `<input>` (RAF-deferred to dodge the mount race, same trick the command palette uses) + `ResultList` (renders `basename / chunk-excerpt` rows with `aria-selected` on the highlighted entry; clicking a row sets `selectedIndex` so mouse and keyboard navigate the same selection state). The `onKeyDown` handler routes Esc → `cancelPendingSearch + close`, Arrow keys → `moveSelection(±1)`, Enter → `insertSelectedSnippet + close`, Cmd/Ctrl+Enter → `copySelectedSnippet + close` (close runs in `.finally` so a clipboard failure still dismisses the overlay). Backdrop click closes; backdrop visual matches the Cmd+I overlay (`oklch(0 0 0 / 0.35)` over the workspace, centred 640px-wide dialog at `paddingTop: 120`). The overlay also runs `cancelPendingSearch` from a `useEffect` cleanup when `visible` flips false, so a late timer can't repopulate a freshly-closed overlay even if the close was via backdrop click rather than Esc. **Coverage**: `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 521 passing + 1 skipped (was 499 / 1; +22 net): 8 store tests in [`recallStore.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/recall/recallStore.test.ts) covering `open()` reset, `close()` retention, `setQuery` non-touch of results, request-id guard on `setResults`, arrow-key clamp at both ends, no-results clamp, reclamp on shorter results list, and `setError` state shape; 5 formatter tests in [`insertFormat.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/recall/insertFormat.test.ts) covering single-line snapshot, multi-line line-prefixing, whitespace trim, empty-chunk handling, and the `.md`-only suffix-stripping rule (`.markdown` and no-suffix names pass through unchanged); 9 runtime tests in [`recallRuntime.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/recall/recallRuntime.test.ts) covering `filterToInboxScope` keep / passthrough / degrade-to-unfiltered, `runSearch` decoder mapping (incl. malformed-entry rejection), inbox-filter wire-up, kernel-error → status:error, debounce empty-query short-circuit, debounce burst-collapse (3 rapid calls → 1 kernel hit with the last query), and a pin-test on `RECALL_DEBOUNCE_MS = 200`. The co-located `*.test.ts` files are re-imported from [`shell/tests/recall.test.ts`](../../shell/tests/recall.test.ts) so the workspace runner's `tests/*.test.ts` glob picks them up. The CodeMirror view splice + clipboard write are exercised at the formatter/store level only — wiring `getActiveCmView()` to a real DOM is out of scope for `node:test`, mirroring the BL-034 / BL-039 ghost-completion test discipline. `pnpm --filter nexus-shell typecheck` clean; `pnpm --filter nexus-shell lint` clean (no new warnings beyond the pre-existing pile). No Rust changes → `scripts/check_ipc_drift.sh` not required. **Out of scope** per the task allowance: a multi-path / tag-based inbox filter (today only the single `memory.inboxPath` file is honoured — BL-046's "from project" filter primitives will replace this); a "no editor active" toast on plain-Enter when there's nothing to insert into (today the splice silently no-ops + closes — a future polish pass can `api.notifications.show` the warning); per-result preview popover with the full chunk text (today rows show a one-line ellipsis-clipped excerpt — the formatter already round-trips the full text into the inserted snippet, so the popover would be cosmetic); cycling through alternate matches when multiple chunks share a `file_path` (today rows are de-duplicated by `${file_path}:${block_id ?? i}` — a richer chunk-picker is a follow-up); persisting the recall hotkey through Tauri's global-shortcut surface so a backgrounded Nexus stays reachable for recall (the BL-043 capture overlay does this via `tauri-plugin-global-shortcut`; BL-044 ships in-window-only because reaching the editor caret only makes sense when the editor is focused, but a future BL can mirror the global-hotkey path if the recall surface grows a "summon Nexus first, then recall" flow). Shipped commits `8c05621` (plugin scaffold + store + runtime + formatter), `caf4fef` (RecallOverlay UI + 22 unit tests).

### BL-035: Right-click AI actions + block AI actions (shared registry) ✅ (2026-04-29)

**Delivered:** AI-AMBIENT-COPILOT-PLAN pattern 5 + the Notion-block follow-up "block AI actions via `com.nexus.ai`" land as a shared in-tree registry plus four shipped built-ins. **Extension-API contract** ([`packages/nexus-extension-api/src/index.ts`](../../packages/nexus-extension-api/src/index.ts)): new `AiActionSurface = 'editor.selection' | 'block' | 'canvas.node'`, three discriminated payload interfaces (`AiActionEditorSelectionContext` carries `relpath` + `selection` + `selectionRange`; `AiActionBlockContext` carries `relpath` + `blockId` + `blockText`; `AiActionCanvasNodeContext` reserved for BL-038), `AiAction { id, label, surfaces, run(ctx) }`, and `AiAPI { registerAction(action): Disposable }`. `NexusPluginContext` gains an `ai: AiAPI` field — types-only at the package boundary; runtime impl is supplied by the host (mirrors how `editor` / `ui` / `workspace` already split). **Singleton registry** ([`shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/actions/registry.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/actions/registry.ts)) mirrors the `contextContributors.ts` shape: `register(action)` returns an idempotent disposer, `list()` snapshots in registration order, `actionsForSurface(surface)` filters by surface tag, `invoke(action, ctx)` catches + `console.warn`s thrown handlers so a misbehaving action can never crash the menu, `_resetForTests()` for isolation. **Built-ins** ([`shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/actions/builtins.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/actions/builtins.ts)): `nexus.ai.summarize`, `nexus.ai.rewrite`, `nexus.ai.translate`, `nexus.ai.explain`, every one wired to `surfaces: ['editor.selection', 'block']`. Each `run(ctx)` extracts the selection/block text, builds a per-action system prompt + user turn, and dispatches through a new [`aiRuntime.streamChat({ messages, system, tools: 'auto' })`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/aiRuntime.ts) helper that wraps `com.nexus.ai::stream_chat` (handler id 6) so the BL-016 tool registry is advertised. Translate honours an optional `targetLanguage` (default `English`); the action's `label` reflects the active language (`Translate to French`). **Output routing**: v1 surfaces results via `api.notifications.show` (clipped to 240 chars in the toast) plus a `console.info` mirror for the developer console, because no `com.nexus.editor::insert_after_selection` IPC exists yet and the task explicitly forbids inventing one — when that IPC lands, swap `surfaceResult` to splice inline. **Plugin registration**: [`shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/index.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/index.ts) `activate()` calls `registerBuiltinAiActions(api)` alongside the existing `registerEditorContextAdapter()`; same disposer-not-tracked rationale (module-scope singleton + no `deactivate` hook + registry tolerates hot-reload duplicates). **Deferred**: hooking the registry into the editor's right-click selection context menu and the block-handle menu is parked for a follow-up — the existing block-handle UI in [`shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/cm/blockHandle.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/cm/blockHandle.ts) renders rows imperatively from a hard-coded `items` array, and the editor selection context menu doesn't exist as a wired surface today (right-click selection just gets the browser default). The registry + built-ins are reachable now via `aiActionRegistry.actionsForSurface(...)`, so the menu-wiring patch is purely additive. **Coverage**: 7 new tests in [`registry.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/actions/registry.test.ts) (register/list ordering, empty-id rejection, surface filter, disposer isolation + idempotency, throwing-handler containment, async happy-path) + 5 new tests in [`builtins.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/actions/builtins.test.ts) (four-action manifest, surfaces include both editor.selection + block, translate `targetLanguage` override, `stream_chat` dispatch shape with `tools: 'auto'`, bulk-register disposer). `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 463 passing (was 456); `typecheck` + `lint` clean (no new warnings). No Rust crates change → no IPC drift check needed. Shipped commit `60a0657`.

### BL-027: Multi-agent orchestration / delegation ✅ (2026-04-29)

**Delivered:** PRD-15 §10's `AgentOrchestrator::delegate / parallel / pipeline` lands as a new module on `nexus-agent` with four IPC handlers wired onto `com.nexus.agent`. Pre-BL-027 a `LlmAgent` planned + executed solo; the orchestrator now hands subtasks between archetypes (Researcher → Writer → Coder) with shared scratch state and an append-only trace log. **Library** ([`crates/nexus-agent/src/orchestrator.rs`](../../crates/nexus-agent/src/orchestrator.rs)): generic `AgentOrchestrator<D: ChatDriver + Clone + 'static, P: ToolDispatcher + Clone>` holding the driver factory, dispatcher, an `Arc<RwLock<HashMap<String, serde_json::Value>>>` scratch map, and an `Arc<Mutex<Vec<TraceEntry>>>` trace log. `delegate(archetype, goal, skills)` builds an archetype `LlmAgent` via `build_archetype`, plans via `Agent::plan`, executes via `PlanExecutor::run`, and appends a `TraceEntry { stage_idx, archetype, goal, started_at_ms, ended_at_ms, status, summary }` whether the stage succeeded, failed at the planner, or failed mid-execution. `parallel(jobs)` fans out via `futures::future::join_all` and returns observations in input order; failed jobs surface as a synthetic failed `Observation` so the positional vector stays aligned and the trace carries the per-stage status. `pipeline(stages)` runs sequentially, stashing each observation's textual summary under `"prev"` and substituting `{{prev}}` into the next stage's `goal_template` before planning; first failure halts and returns the partial vector (not `Err`) so the caller still sees pre-failure work. **IPC** ([`crates/nexus-agent/src/core_plugin.rs`](../../crates/nexus-agent/src/core_plugin.rs)): four new append-only handler ids — `HANDLER_DELEGATE: u32 = 9`, `HANDLER_PARALLEL: u32 = 10`, `HANDLER_PIPELINE: u32 = 11`, `HANDLER_TRACE_GET: u32 = 12`. DTOs: `DelegateArgs { archetype, goal }`, `ParallelArgs { jobs: Vec<ParallelJob> }`, `PipelineArgs { stages: Vec<PipelineStage { archetype, goal_template }> }`, response wrapper `TraceResponse { entries: Vec<TraceEntry> }`. The plugin caches one orchestrator behind a `std::sync::Mutex<Option<Arc<…>>>` so trace + scratch state survive across handler calls — the cache is wired the first time any of the four handlers fire and reuses the same `AiChatBridge` + `KernelToolBridge` adapters the existing `plan` / `run` handlers use (both bridges are now `#[derive(Clone)]` to satisfy the orchestrator generics). The kernel-context wiring lives in `dispatch_async` so a non-orchestrator handler still sees the same eager-context error as before. **Coverage**: `cargo test -p nexus-agent` 25 passing (was 21; +4 net). Three new in-module unit tests in `orchestrator.rs` (`delegate_runs_and_appends_trace`, `scratch_state_round_trips`, `trace_ordering_reflects_append_order`) plus one new e2e test in [`crates/nexus-agent/tests/orchestrator_e2e.rs`](../../crates/nexus-agent/tests/orchestrator_e2e.rs) (`pipeline_substitutes_prev_and_returns_two_observations`) wiring a branching `ChatDriver` that swaps replies based on the system prompt — researcher returns a one-step plan with description `"find data X"`, writer returns `"summary of: {prev}"`, and the test asserts (a) two observations come back, (b) both succeed, (c) the second `TraceEntry.goal` no longer contains `{{prev}}` and grew beyond the template prefix. `cargo clippy -p nexus-agent --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean; `bash scripts/check_ipc_drift.sh` clean (no schema drift — these handlers don't expose ts-rs types). **Out of scope**: skill layering on `delegate` (the `_skills` arg is reserved; per the BL-027 task allowance the orchestrator forwards `None` to `build_archetype` today and callers thread skill-resolved prompts through the goal text); replay hooks (PRD-15 §12 — deferred until orchestration UX settles); reactive rules (PRD §6.3 — same). Shipped commits `8ef52f8` (orchestrator + unit tests) and `4242b90` (IPC handlers + e2e test).

### BL-022: Skill in-app editor UI ✅ (2026-04-29)

**Delivered:** PRD-13 §16's in-app editor lands in `shell/src/plugins/nexus/skills/`. Pre-BL-022 the Skills panel was read-only — mutations required editing `.skill.md` on disk and calling `reload` by hand. The new editor surfaces an "Edit", "Delete", and "+ New skill" affordance, round-tripping every save through the existing `com.nexus.storage::write_file` + `com.nexus.skills::reload` pair (no bespoke "save_skill" IPC — the storage handler stays the single source of write truth per ADR-0005). **Wire-shape augmentation**: `com.nexus.skills::list` and `::get` now include a `relpath` field on each entry — `Vec<u8>` builders in [`core_plugin.rs`](../../crates/nexus-skills/src/core_plugin.rs) `dispatch_list` / `dispatch_get` augment each `Skill` JSON value with the forge-relative path computed from `SkillRegistry::path_for(...)` against the configured root. Append-only on the wire — pre-BL-022 consumers ignore the new field. New helper [`relpath_for(root, abs)`](../../crates/nexus-skills/src/core_plugin.rs) returns the canonical `.forge/skills/<sub>/<name>.skill.md` shape with forward slashes (the storage handler canonicalises to the platform separator on its end). **New components**: [`SkillEditor.tsx`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/skills/SkillEditor.tsx) is a standalone form taking only a `kernel: SkillsKernelAPI` prop — frontmatter goes through a typed `<FrontmatterForm>` (id, name, description, version, author, created, plus comma-separated `tags` / `applicable_contexts` / `triggers` / `depends_on` via `<ListField>`); body goes through a `<BodyField>` textarea. The component is split into per-row sub-components specifically so future surfaces (BL-046's "code-aware capture" UI patterns per the BACKLOG risk #5 note) can swap the body editor without touching the frontmatter form. The editor is mounted both inline inside the expanded `<SkillRow>` (when `editingId === skill.id`) and as a standalone panel pinned to the top of the listing (when `editingId === '__new__'`). **Store extensions** ([`skillsStore.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/skills/skillsStore.ts)): new `SkillDraft` interface; new state `editingId: string | null`, `draft: SkillDraft | null`, `saveError`, `saving`; new actions `openEditor(id)` / `openNewSkill()` / `cancelEditor()` / `patchDraft(patch)` / `saveDraft(api)` / `deleteSkill(api, id)`. `openEditor` hydrates the draft straight from the listing snapshot (the kernel returns the full body in `list`, so no extra round trip). `openNewSkill` seeds a starter draft with today's date as `created` and `version: 0.1.0`. `patchDraft` keeps the relpath in lockstep with the id slug for new skills (the user picks the slug; the file path follows). **Serialization**: new pure `serializeDraft(draft) -> string` re-emits the `.skill.md` format — `---\n<yaml frontmatter>\n---\n<body>` — with a stable key order (id-like fields first, then descriptive, then list fields) so a save round-trip is deterministic and diff-friendly. Conservative scalar quoting handles the YAML-reserved bare words (`true`, `false`, `null`, `yes`, …) and numeric-looking strings; multi-line scalars fall back to JSON-style. New `validateDraft(draft) -> string | null` checks every required frontmatter field plus the kebab-case id pattern (mirrors the kernel-side `parse_skill_text`'s required-field set) so the user catches problems before disk I/O — and `saveDraft` no-ops the IPC call when validation fails. **Save flow**: `saveDraft` calls `com.nexus.storage::write_file({ path, bytes: number[] })` (UTF-8 encoded via `TextEncoder`), then `com.nexus.skills::reload({})` to make the registry pick up the new file. Reload failure logs a warning but doesn't fail the save (the file is on disk; the next `refresh` will see it). On success the editor closes and the listing refreshes via a new module-local `subscribeSkillsChanged(listener)` channel — chosen over `eventBus.emit` to keep `skillsStore.ts` clean of `host/EventBus` imports (the `plugin-import-hygiene.test` guards that boundary). The `subscribeSkillsChanged` API mirrors the singleton-module pattern used by `contextContributors` in `nexus.ai`. **Delete flow**: `deleteSkill(api, id)` confirms via `window.confirm`, calls `delete_file` + `reload`, and optimistically prunes the listing so the row vanishes before the next refresh round-trip lands. **Edit/Delete gating**: both buttons hide for skills loaded out-of-tree (empty `relpath`) — the kernel can't write back to a skill it didn't load from disk (built-in skills bundled in the binary, hypothetical future plugin-supplied skills). **BL-021 surface**: the expanded panel now renders a `depends_on` chip row alongside `tags` / `contexts` / `triggers` so the inheritance chain is visible on the listing. **Coverage**: `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 462 passing (was 456; +6 net). New tests in [`skillsStore.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/skills/skillsStore.test.ts): `serializeDraft round-trips frontmatter + body`, `serializeDraft quotes scalars that look numeric or reserved`, `validateDraft surfaces required-field messages`, `openEditor seeds the draft from the listing snapshot`, `saveDraft: write_file then reload, then editor closes` (asserts the IPC call ordering), `saveDraft: validation failure sets saveError without IPC`. `pnpm --filter nexus-shell typecheck` and `lint` clean (no new warnings). `cargo test -p nexus-skills` still 51 passing — the `relpath` augmentation is a wire-shape addition only. **Out of scope**: live preview during edit (existing `<RenderForm>` flow is the rendering surface — invoked from the same expanded panel without round-tripping through the editor); markdown WYSIWYG (textarea is the v1 body editor); rename-as-move semantics (changing the id of an existing skill writes a new file; the old one needs to be deleted explicitly). Shipped commit `3438b29`.

### BL-021: Skill `depends_on` composition resolver ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** PRD-13 §5's four sub-tasks land as new [`crates/nexus-skills/src/compose.rs`](../../crates/nexus-skills/src/compose.rs) plus a new IPC handler and a planner-side consumer. **Sub-task 1 — parse `depends_on`** was already wired (`SkillMeta.depends_on: Vec<String>`); the new module just consumes it. **Sub-task 2 — topological sort + cycle detection**: iterative DFS with the standard white/gray/black colouring. A back-edge into a `Gray` node reconstructs the offending cycle path from the active stack — `ComposeError::Cycle { path: Vec<String> }` carries `[a, b, c, a]` so the operator sees the loop without re-walking. Self-cycles, indirect cycles, and unresolvable ids each surface as a distinct typed variant (`Cycle` / `MissingDependency { from, missing }` / `UnknownRoot`). Diamond inheritance dedupes naturally — visiting a `Black` node short-circuits — so `d → b → a; d → c → a` produces `[a, b, c, d]` with `a` appearing once. **Sub-task 3 — prompt-fragment merge order**: post-order DFS puts dependencies first and the root last, mirroring how class inheritance reads top-down. Within a layer, children are visited in `depends_on` declaration order so the output is stable across runs. The merged body emits each fragment under a `## Skill: <name> [<id>]` heading separated by blank lines, giving the model a clear boundary to latch onto. **Sub-task 4 — conflict-warning UX**: non-fatal `ComposeConflict` enum with two variants today: `ParameterClash { parameter, skill_ids }` (two ancestors declare the same parameter name with differing `param_type` or `default`) and `RestrictionsDisagree { field, skill_ids }` (`modify_files` / `delete_content` / `execute_code` / `allowed_tools` levers carrying contradictory values across the closure). Conflicts ride alongside `fragments` + `merged_body` on `ComposedSkill` so the Skills UI can surface a banner without losing the merged composition. **IPC handler 7 — `compose`**: new [`HANDLER_COMPOSE: u32 = 7`](../../crates/nexus-skills/src/core_plugin.rs) registered in [`nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs`](../../crates/nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs) under the `com.nexus.skills` manifest. Args: `{ id }`. Returns `ComposedSkill` JSON: `{ root_id, fragments: [{ id, name, body }], merged_body, conflicts: [{ kind, ... }] }`. Handler ids are append-only — pre-BL-021 callers (`list` / `get` / `list_by_context` / `triggered_by` / `reload` / `render`) are untouched. **Planner integration**: [`nexus-agent`](../../crates/nexus-agent/src/core_plugin.rs)'s `system_prompt_with_skills` now calls a new `compose_skill_body(ctx, id)` for each triggered skill BEFORE falling back to the single-skill `render_skill_body`. The composed merged body replaces the per-skill section so an inheritance chain like `concise → markdown-style → rust` contributes every layer's instructions in topo order. Errors (cycle / missing dep / IPC unavailable) silently degrade to the pre-BL-021 single-skill path so a broken dep graph never blocks planning. Conflicts are emitted via `tracing::warn!` with `skill_id` + `conflict_count` so operators can spot them in logs without us having to plumb an event channel through to the planner UI; the Skills panel will surface them through the IPC response when BL-022 lands. **Coverage**: `cargo test -p nexus-skills` 51 passing (was 42; +9 net). New tests: `compose_returns_self_only_when_no_deps`, `compose_orders_deps_before_dependents`, `compose_diamond_dedupes_to_single_visit`, `compose_reports_cycle_with_full_path`, `compose_reports_self_cycle`, `compose_reports_missing_dependency`, `compose_reports_unknown_root`, `compose_surfaces_parameter_clash`, `compose_surfaces_restriction_disagreement`. `cargo clippy -p nexus-skills -p nexus-agent -p nexus-bootstrap --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean. **Out of scope**: parameter-substitution composition (compose returns raw bodies; per-fragment `render` substitution is a follow-up if needed); UI surfacing of conflicts inside the Skills panel (folded into BL-022). Shipped commit `4838e8e`.

### BL-025: MCP authentication ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** PRD-14 §8's three auth flows land as a tagged enum on the BL-023 transport layer. New [`crates/nexus-mcp/src/auth.rs`](../../crates/nexus-mcp/src/auth.rs) module exposes `pub enum McpAuth { ApiKey { header, value }, Bearer { token }, OauthClientCredentials { token_url, client_id, client_secret, scope } }` with `#[serde(tag = "type", rename_all = "snake_case")]` so a `mcp.toml` block reads naturally:

```toml
[servers.alpha.auth]
type = "api_key"
header = "X-API-Key"
env = "ALPHA_API_KEY"

[servers.beta.auth]
type = "bearer"
token = "ey…"

[servers.gamma.auth]
type = "oauth_client_credentials"
token_url = "https://auth.example.com/oauth2/token"
client_id_env = "GAMMA_CLIENT_ID"
client_secret_env = "GAMMA_CLIENT_SECRET"
scope = "mcp:tools"
```

Each secret-bearing field uses an untagged `McpAuthSecret { Inline { value }, Env { env } }` (or its `client_id` / `client_secret` siblings) so `value = "…"` and `env = "…"` are mutually exclusive in the file — empty/unset env vars surface as a typed `AuthError::MissingEnv { name }` at resolve time. Future ADR-0009 keyring integration slots in alongside `Env` without a wire-format break (consumers of `ResolvedAuth` see only the final string regardless of source). [`auth::resolve(auth) -> Result<ResolvedAuth, AuthError>`](../../crates/nexus-mcp/src/auth.rs) is pure for `ApiKey` / `Bearer` (no I/O); the `OauthClientCredentials` path POSTs `grant_type=client_credentials` to the token endpoint via the workspace `reqwest 0.12` client (HTTP Basic auth on the credentials per RFC 6749 §2.3.1, `scope` in the form body, 30 s timeout — same order of magnitude as the rmcp `CONNECT_TIMEOUT`), parses the `TokenResponse`, validates `token_type` is `bearer` (case-insensitive), and returns the access token wrapped as `Bearer <token>`. Bearer's resolver is tolerant of either `"ey…"` or `"Bearer ey…"` so an operator migrating from a hand-rolled `auth_header = "Bearer …"` setup just changes the table header without re-stringing. `ApiKey` lands on `Authorization` if the `header` field is the canonical name (case-insensitive); otherwise on `extra_headers` so it ends up in rmcp's `custom_headers` map. **New `auth: Option<McpAuth>` field on [`McpServerSpec`](../../crates/nexus-mcp/src/config.rs)** with `skip_serializing_if = "Option::is_none"` so existing pre-BL-025 files round-trip untouched. **Wire-up in [`McpClient::connect_http`](../../crates/nexus-mcp/src/client.rs)**: when `spec.auth` is set the resolver runs first and any `MissingEnv` / `Oauth` / `OauthResponse` failure aborts connect with a new `McpClientError::Auth(#[from] AuthError)` variant — the operator gets a typed error pointing at the failing env var or token endpoint instead of the generic `Handshake` they used to see when the request landed without credentials. Resolved auth is merged into rmcp's `auth_header(...)` slot for `Authorization`-bearing flows and into `custom_headers(...)` for non-`Authorization` API keys; the legacy static `auth_header` field from BL-023 still works (back-compat with installs that pinned a token by hand) but a present `auth` block always wins on conflict — declarative beats legacy. **Why a hand-rolled flow rather than rmcp's `auth` feature**: rmcp 1.5 ships a full OAuth manager (`rmcp::transport::auth`) that covers PKCE / refresh tokens / DCR, but enabling it pulls in extra TLS-feature scaffolding the workspace doesn't otherwise need and exposes a stateful `OAuthState` surface that's overkill for the single-shot client-credentials flow PRD-14 §8 calls for. The ~50 lines in `auth.rs` are faster to audit and reuse the workspace `reqwest 0.12` already in the closure for the AI provider crates (rmcp's reqwest 0.13 is the rmcp transport's, not ours). Refresh-on-401 is deliberately not implemented — token is refetched on the next `connect()` (the rmcp transport's expired-session recovery covers MCP-level session expiration; OAuth token expiration is a separate concern that compounding both into one round-trip wouldn't simplify). **ADR-0009 interaction**: today `Env`-indirected secrets fall through to the env-var lookup; the same `McpAuthSecret` enum can grow a `Keyring { service, account }` variant when ADR-0009's keyring service lands without breaking deployed `mcp.toml` files. **Coverage**: `cargo test -p nexus-mcp` 47 passing (was 38; +9 net). New tests in [`auth.rs`](../../crates/nexus-mcp/src/auth.rs): `api_key_inline_authorization_lands_on_authorization_slot`, `api_key_custom_header_lands_on_extras`, `bearer_inline_prepends_scheme_when_missing`, `bearer_inline_preserves_caller_supplied_scheme`, `env_indirection_resolves_when_set`, `env_indirection_errors_when_unset`, `toml_parses_api_key_with_env_indirection`, `toml_parses_oauth_client_credentials`. New integration test in [`client.rs`](../../crates/nexus-mcp/src/client.rs): `http_transport_auth_missing_env_surfaces_as_auth_error` (proves the typed `Auth(MissingEnv)` error fires from `connect()` before any network I/O happens). `cargo clippy -p nexus-mcp --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean. **Out of scope**: PKCE / authorization-code flow / DCR / refresh tokens (rmcp's `auth` feature is the natural home if those are wanted later); keyring integration (waits on ADR-0009 enforcement). Shipped commit `ac36715`.

### BL-023: MCP WebSocket + HTTP+SSE transports ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** PRD-14 §4.2 lands behind a transport-abstraction layer in `nexus-mcp`. Pre-BL-023 [`McpClient::connect`](../../crates/nexus-mcp/src/client.rs) only spawned a child process and ran the MCP handshake over its stdio (`TokioChildProcess`). `mcp.toml` now carries a per-entry [`McpTransport`](../../crates/nexus-mcp/src/config.rs) discriminator (`stdio` / `http` / `websocket`) keyed off a new `transport` field on [`McpServerSpec`](../../crates/nexus-mcp/src/config.rs); back-compat is preserved by `transport = "stdio"` being the serde default — every existing file that omits the field continues to dispatch through the original child-process path. New remote-only fields ride on the same struct (`url: Option<String>`, `auth_header: Option<String>`, `headers: BTreeMap<String, String>`) with `skip_serializing_if` so stdio-mode entries don't grow unused TOML keys on round-trip. Validation moved into [`McpHostConfig::validate`](../../crates/nexus-mcp/src/config.rs): stdio entries must have a non-empty `command`; http / websocket entries must have a non-empty `url`. **HTTP+SSE (Streamable HTTP)**: `McpClient::connect_http` constructs an [`rmcp::transport::StreamableHttpClientTransport`](https://docs.rs/rmcp/1.5.0/rmcp/transport/struct.StreamableHttpClientTransport.html) via `from_config(StreamableHttpClientTransportConfig::with_uri(...).custom_headers(...).auth_header(...))`. Header strings are validated up front (`http::HeaderName::try_from` / `HeaderValue::try_from`) so malformed entries surface as `McpClientError::Config` before any wire I/O — easier to diagnose than rmcp's typed-error stack on first request. The reqwest-backed default client is constructed inside rmcp via the new `transport-streamable-http-client-reqwest` feature; the call site deliberately does NOT name `reqwest::Client` because the workspace pins reqwest 0.12 for the AI provider crates while rmcp 1.5 ships with reqwest 0.13, and the two `Client` types are not interchangeable. Going through rmcp's `from_config` constructor avoids the version gap (an in-source comment documents the rationale so a future bump doesn't re-introduce a typed `reqwest::Client` reference). New rmcp features added to the workspace dep: `transport-streamable-http-client`, `transport-streamable-http-client-reqwest`, `reqwest-native-tls` (so `reqwest 0.13` picks up native-TLS for the system OpenSSL, dodging the rustls crypto-provider panic on `Client::new` that fired without an explicit TLS feature), and `client-side-sse`. **WebSocket (reserved)**: rmcp 1.5 ships only a stub at [`src/transport/ws.rs`](https://docs.rs/rmcp/1.5.0/src/rmcp/transport/ws.rs) whose top-of-file comment is "Maybe we don't really need a ws implementation?" — the MCP working group folded WebSocket into Streamable HTTP in the 2025-03-26 spec, deprecating the WS transport upstream. Honoring that direction, `McpTransport::Websocket` parses cleanly in `mcp.toml` (so a deployed file declaring it doesn't fail to load) but `connect()` returns a precise `McpClientError::Unsupported` whose message points the operator at `transport = "http"`. The variant stays in the schema so a future rmcp WS impl can be wired in without a breaking config change. New `McpClientError` variants: `Config { reason }` (validated-up-front spec-shape errors) and `Unsupported { reason }` (recognised-but-not-dispatchable transports). The existing `Spawn` / `Handshake` / `Service` cases are unchanged. **Refactor**: the handshake driver moved into a `run_handshake<F, E>(...)` helper so both transport branches race the rmcp `serve_client(...)` future against the existing `CONNECT_TIMEOUT` (15 s) uniformly; previously the timeout policy was inlined in the stdio branch. **Coverage**: `cargo test -p nexus-mcp` 38 passing (was 28; +10 net). New tests in [`config.rs`](../../crates/nexus-mcp/src/config.rs): `parses_http_transport` (the full remote shape), `http_transport_requires_url`, `stdio_transport_default_keeps_back_compat` (regression for the no-`transport` file format), `websocket_transport_parses_but_is_reserved`. New tests in [`client.rs`](../../crates/nexus-mcp/src/client.rs): `websocket_transport_returns_unsupported` (asserts the migration hint mentions both "WebSocket" and "http"), `http_transport_rejects_missing_url_with_config_error`, `http_transport_rejects_invalid_header_name`, `http_transport_handshake_times_out_against_dead_endpoint` (routes through `connect_http` against `http://127.0.0.1:1` and asserts non-success without panicking). `cargo clippy -p nexus-mcp --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean. **Out of scope**: connection pooling / reconnection policy (lives in `pool.rs` and is transport-agnostic — pre-BL-023 design intent already covers both transports because each `McpClient` is opaque to the pool). Shipped commit `1aeaa7a`.

### BL-033: AMB context chips + model switcher ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** Closes the AI-AMBIENT-COPILOT-PLAN patterns 2 + 3 follow-on to BL-032 by giving the Cmd+I overlay both a click-to-remove chip rail and a per-overlay model switcher whose selection writes through to the global `ai.provider` / `ai.model` config keys. **Click-to-remove**: chips in [`CmdIOverlay.tsx`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/CmdIOverlay.tsx)'s `ContextChipRail` are now `<button role="listitem">`s with a trailing "×" affordance, an aria-label and a kind-prefix glyph (📄 file, ✂ selection, ▦ block, ≡ row, ◇ node, ? query, ✎ note); clicking dispatches `useCmdIStore.removeChip(id)` (new action; the store grows a `removedChipIds: string[]` tracked alongside `chips`, reset on every `open()`). The runtime threads removal through to the prompt assembler — [`cmdIRuntime.submitCmdI`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/cmdIRuntime.ts) builds a `Set<string>` from `removedChipIds` and passes it as the third arg to [`assemblePrompt`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/contextContributors.ts), which gained a new `removedChipIds: ReadonlySet<string>` parameter and a new optional `chipPromptBlocks?: Record<chipId, string>` field on `ContextContribution` for chip-granular fragments. Two assembly modes coexist: **per-chip** (when `chipPromptBlocks` is set, only kept chips' fragments are emitted, in chip order) and **coarse fallback** (drop the whole surface's `promptBlock` only when ALL of its chips were removed). The editor adapter at [`editorContextAdapter.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/editorContextAdapter.ts) was reshaped to populate `chipPromptBlocks` for both the file chip and the selection chip so removing one no longer drops the other's body. **Model switcher**: a new `<ModelSwitcher>` native `<select>` sits between the chip rail and the textarea. Six presets ship today (Anthropic Opus 4.7 / Sonnet 4.6 / Haiku 4.5; OpenAI GPT-4o / GPT-4o-mini; Ollama llama3.1) — selecting one calls `useConfigStore.set('ai.provider', …)` + `set('ai.model', …)`, which fires `config:changed:ai.provider` / `config:changed:ai.model` events the AI plugin's [`index.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/index.ts) `aiKeys` listener already forwards to the kernel via `pushUserConfig` → `set_config` (handler id 1). Same keys back the Settings panel — toggles in the overlay become the new global default and persist into the chat surface and ghost completions. The control reads via `useConfigValue` so it re-renders reactively when those keys change anywhere in the app; non-preset settings (env-var fallback, custom model strings) are surfaced as a disabled `(custom)` row so the user sees what's active without us silently overwriting it. **Wire shape unchanged** — no IPC drift was needed: BL-033 reuses `set_config` for the model bind and `stream_chat` for the prompt, so `scripts/check_ipc_drift.sh` is a no-op. **Coverage**: `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 462 passing (was 456); new tests cover (a) `removeChip` idempotency + reset on `open()` in [`cmdIStore.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/cmdIStore.test.ts), (b) per-chip vs coarse removal semantics for `assemblePrompt` (3 cases) in [`contextContributors.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/contextContributors.test.ts), and (c) end-to-end in [`cmdIRuntime.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/cmdIRuntime.test.ts) where a removed `editor:selection:*` chip drops only the selection fragment from the assembled `stream_chat` payload. `pnpm --filter nexus-shell typecheck` and `pnpm --filter nexus-shell lint` clean (no new warnings). Shipped commit `1b3e5ac`.

### BL-034: AMB ghost suggestions (CM6 inline-completion decoration) ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** The Phase-2 lock-in's "ghost completion shares the engine with `nexus ai complete`" requirement lands as new [`shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/cm/ghostCompletion.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/cm/ghostCompletion.ts). Typing in a markdown source-mode editor triggers a debounced call to `com.nexus.ai::stream_chat` with `mode = complete`, `tools = none`, `trim = true`, `max_tokens = 64`, `stop = ["\n\n"]` — byte-for-byte the same shape BL-011's CLI uses. The suggested continuation renders as a `Decoration.widget` after the caret with `opacity: 0.45` muted styling and `pointer-events: none` so clicks land on the underlying line. Tab accepts (inserts the suggestion as plain text and clears the field); Esc dismisses. Both bindings sit at `Prec.high` and return `false`-fallthrough so the editor's normal Tab / Esc resume when no suggestion is live. Single-flight + cancel-on-edit: a monotonic `requestId` tags every fetch; `update.docChanged || update.selectionSet` invalidates the in-flight request and any rendered widget (the field's update predicate also clears non-effect doc changes / selection moves). Late resolutions for stale prefixes are dropped silently rather than surfaced — ghost is best-effort UX, not a notification surface. Five new `ai.ghost.*` settings (`enabled` / `debounceMs` / `minChars` / `contextChars` / `maxTokens`) live in the AI plugin's [configuration schema](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/index.ts) so the Settings panel auto-renders them; the CM extension reads them lazily per fetch via `configStore.get(...)` so live edits take effect on the next keystroke without remounting the editor. New [`ghostApi.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/ghostApi.ts) singleton (mirror of `cmdIApi.ts`) holds the `PluginAPI` handle so the CM extension factory — which runs far from the AI plugin's activate closure — can reach `api.kernel.invoke`. The extension is composed alongside `transactionBridge` / `slashCommandExt` / `blockSelectionExt` / etc. inside [`EditorView.tsx`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/EditorView.tsx)'s `buildExtensions` factory. Trigger heuristic: skip when the prefix doesn't end with whitespace or punctuation so we don't fire mid-word. Coverage: `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 450 passing including 6 new tests in [`ghostCompletion.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/cm/ghostCompletion.test.ts) (state-only — DOM-driven Tab/Esc handlers exercised via integration). Shipped commit `695bbc7`.

### BL-030: Bases per-surface undo / redo ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** PRD-10's bases surface now has the per-base ring-buffered undo/redo the BACKLOG entry specified. New [`shell/src/plugins/nexus/bases/activeBases.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/bases/activeBases.ts) mirrors the `canvas/activeCanvas.ts` registry-of-one pattern: every mounted `BasesView` registers a `BasesHandle { undo, redo, cut, copy, paste }` on focusin and clears it on focusout, and the bases plugin's command handlers dispatch to the active handle via `withActiveBases(...)`. The plugin's `index.ts` contributes two new commands (`nexus.bases.undo` / `nexus.bases.redo`) plus three keybindings (`mod-z` / `mod-shift-z` / `mod-y`) gated on `when: 'bases.focused'`, replacing the duplicate `BasesTable.tsx` keydown branch that only fired when the table itself had focus. Every base-mutating call site that bypassed the `pushHistory` ring buffer is now wrapped in paired forward/reverse `HistoryEntry`s: schema editor mutations (rename / retype / toggle-required / update-options / update-expression / delete-column / add-column), view CRUD (create / update / delete), and the non-Table view drag handlers (`BasesBoard` drop, `BasesCalendar` create-on-day). Schema retypes and column deletes snapshot per-record values for lossless undo; bases > 50,000 records refuse to push the destructive entry and surface a "history truncated" hint via a new `lastUndoError` field on `BasesTabState` rendered as a dismissable banner. Toolbar undo/redo buttons now live on `BasesView` for parity across all view modes. Coverage: shell tests pass with 10 new BL-030-specific tests in `basesStore.test.ts` (history cap, redo-stack-clear-on-push, cell-edit / add-row / soft-delete / schema-rename / schema-delete-with-cell-restore round-trips, view CRUD round-trips, focus-gated command dispatch). Per-surface undo only — global cross-surface Cmd-Z stays the explicit non-goal documented in the BACKLOG 2026-04-28 design note. Shipped commit `f42020c`.

### BL-043: MEM quick-capture hotkey ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** AI-MEMORY-LAYER-PLAN piece 1 lands as a pure-file-write capture pipeline with no AI dependency. **Rust-side** (commit `e53b617`): new [`com.nexus.storage::note_append`](../../crates/nexus-storage/src/core_plugin.rs) IPC handler (id 54) does an atomic "read existing + append `\n\n{snippet}` + write" through the same `StorageEngine::write_file` safety path as `write_file` — confines paths to the forge root and rejects absolute paths up front. Mirrored types `StorageNoteAppendArgs` / `StorageNoteAppendResult` in [`nexus-storage/src/ipc.rs`](../../crates/nexus-storage/src/ipc.rs) with `#[derive(TS, JsonSchema)]`; manifest mapping in `nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs`; TS + JSON Schema bindings emitted via the existing pilot harness. **Shell side** (commit `0d4e8e6`): `tauri-plugin-global-shortcut@2` wired into the Builder in [`shell/src-tauri/src/lib.rs`](../../shell/src-tauri/src/lib.rs), capability permissions added (`global-shortcut:default` + `allow-register` + `allow-unregister`), and `@tauri-apps/plugin-global-shortcut@^2.0.0` added to `shell/package.json`. New [`shell/src/plugins/nexus/memory/`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/memory/) plugin (default-on so the global shortcut is registered at boot): `index.ts` contributes the manifest commands `nexus.memory.captureOpen` / `nexus.memory.captureCommit` plus the `memory.hotkey` (default `CommandOrControl+Alt+N` to avoid Spotlight collision) and `memory.inboxPath` (default `Inbox.md`) configuration keys; `kernelClient.ts` typed-wraps `appendInbox(path, snippet)`; `captureStore.ts` Zustand store with `{ open, draft, error, sourceMeta }` + commit pipeline + best-effort `navigator.clipboard.readText()` pre-fill (handles a rejection cleanly); `CaptureOverlay.tsx` in-window slot modal with `Mod+Enter` save / `Esc` cancel. Detects "no forge" via `api.kernel.isBooted()` and surfaces an error toast instead of opening the overlay. Coverage: `cargo test -p nexus-storage` 335 passing including 5 new BL-043 tests; shell tests pass with 5 new tests in `memory-capture-store.test.ts`. Out of scope per the BL-043 plan: separate `WebviewWindow` capture (in-window overlay only — Tauri global-shortcut fires regardless of focus, sufficient for the alt-tab → hotkey workflow); proper OS-level source-app metadata (v1 stores `document.title` only — needs `tauri-plugin-os` for cross-platform fidelity, deferred follow-up).

### BL-032: Cmd+I command-anywhere AI overlay ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Source**: [../AI-AMBIENT-COPILOT-PLAN.md](../AI-AMBIENT-COPILOT-PLAN.md) pattern 1.
**Effort**: Medium. **Crate / Package**: `shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/`.
**Delivered:** Phase-1 foundation that the BL-010 / BL-011 / BL-033 / BL-034 / BL-044 surfaces all hang off — a modal overlay invocable from any focused surface (`Ctrl+I` / `Cmd+I`) that takes a free-form prompt, gathers per-surface context via a registry of contributor adapters, and routes the assembled prompt through `com.nexus.ai::stream_chat` with an isolated session id so streaming events don't bleed into the chat panel store. Shipped commit `715d82d` (PR #27).

- **Context-contributor registry** ([`contextContributors.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/contextContributors.ts)): singleton-module registry mirroring `fencedCodeRegistry` (BL-008). Each contributor returns a `ContextContribution { surfaceId, chips: ContextChip[], promptBlock?: string, chipPromptBlocks?: Record<chipId, string> }` from an async `collect()` call. `ContextChip` carries `{ id, label, kind }` with `kind ∈ 'file'|'selection'|'block'|'row'|'node'|'query'|'note'` so chips render with kind-prefix glyphs without surface-specific renderers. `assemblePrompt(contributions, removedChipIds)` composes the final user-prompt prefix in two modes — per-chip (when `chipPromptBlocks` is set, only kept chips' fragments emit, in chip order) and coarse fallback (drop the surface's whole `promptBlock` only when ALL of its chips are removed). Adapter contract is async + null-returning so a no-op contribution (e.g. editor with no tab focused) just falls out of the assembled prompt.
- **Editor adapter** ([`editorContextAdapter.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/editorContextAdapter.ts)): first surface adapter, ships in this PR. Reads `useEditorStore` for the active tab + body snapshot and `getActiveCmView()` (sibling-plugin import — same pattern `editor/cm/linkSuggest.ts` uses for BL-039) for the live CodeMirror selection. Emits two chips per activation when there's a selection (file + selection) and one when there isn't (file only); body cap is `8 KB` per file with a line-boundary truncate so the model never sees a half-fenced code block. Lives in the AI plugin's directory rather than the editor plugin's because the editor plugin is default-on and we don't want it depending on a default-off plugin.
- **Store** ([`cmdIStore.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/cmdIStore.ts)): zustand `useCmdIStore` with `{ visible, prompt, chips, removedChipIds, status: 'idle'|'collecting'|'submitting'|'streaming'|'done'|'error', responseText, error, currentRequestId }`. `open()` clears everything per activation so chips/response from a prior summon don't bleed in; status starts `'collecting'` until the runtime hydrates the chips. Tail-chunk guards on `appendResponseChunk` / `finishResponse` reject mismatched `currentRequestId` so a late `stream_chunk` can't append into a closed overlay.
- **Runtime** ([`cmdIRuntime.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/cmdIRuntime.ts)): `openCmdI()` resolves every registered contributor (pure — does NOT call the kernel), pushes chips into the store, and flips `visible: true`. `submitCmdI()` mints a `cmdi-<uuid>` session id (segregates events from the persistent chat panel), assembles the prompt via `assemblePrompt(contributions, new Set(removedChipIds))`, and fires `com.nexus.ai::stream_chat` with `tools: 'auto'` to advertise the BL-016 registry. `routeStreamEvent` is the unified handler the AI plugin's single `com.nexus.ai.stream_*` subscription installs on activate; it dispatches each chunk/done event to either the chat store or the cmd-I store based on the session-id correlation, so the runtime doesn't open a second subscription.
- **Overlay UI** ([`CmdIOverlay.tsx`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/CmdIOverlay.tsx)): chrome `overlay`-slot modal, centred 640px-wide dialog with `oklch(0 0 0 / 0.35)` backdrop. Autofocused `<textarea>` (RAF-deferred to dodge the mount race), `ContextChipRail` rendering the chips read-only in v1 (click-to-remove + the model switcher land in BL-033), streaming response panel below the input, `Esc` closes, `Mod+Enter` submits, plain `Enter` inserts a newline (so multi-line prompts work without bracketed-paste tricks). Backdrop click closes.
- **Plugin wiring** ([`index.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/index.ts)): manifest contributes commands `nexus.ai.cmdI.open` (keybinding `ctrl+i` / `cmd+i`) and `nexus.ai.cmdI.close` (Esc, gated on the `nexus.ai.cmdI.visible` context-key); the overlay mounts in the `overlay` slot via `views.registerPanel(VIEW_ID_CMD_I_OVERLAY, …)`. `setCmdIApi(api)` hands the kernel handle to the runtime so submit can call `api.kernel.invoke(...)` without a DI dance. `useCmdIStore.subscribe(...)` flips the context-key when `visible` changes so the Esc keybinding only competes for the chord while the overlay is up.

Coverage: 4 new unit-test files. [`cmdIStore.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/cmdIStore.test.ts) (5 cases) covers open-clears, status transitions, tail-chunk rejection by request-id, error sticks until next submit, close wipes `currentRequestId`. [`cmdIRuntime.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/cmdIRuntime.test.ts) (8 cases) covers prompt assembly with multiple contributors, session-id isolation from the chat surface, kernel-failure → `setError`, abort propagation, and unified-handler dispatch. [`contextContributors.test.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/ai/contextContributors.test.ts) (7 cases) covers register/list ordering, idempotent disposers, throwing-contributor isolation, the per-chip vs coarse `assemblePrompt` modes, and removed-chip filtering. [`shell/tests/cmd-i-overlay.test.ts`](../../shell/tests/cmd-i-overlay.test.ts) re-exports the trio so the workspace `tests/*.test.ts` glob picks them up. **Out of scope** per the BL entry (deferred to follow-ons): citations (BL-038 — ✅ shipped 2026-04-29), right-click actions (BL-035 — ✅ shipped 2026-04-29), context chip click-to-remove + model switcher (BL-033 — ✅ shipped 2026-04-28), additional surface adapters for bases / canvas / terminal (each lands with its plugin without touching the overlay surface itself). No Rust changes — `stream_chat` is already exposed by `crates/nexus-ai`; `scripts/check_ipc_drift.sh` is a no-op.

### BL-016: AI tool registration for LLM function-calling ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Source**: PRD-12 §8.1 (`ToolRegistry`, `ToolExecutor`, built-in `read_file` / `write_file` / etc.).
**Effort**: Medium. **Crate**: `nexus-ai`.
**Delivered:** Phase-1 keystone landed in three sequenced commits; downstream tracks (BL-010, BL-011, BL-027, BL-035, BL-036, BL-044) gain native function-calling on Anthropic, OpenAI, and Ollama through one shared registry rather than per-provider scaffolding.

- **Sub-task 1 — `ToolRegistry` + `ToolExecutor` core** _(commit `de4eb81`)_: new module [`crates/nexus-ai/src/tools/`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/tools/) with three files. [`registry.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/tools/registry.rs) defines `ToolSchema { name, description, input_schema: serde_json::Value }` (JSON-Schema-shaped tool description), `ToolError` (`NotFound(name)` / `ExecutionFailed(msg)` / `InvalidInput(msg)`), the `#[async_trait] ToolExecutor` trait with `execute(&self, input: Value) -> Result<String, ToolError>`, `RegisteredTool { schema, executor: Arc<dyn ToolExecutor> }` (cheap-clone via Arc-shared executor), and `ToolRegistry` with `new` / `register` (overwrites by name) / `schemas` / `len` / `is_empty` / `contains` / async `execute(name, input)`. The schema is not enforced inside the registry — providers paste the raw `Value` the model produced and the executor does its own validation. [`functions.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/tools/functions.rs) ships `ReadFileTool` / `WriteFileTool` as thin wrappers over `com.nexus.storage::read_file` / `write_file`, dispatched through `KernelPluginContext::ipc_call` per CLAUDE.md invariants 2 + 3 (no direct dep on `nexus-storage`). `register_storage_builtins(&mut registry, ctx)` is the convenience seam sub-task 2's dispatch loop calls. 13 unit tests cover registry mechanics (register / overwrite / schemas / execute round-trip / `NotFound` / executor-error propagation / clone / serde) and built-in schema shape; the `dep_invariants` test still passes (no new direct dependencies into forbidden subsystems).

- **Sub-task 2 — Anthropic + OpenAI tool wire format** _(commit `91e9c0f`)_: provider trait gains `chat_turn_with_tools` plus cross-provider `ChatTurn` / `ToolCall` / `ChatTurnOutput` types in [`provider.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/provider.rs); the default impl falls back to plain text streaming so Ollama (sub-task 3) keeps compiling untouched. [`anthropic.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/anthropic.rs) serializes `tools[]` and switches to the block-array message form, parses interleaved `text` / `tool_use` content blocks, batches consecutive tool-result turns into a single user message, and tolerates unknown block types for forward-compat. [`openai.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/openai.rs) wraps tools in `{type:"function", function:{...}}` envelopes, encodes `tool_calls[].function.arguments` as a JSON string (and decodes the same field back into a `Value` on response), and prefixes tool errors with `[error]` since OpenAI lacks an `is_error` flag. `AiCorePlugin` now owns an `Arc<ToolRegistry>` populated in `wire_context` via `register_storage_builtins`, so every frontend reaches `read_file` / `write_file` through the same IPC path. The dispatch loop in [`core_plugin.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/core_plugin.rs) caps at 8 rounds to bound runaway tool-use chains. Tests grew 44 → 70 covering Anthropic + OpenAI serialization, response parsing including the `arguments`-string quirk and unknown-block tolerance, and a scripted-provider end-to-end exercising the dispatch loop, error mapping, and round cap.

- **Sub-task 3 — Ollama tool-call wire format** _(commit `57d43a6`)_: replaces the default `chat_turn_with_tools` fallback for `OllamaProvider` in [`ollama.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/ollama.rs) with a native streaming tool-call implementation, so an Ollama-backed forge gets the same dispatch-loop semantics as Anthropic and OpenAI. Wire format matches Ollama's `/api/chat` tool spec — request `tools[]` uses the OpenAI-style `{type:"function", function:{...}}` envelope; assistant turns serialize `tool_calls[]` with `function.arguments` as a JSON **object** (the key wire-level distinction from OpenAI, which encodes arguments as a JSON-encoded string); tool-result turns map to `role: "tool"` messages with `tool_call_id` set; failures get an `[error] ...` prefix mirroring the OpenAI adapter; system prompts go as a synthetic `role: "system"` message because Ollama has no top-level system field. The streaming reader parses NDJSON chunks with optional `message.tool_calls`, synthesizes a stable `ollama_call_<n>` id when the model omits one (most builds do; preserves a real id when supplied), and flushes any trailing buffered line at EOF so a server that closes mid-line doesn't drop the last record. Tests grew 70 → 86: `tool_format_tests` cover schema serialization, turn → message translation, error prefixing, the arguments-as-object quirk, and request-body shaping; `streaming_dispatch_tests` drive a hand-rolled HTTP server through the real `chat_turn_with_tools` to cover id synthesis, multi-chunk text aggregation, and HTTP error propagation.

`cargo test -p nexus-ai` 86 passing across all three splits; `cargo test -p nexus-bootstrap --test dep_invariants` clean; `cargo build --workspace` clean. The Phase-2 `stream_chat` engine consumes this surface via the `tools: "auto" | "none"` arg toggle (BL-010 / BL-011 / BL-034 ship that path).

### Phase 2 — shared chat/complete engine for BL-010 / BL-011 / BL-034 ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** The Phase-2 lock-in BACKLOG.md called out (a single engine in `nexus-ai` driving the chat REPL, ghost completion, and headless complete CLI) is now in place. [`com.nexus.ai::stream_chat`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/core_plugin.rs) (handler id 6, unchanged per ADR-0005) gained five optional fields on its arg envelope: `mode: "chat" | "complete"` (default `chat`, preserving back-compat), `tools: "auto" | "none"` (default `auto`; `none` hides the registry from the model), `max_tokens`, `stop` (post-process truncation), and `trim` (post-process: prompt-echo strip + natural-break clip). When `mode = complete`, the dispatcher physically bypasses `run_tool_dispatch_loop` and routes through a new `run_complete(...)` path that calls `chat_stream_with` directly with an empty `&[ToolSchema]` so single-turn completions can never trigger tool-calling. New private `EngineEnvelope` helper wraps the bus contract (`build_ai_provider` + `stream_start` + per-chunk `stream_chunk` events + `stream_done`) so both modes publish byte-identical wire events. New typed `AiStreamChatArgs` / `AiStreamChatMode` / `AiToolPolicy` in [`nexus-ai/src/ipc.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/ipc.rs) emit TS + JSON Schema bindings via the existing pilot harness. Coverage: `cargo test -p nexus-ai` 94 passing; new tests cover `complete_mode_skips_tool_loop`, `complete_mode_strips_prompt_echo`, `complete_mode_trims_to_natural_break`, `apply_stop_truncates`, `chat_mode_unchanged` regression, plus 4 round-trip serde tests for the new arg shape. No new dependencies; `stop` is implemented as post-processing rather than a wire-level provider extension. `handle_stream_ask` (RAG path) intentionally untouched. Phase-2 surfaces (BL-010 `nexus ai chat`, BL-011 `nexus ai complete`, BL-034 ghost completion) consume this engine in follow-up commits. Shipped commit `b586ac3`.
### F-8.1.2: Boundary-bound `pluginId` for sandboxed plugins ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** Closes the second F-8.1.x red-tier item by deriving the authoritative `pluginId` from the iframe boundary instead of trusting any string the plugin (or host wiring) self-asserts. Pre-fix, [`shell/src/main.tsx`](../../shell/src/main.tsx) built one `PluginAPI` instance with `pluginId: 'community-sandbox'` and shared it across every sandboxed plugin via `SandboxOrchestratorOptions.api`. The accompanying comment claimed "each router actually enforces its own pluginId when it dispatches API calls" — but [`shell/src/host/sandbox/router.ts`](../../shell/src/host/sandbox/router.ts) `dispatchMethod` only used `this.pluginId` for error envelopes; every `this.api.storage.set(...)` / `this.api.events.emit(...)` / `this.api.activityBar.addItem(...)` call ran against the shared instance, so storage namespacing (`plugin:community-sandbox:<key>`), `eventBus.emit('activityBar:itemAdded', { ...config, pluginId: 'community-sandbox' })` tagging at [`PluginAPI.ts:422`](../../shell/src/host/PluginAPI.ts), and `PluginRegistry.track('community-sandbox', …)` ownership all collapsed concurrent sandboxed plugins into one bucket — with a corresponding cross-plugin storage leak / impersonation surface. **The fix has three pieces.** First, [`SandboxOrchestrator`](../../shell/src/host/sandbox/SandboxOrchestrator.ts) now takes `apiFactory: (pluginId: string) => PluginAPI` instead of a single shared `api: PluginAPI`. `SandboxInstanceImpl.start()` calls the factory with the orchestrator-set `pluginId` (the same id the spec passed at `orchestrator.load(spec)` time, which is always the `manifest.id` from the plugin's `plugin.json`), so every router gets its own `PluginAPI` whose `localStorage` keys, event payloads, and registry-track entries derive from the boundary id. Second, [`shell/src/main.tsx`](../../shell/src/main.tsx)'s sandbox wiring drops the false-claim comment and plugs in the factory: `apiFactory: (sandboxedPluginId) => buildPluginAPI(reg, { pluginId: sandboxedPluginId, isCore: false })`. The literal `'community-sandbox'` label is gone; nothing in the codebase still bakes that string into a real `PluginAPI`. Third, new helper [`assertValidPluginId`](../../shell/src/host/PluginAPI.ts) is the choke point — `buildPluginAPI` calls it on every construction. Empty strings, non-string inputs, and colon-bearing ids all throw before any side-effecting key is computed. The `:` ban closes the namespace-escape vector: a plugin built with `pluginId: "evil:hijack"` would otherwise share the `plugin:evil:` `localStorage` prefix with the legitimate `evil` plugin; rejecting `:` keeps each plugin pinned to its own sub-tree. Real plugin ids in this codebase are dotted (`com.nexus.editor`, `community.hello-world`) and never contain colons, so the constraint is non-breaking for shipped plugins. **Test coverage**: 9 new tests across two files. [`shell/src/host/PluginAPI.test.ts`](../../shell/src/host/PluginAPI.test.ts) (new — 7 tests) locks `assertValidPluginId` behaviour for empty / non-string / colon-bearing / valid dotted ids, asserts `buildPluginAPI` rejects the same shapes, and exercises end-to-end `localStorage` isolation between two `PluginAPI` instances built with `'plugin.a'` vs `'plugin.b'` (both writing the same logical key `'shared-key'` see distinct values; `apiA.storage.clear()` does not wipe `apiB`'s namespace). [`shell/src/host/sandbox/sandboxE2E.test.ts`](../../shell/src/host/sandbox/sandboxE2E.test.ts) gains 2 tests under a new `F-8.1.2 — pluginId binding at the sandbox boundary` section: `apiFactory` is called once per `orchestrator.load(spec)` with the spec's `pluginId` (verified via captured-call array `['plugin.a', 'plugin.b']`), and two distinct routers receive distinct `PluginAPI` instances (`assert.notEqual(apiA, apiB)`). The existing test harnesses in `orchestrator.test.ts` and `sandboxE2E.test.ts` were updated from `api: makeApi()` to `apiFactory: () => makeApi()` with no behavioural change — the per-test `makeApi` helpers stay; tests get one factory wrapper instead of a direct API. Mechanical change, not semantic. **Coverage:** `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 415/416 (was 406/407; +9 net new), `pnpm --filter nexus-shell typecheck` clean, `pnpm --filter nexus-shell lint` clean (sandbox / PluginAPI surfaces have zero new warnings), `pnpm --filter nexus-shell build` succeeds. **Out of scope per the F-8.1.2 plan:** legacy non-sandboxed plugins still receive a `PluginAPI` built with their `manifest.id` (the existing path through `ExtensionHost`); plugins themselves never call `buildPluginAPI` directly, so the self-assertion vector for legacy plugins is purely theoretical. The validation gate in `assertValidPluginId` is the single ingress check that catches both surfaces uniformly. With F-8.1.1 + F-8.1.1-fo1 + F-8.1.2 closed, the iframe-sandbox red-tier items from `docs/archive/planning/UI-AUDIT.md` are fully resolved.

### F-8.1.1-fo1: Precompiled sandbox runtime bundle ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** Closes the F-8.1.1 follow-on by shipping a real `bootstrapSandboxedPlugin` runtime to every sandboxed-iframe load. New [`shell/vite.sandbox-runtime-plugin.ts`](../../shell/vite.sandbox-runtime-plugin.ts) — a Vite plugin whose `bundleSandboxRuntime()` helper runs esbuild against [`packages/nexus-extension-api/src/sandbox/runtime.ts`](../../packages/nexus-extension-api/src/sandbox/runtime.ts) (`bundle: true`, `format: 'esm'`, `target: 'es2021'`, `platform: 'browser'`, `legalComments: 'none'`) so `protocol.ts` and the rest of the runtime's runtime-imports are inlined into one self-contained ESM string. The plugin exposes that string as the virtual module `virtual:sandbox-runtime`; [`shell/src/main.tsx`](../../shell/src/main.tsx)'s `getRuntimeUrl` imports the source, blob-wraps it once on first sandbox load, and caches the URL — every sandboxed plugin reuses the same blob. The previous no-op shim is gone; type declaration at [`shell/src/types/sandboxRuntime.d.ts`](../../shell/src/types/sandboxRuntime.d.ts) keeps `tsc` and ESLint happy. `esbuild ^0.21.5` is now a direct devDependency of the shell (was already in the pnpm store via Vite — pinned the major). Hello-world migrated: [`shell/src/plugins/community/hello-world/index.js`](../../shell/src/plugins/community/hello-world/index.js) drops the ~270-line hand-rolled handshake / dispatch / postMessage scaffolding in favour of a 60-line plain `export default { activate(ctx) { … } }`. The orchestrator's srcdoc reads `bundle.default` and passes it to `runtime.bootstrapSandboxedPlugin(plugin)` — no more inline `bootstrapSandboxedPlugin(plugin)` side-effect call inside the plugin (which would have double-fired the handshake now that the runtime is live). [`shell/src/plugins/community/hello-world/index.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/community/hello-world/index.ts), the spec for the future per-plugin bundler output, mirrors the new shape. Coverage: 7 new unit tests in [`shell/tests/sandbox-runtime-bundle.test.ts`](../../shell/tests/sandbox-runtime-bundle.test.ts) lock the bundle invariants `getRuntimeUrl` relies on — non-empty output, named-export `bootstrapSandboxedPlugin`, no bare-specifier imports (would fail to resolve in the null-origin iframe), `protocol.ts` inlined (`SANDBOX_PROTOCOL_VERSION` present), `window.parent.postMessage` survived DCE, and deterministic re-build. `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 406/407 (+7), `pnpm --filter nexus-shell typecheck` clean, `pnpm --filter nexus-shell build` succeeds and the production `index-*.js` chunk inlines `bootstrapSandboxedPlugin` + `SANDBOX_PROTOCOL_VERSION` (verified via grep). Out of scope per the F-8.1.1-fo1 plan: a per-plugin author-side bundler that emits the same shape from TS source (the `index.ts` spec). That plugin-side toolchain is a separate slice and is not gated on this work — community-plugin authors can hand-write the `export default` shape today, exactly as the migrated hello-world bundle now does.

### F-8.1.1: Iframe-sandbox script-plugin runtime — sub-tasks 1–5 ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** UI F-8.1.1 closes via the existing in-tree implementation, verified end-to-end against the BACKLOG split. **Sub-task 1 — iframe scaffold + sandbox flags** lives in [`shell/src/host/sandbox/SandboxOrchestrator.ts`](../../shell/src/host/sandbox/SandboxOrchestrator.ts): `SandboxInstanceImpl` constructs an `<iframe>` with `sandbox="allow-scripts"` (null origin via the deliberate omission of `allow-same-origin`), styles it off-screen at `1×1`, and assigns a srcdoc that loads the guest. `buildSandboxSrcDoc()` emits a minimal HTML document whose only script is a top-level `await import(runtime); await import(bundle); runtime.bootstrapSandboxedPlugin(plugin)` chain — `JSON.stringify`-quoted URLs to defang blob/data percent-encoding, with a try/catch that posts a `handshake`-shaped `dispatch_failed` frame to `window.parent` so the orchestrator fails the load promptly instead of waiting out the 5 s handshake timeout. **Sub-task 2 — postMessage protocol** lives in [`packages/nexus-extension-api/src/sandbox/protocol.ts`](../../packages/nexus-extension-api/src/sandbox/protocol.ts) and the host counterpart [`shell/src/host/sandbox/router.ts`](../../shell/src/host/sandbox/router.ts) + [`shell/src/host/sandbox/IframePort.ts`](../../shell/src/host/sandbox/IframePort.ts): a single `RpcEnvelope` shape (`id` / `direction` / `kind` ∈ `handshake|request|response|event|dispose` / `method` / `payload` / `error`), `SANDBOX_PROTOCOL_VERSION = 1`, version-locked handshake (rejects mismatched versions with `protocol_mismatch`), per-method timeout, capability-precheck via [`shell/src/host/sandbox/capabilityGuard.ts`](../../shell/src/host/sandbox/capabilityGuard.ts) (`METHOD_CAPABILITY_MAP` exhaustive over the 39-method `SandboxMethodCatalog`), subscription lifecycle that rejects in-flight requests on dispose, and host→guest dispatch for `dispatch.command` / `dispatch.uri` / `views.render` so the shell command palette and view registry can round-trip into the sandbox. `IframePort` filters `MessageEvent`s by `event.source === iframe.contentWindow` to satisfy the host-side identity guard (design §3 threat 7) without trusting `event.origin` (which is `"null"` for sandboxed iframes). **Sub-task 3 — `NexusPluginContext` proxy** lives in [`packages/nexus-extension-api/src/sandbox/runtime.ts`](../../packages/nexus-extension-api/src/sandbox/runtime.ts) (`bootstrapSandboxedPlugin(plugin)`) and [`packages/nexus-extension-api/src/sandbox/context.ts`](../../packages/nexus-extension-api/src/sandbox/context.ts) (`SandboxedPluginContext` shape): every method on `commands` / `kernel` / `platform.{fs,dialog,window,shell}` / `events` / `storage` / `notifications` / `context` / `views.registerPanel` / `input` / `uri` / `activityBar` / `statusBar` marshals into a `request` envelope and awaits a correlated `response`; subscriptions hand back `Disposable`s that send a `dispose` frame on call. Because closures don't survive structured-clone, the proxy mints UUID `handlerSub` / `renderSub` ids and keeps the live function in a guest-side map — the host echoes the id on every dispatch and the guest looks it up locally. **Sub-task 4 — per-plugin manifest flag** lives in [`shell/src/host/communityPluginLoader.ts`](../../shell/src/host/communityPluginLoader.ts): `CommunityPluginManifest.sandboxed?: boolean` (line 61); the loader's routing decision at line 302 forwards `sandboxed === true` manifests to `SandboxOrchestrator.load(...)` and leaves anything else on the legacy `URL.createObjectURL` + `import()` path. The BACKLOG split spec'd this as a `manifest.toml` `sandbox: "iframe" | "legacy"` enum, but JS plugins on this side of the boundary use `plugin.json` (Rust-side WASM plugins use `manifest.toml`); the boolean carries the same semantic content (`true` = iframe, `false`/absent = legacy) and the field name `sandboxed` matches the manifest convention used by every other community plugin. Examples: [`shell/src/plugins/community/hello-world/plugin.json`](../../shell/src/plugins/community/hello-world/plugin.json) opts in (`"sandboxed": true`); [`shell/src/plugins/community/mermaid/plugin.json`](../../shell/src/plugins/community/mermaid/plugin.json) explicitly opts out (`"sandboxed": false`). The per-plugin migration posture decided 2026-04-28 holds: legacy + sandboxed plugins coexist during the runtime-bundler build window. **Sub-task 5 — CSP + tests**: host-level CSP in [`shell/src-tauri/tauri.conf.json`](../../shell/src-tauri/tauri.conf.json) ships `frame-src 'self' blob:` (so the orchestrator can mount blob srcdocs) and is otherwise strict — `default-src 'self'`, `script-src 'self'` (no `unsafe-eval` in production), `object-src 'none'`. Iframe-level CSP inside the srcdoc is `default-src 'none'; script-src 'self' blob: data: 'unsafe-inline'` — `'self'` for the inline boot script, `blob:` for the runtime + plugin bundle URLs, `'unsafe-inline'` only effective for the srcdoc's own pre-CSP module script (not for any dynamically injected script tag). 2,255 lines of tests across [`shell/src/host/sandbox/orchestrator.test.ts`](../../shell/src/host/sandbox/orchestrator.test.ts) (mount + handshake + watchdog + srcdoc safety + PanelNode renderer), [`shell/src/host/sandbox/sandboxProtocol.test.ts`](../../shell/src/host/sandbox/sandboxProtocol.test.ts) (every `RpcKind`, capability denial, timeout, dispose-mid-flight, catalog parity assertion), [`shell/src/host/sandbox/sandboxE2E.test.ts`](../../shell/src/host/sandbox/sandboxE2E.test.ts) (concurrent-plugin isolation, real crash recovery, sub-50 ms round-trip, slow-handler backpressure, lifecycle + duplicate-load rejection). The CSP layer itself is verified at the unit level (`buildSandboxSrcDoc embeds runtime + bundle URLs and CSP`); browser-level enforcement is a manual smoke step listed in the E2E test header. Out of scope per the BL split: shipping a precompiled `bootstrapSandboxedPlugin` runtime asset so plugins stop hand-rolling the protocol — `getRuntimeUrl` in [`shell/src/main.tsx:248-256`](../../shell/src/main.tsx) returns a no-op shim today and `hello-world/index.js` ships the protocol inline; tracked as **F-8.1.1-fo1** in [BACKLOG.md](BACKLOG.md). The proxy + protocol + iframe boundary themselves are production-ready and exercised by every test in the suite. F-8.1.2 (boundary-bound `pluginId`) is now unblocked — the `pluginId` field on `SandboxRouter` is set by the orchestrator at handshake time and is no longer self-asserted by the plugin. Coverage: `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test` 399 passing / 1 skipped; `pnpm --filter nexus-shell typecheck` clean; `pnpm --filter nexus-shell lint` clean (sandbox/ directory has zero warnings — pre-existing repo-wide warnings are unrelated).

### BL-013: Terminal event subscription over plugin IPC ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** PRD-09 §11.2's `subscribe_events` story now reaches the kernel bus. `TerminalCorePlugin::with_event_bus` (the same builder bootstrap already calls in `crates/nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs:875`) now also subscribes to the in-memory server's `TerminalEvent` mpsc and spawns a `nexus-terminal-lifecycle` forwarder thread that republishes every event onto the kernel bus as `com.nexus.terminal.events.<session_id>` (new `EVENT_LIFECYCLE_PREFIX` constant, exported from `nexus_terminal`). The payload is the `TerminalEvent` itself — `serde(tag = "kind")` keeps `session_created` / `output_received` / `pattern_matched` / `session_closed` distinguishable, so a single `EventFilter::CustomPrefix("com.nexus.terminal.events.")` subscription gives plugins everything they need to react to lifecycle and per-line output without re-implementing pump loops; an `EventFilter::CustomExact` subscription against a specific `<session_id>` topic is also viable for remote-terminal style consumers. The byte-stream topic added in WI-12 (`com.nexus.terminal.output.<session_id>`) stays the right channel for xterm-style frontends; the lifecycle topic complements it. The forwarder owns the receiver end only — it never holds the server lock — so it adds zero contention to dispatch. Drop ordering is correct: `LifecycleForwarderHandle::drop` flips a stop flag and joins (worst-case ~one `LIFECYCLE_RECV_TIMEOUT_MS = 100ms` tick); the thread also exits naturally when the server's senders go away, so a forwarder outliving its server still terminates. New `TerminalEvent::session_id()` helper extracts the id from any variant for topic-suffix derivation. Five new unit tests (`crates/nexus-terminal/src/core_plugin.rs`) verify each variant lands on the bus end-to-end (`SessionCreated`, `OutputReceived`, `PatternMatched`, `SessionClosed`, plus a topic-suffix invariant). Coverage: `cargo test -p nexus-terminal`: 253 passing (+5 new); `cargo clippy -p nexus-terminal --all-targets -- -D warnings`: clean; `cargo check --workspace`: clean. Out of scope per the BL-013 backlog note: a generic plugin-host stream convention — the `Custom` event with a per-session prefix already gave us the ergonomics the backlog called out, and codifying a wider streaming trait is a separate cross-cutting effort the backlog can pick up when a second streaming consumer (file watcher, MCP notifications) appears.

### BL-015: Soft-deleted bases — trash view UI ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** PRD-10's soft-delete trash UX was already most of the way there — the audit trail showed `BaseRecord.deletedAt` wired end-to-end (table actions, kernel filter at `BasesView.tsx`, IPC handlers `base_record_soft_delete` / `base_record_restore`) and a Trash filter toggle in the header (`BasesView.tsx:145-164`) that swaps the live record set for the soft-deleted set, plus toolbar actions in `BasesTable.tsx:408-427` for **Restore** and **Delete forever** that only render when `trashOpen && selectedRecordId`. The default Backspace path goes through `handleSoftDeleteRow` (lands records in the trash, restorable); hard-delete is gated behind the trash view so a reflexive Backspace can't permanently destroy data. Both directions are integrated with the bases undo stack (`pushHistory` with paired forward/inverse) so soft-delete and restore round-trip via Cmd-Z. The remaining gap closed in this pass: an empty-state for the trash. Previously, switching into trash mode with zero soft-deleted records dropped through to whichever view was active (table / calendar / timeline / etc), which renders awkwardly on the non-table views (empty months, empty lanes). New `TrashEmptyState` component in `BasesView.tsx` short-circuits before any of the per-mode views mount when `trashOpen && trashCount === 0`, showing a plain "The trash is empty." message and a "Back to live records" button that flips `setTrashOpen(relpath, false)`. Out of scope for v1: bulk "Empty trash" action (one-shot delete-all-forever) — sensible follow-up but not on the BL-015 critical path. Coverage: pre-existing tests for soft-delete/restore IPC and undo stack continue to pass; no new unit tests since the empty-state is a pure-DOM short-circuit with no IPC. Total `pnpm --filter nexus-shell test`: 370 passing (1 pre-existing skip), `pnpm --filter nexus-shell typecheck`: clean.

### BL-009: Whole-File `.mermaid` Viewer ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** `shell/src/plugins/community/mermaid/` extends BL-008's fenced renderer with a whole-file viewer for `.mermaid` files. The plugin's `activate()` now registers a `mermaid` view-type via `viewRegistry.register(VIEW_TYPE, creator)` and claims the `.mermaid` extension via `viewRegistry.registerExtensions(['mermaid'], 'mermaid')` (same pattern as `nexus.canvas`'s `.canvas` claim). New `MermaidPaneView` extends `ViewBase`: on `onOpen` it reads the file via `kernel.invoke('com.nexus.storage', 'read_file', { path })` (decoded via `TextDecoder('utf-8')`), caches the source so toggling modes is instant, and renders the SVG via the existing `renderMermaid()` helper that BL-008 already used.
