A "View Source" / "Render" toolbar button in the top-right toggles between the rendered SVG and a `<pre>` view of the raw source (caching means no re-IPC on toggle). Errors during read or render fall back to the same `buildErrorBox` BL-008 ships. Stylesheet additions in `mermaid.css` cover the pane chrome (`.nexus-mermaid-pane`, `.nexus-mermaid-toolbar`, `.nexus-mermaid-source`, `.nexus-mermaid-placeholder`); existing `.nexus-mermaid-diagram` is reused so fenced and whole-file renders look identical. Disposal: `deactivate()` runs both the fenced-renderer and view-registry disposers; `onClose()` clears the container and drops the cached source. Plugin stays default-off (`DEFAULT_OFF_PLUGINS`); users opt in via Settings → Plugins. Edit-in-place is explicitly out of scope for v1 — the spec called this out, and "View Source" is the escape hatch. Coverage: pre-existing typecheck and lint pass; no new unit tests since the surface is purely the viewRegistry hook + a thin DOM wrapper around an already-tested render function. Out of scope per the BL-009 plan: no editor handoff (open in CodeMirror via the existing extension override flow), no zoom/pan controls (mermaid SVG inherits page zoom; canvas-style pan would be a separate plugin), no auto-reload on file change (next iteration; today the user closes/reopens). Plugin docs and `plugin.json` description unchanged — informational only since the loader path goes through the shell catalog.

### BL-024: MCP Reconnection + Connection Pool ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** PRD-14 §4.2.4 lands as a new [`crates/nexus-mcp/src/pool.rs`](../../crates/nexus-mcp/src/pool.rs) module that replaces the ad-hoc `Arc<RwLock<HashMap<String, Arc<Mutex<McpClient>>>>>` field on `McpHostPlugin`. `PoolConfig::default()` ships the spec values: `max_per_server = 10` (BACKLOG override of PRD-14 §4.2.4's 5 — flagged in commit body since the discrepancy was deliberate), `idle_timeout = 300s`, `connect_timeout = 30s`, and `backoff = [100ms, 500ms, 2s, 10s, 30s]` matching PRD-14 §11.1 verbatim. `ConnectionPool::get_or_connect(server, host_cfg)` keeps lazy-connect semantics — entries are created on first access — but every call now runs `sweep_idle()` first, dropping any entry whose `last_used.elapsed() > idle_timeout`. Successful ops refresh `last_used` via the private `touch(server)` helper. Each entry carries a `tokio::sync::Semaphore::new(cfg.max_per_server)` so per-server in-flight calls are capped — advisory rate-limiting today since the inner `Mutex<McpClient>` already serializes, but load-bearing once a future refactor moves to `&McpClient` borrows. `McpClientError::is_transient()` returns `true` only for the `Service(_)` variant; `Spawn` (binary missing) and `Handshake` (initialize timeout / protocol error) are non-transient because retrying just delays surfacing misconfiguration. `call_with_reconnect(server, host_cfg, op)` is the retry surface: it iterates `1 + backoff.len()` total attempts, force-reconnects between attempts on transient connect / op failures, sleeps the appropriate backoff, and bails immediately on any non-transient error. The 4 dispatch-site handlers in `core_plugin.rs` (`list_tools`, `call_tool`, `list_resources`, `list_prompts`) call `pool.get_or_connect` today; threading the inner ops through `call_with_reconnect` is a follow-up so the closure-`Fn` capture rewrite of `tool` / `tool_args` can be reviewed independently. `on_stop` calls `pool.shutdown_all().await` instead of the old `clients.write().await.clear()` — same semantics (entries dropped, `McpClient::Drop` runs graceful close), tighter encapsulation. Testability is via a private `Connectable` trait with two impls: production wires `RealConnector` (which calls `McpClient::connect`); tests wire a `FakeConnector` that pops outcomes from a queue and increments an attempt counter. Combined with `#[tokio::test(flavor = "current_thread", start_paused = true)]` + `tokio::time::advance(...)` this exercises the full retry loop in deterministic constant time without spawning child processes — the previously feature-gated `tokio` `test-util` is now a `dev-dependencies` feature on the crate (no new external dep — `tokio` was already there). Coverage: 9 new unit tests in `pool.rs` — `backoff_schedule_matches_spec` (locks the [100ms..30s] array), `pool_config_defaults` (locks the four numeric defaults), `call_with_reconnect_gives_up_after_full_schedule` (6 transient errors → returns last error, `attempts == 6`), `call_with_reconnect_does_not_retry_non_transient` (one Handshake → 1 attempt), `call_with_reconnect_stops_at_non_transient_op_error` (in-budget retry counter ≤ 6), `idle_sweep_on_empty_pool_evicts_nothing` (boundary case after time-advance past the idle window), `disconnect_returns_false_for_unknown_server`, `shutdown_all_clears_empty_pool`, and `is_transient_only_for_service_variant` (variant table guard). Total `cargo test -p nexus-mcp`: 30 passing (was 21). Out of scope per the BL-024 plan: no background sweep task (lazy eviction only), no transport changes (rmcp untouched), no IPC contract drift (handler ids 1–7 and arg shapes stay), no auth flow (BL-025), no in-handler `call_with_reconnect` wiring (deferred so the call-site closure rewrite can be a focused follow-up).

### BL-017: AI PII / Secret Egress Filter ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** PRD-12 §15.1 lands as a small library-only addition to `nexus-ai`. New [`crates/nexus-ai/src/privacy.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/privacy.rs) defines `PrivacyPolicy` (`Off` default, `Redact`, `Strict` — `#[derive(Default, Serialize, Deserialize)]`, `#[serde(rename_all = "lowercase")]`), `Redaction { pattern_id: &'static str, start: usize, end: usize }` records (byte offsets into the *original* input — useful for diagnostics), and a `Redactor` that compiles a default set of six high-confidence secret patterns under `regex-lite` 0.1 (already a workspace dep — no new external crate; the full-fat `regex` was deliberately avoided). Pattern set: `aws-access-key` (`AKIA[0-9A-Z]{16}` → `[REDACTED:aws-access-key]`), `aws-secret` (`(?i)aws(.{0,20})?(secret|access)?(.{0,20})?[=:\s]+[A-Za-z0-9/+=]{40}` → `[REDACTED:aws-secret]` — verified `regex-lite` accepts the leading `(?i)` flag and `[\s\S]` character class on its own; no syntax adjustments were required), `api-token` (`sk_(live|test)_[A-Za-z0-9]{24,}` → `[REDACTED:api-token]` for Stripe-style keys), `github-pat-classic` (`ghp_[A-Za-z0-9]{36}` → `[REDACTED:github-token]`), `github-pat-fine` (`github_pat_[A-Za-z0-9_]{82}` → `[REDACTED:github-token]`), and `private-key` (PEM `-----BEGIN [A-Z ]*PRIVATE KEY-----[\s\S]*?-----END [A-Z ]*PRIVATE KEY-----` → `[REDACTED:private-key]`). API surface: `Redactor::with_default_patterns()` / `with_strict()` / `for_policy(PrivacyPolicy) -> Option<Self>` (returns `None` for `Off` — the convention callers thread through the prompt builder), `redact(&self, &str) -> (String, Vec<Redaction>)` and the in-place variant `redact_in_place(&self, &mut String) -> Vec<Redaction>`, plus `is_strict()` returning the configured intent so a future error-on-match wiring can branch without an enum-shape break. Wire point is intentionally narrow: [`build_rag_prompt_budgeted`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/rag.rs) gained a fourth `redactor: Option<&Redactor>` parameter that runs each accepted chunk's text through `redact_in_place` before it's charged against the token budget and stitched into the prompt body. `stream_chat`, the Anthropic / OpenAI / Ollama provider HTTP request bodies, and the `AiCorePlugin` dispatcher are deliberately untouched — RAG injects retrieved content the user didn't paste this turn, which is the right boundary; silently mutating the user's typed prompt would be surprising and the user already chose to send what they pasted. The legacy `build_rag_prompt(sources)` wrapper threads `None` through so its byte-output stays identical to the BL-018 contract (verified by `budgeted_prompt_passes_through_when_redactor_is_none`). `AiConfig` gained `pub privacy: PrivacyPolicy` defaulting to `Off` — opt in by setting it to `Redact` (or `Strict`) and constructing a `Redactor` via `Redactor::for_policy(...)`. `PrivacyPolicy::Strict` is shipped today as a no-op alias of `Redact`: it constructs the same redactor and replaces the same matches with the same placeholders, but `Redactor::is_strict()` returns `true` so when a downstream caller wants the error-on-match path (e.g. refusing to send the prompt at all when a secret is detected), the wiring is a one-line check on the redactor without re-plumbing the config enum. Coverage: 7 new unit tests in `privacy.rs` (`redactor_replaces_aws_access_key`, `redactor_replaces_private_key_block_multiline`, `redactor_replaces_multiple_distinct_secrets_in_one_pass` covering Stripe key + GitHub PAT in one input, `redactor_no_match_returns_input_unchanged` proving clean text round-trips with an empty event vec, `for_policy_returns_none_for_off`, `is_strict_reflects_constructor`, `privacy_policy_default_is_off`) plus 2 new tests in `rag.rs::tests` (`budgeted_prompt_redacts_chunk_text_when_redactor_supplied`, `budgeted_prompt_passes_through_when_redactor_is_none` — the BL-018 byte-identity guard). Total `cargo test -p nexus-ai`: 31 passing (was 22). Out of scope per the BL-017 plan: no IPC handler (the existing `AiCorePlugin` dispatcher is untouched), no `nexus-security` integration, no error path on `Strict`, no plumbing through `stream_ask` — those ship when a downstream caller needs them.

### BL-026: MCP Resource Enumeration ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** PRD-14 §7 lands as a focused server-side addition to [`crates/nexus-mcp/src/server.rs`](../../crates/nexus-mcp/src/server.rs). `NexusMcpServer`'s `ServerHandler` impl now overrides `list_resources` and `read_resource` in addition to the existing `get_info` / `call_tool` / `list_tools`; the capability advertisement in `get_info` gains `.enable_resources()` so MCP clients negotiate the resource surface during initialize. Notes are exposed under the URI scheme `mcp://nexus/notes/<vault-relative-path>` (the listing root `mcp://nexus/notes` is non-readable). `list_resources` reuses `com.nexus.storage::query_files` (handler id 1) — same IPC path the existing `nexus_list_notes` tool uses — and maps each `{ path, size_bytes }` record to a `RawResource` with `mime_type = "text/markdown"`, description `"Markdown note in the Nexus forge"`, name set to the file basename, and size clamped to `u32::MAX` via `u32::try_from(...).unwrap_or(u32::MAX)` (no silent `as u32` truncation). `read_resource` dispatches `parse_note_uri(&request.uri)` first — non-`mcp://nexus/notes/` URIs and the bare notes-root URI return `ErrorData::resource_not_found` — then routes the relative path through `com.nexus.storage::read_file` (id 2), decodes the byte array via `String::from_utf8_lossy`, and returns a single `ResourceContents::TextResourceContents { uri, mime_type: "text/markdown", text }`. No new external dependencies; no IPC contract drift; no `nexus-storage` linkage (the existing `storage_call` helper handles the IPC dispatch). The host plugin (`com.nexus.mcp.host`) and `com.nexus.storage` handlers are untouched — BL-026 is server-side only. `mcp://nexus/db/...` is intentionally deferred per the PRD-14 §7.3 note: that shape needs a `com.nexus.bases::list_columns`-equivalent handler that doesn't exist yet. Coverage: 3 new unit tests at the bottom of `server.rs` — `parse_note_uri_extracts_path` (valid path, missing prefix, notes-root URI), `build_note_resource_sets_uri_mime_and_size`, `build_note_resource_clamps_oversize_to_u32_max`. Total `cargo test -p nexus-mcp`: 21 passing (was 18).

### BL-014: nexus db CLI Subcommand Group ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** New [`crates/nexus-cli/src/commands/db.rs`](../../crates/nexus-cli/src/commands/db.rs) — three subcommands wrap existing `com.nexus.database` IPC handlers via the `ipc_call` boundary with a 30 s timeout, mirroring the `nexus skill` / `nexus mcp` posture so the CLI never links `nexus-database` directly (`nexus_bootstrap::database` typed helpers are explicitly avoided — using them would re-export `nexus-database` types and violate microkernel invariant #3 in `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` §7). Subcommands: `nexus db import-csv <FILE> --fields <a,b,c> [--has-header] [--column-mapping <JSON|@file>]` reads the CSV file, builds a `csv_import` (handler id 1) request, and prints `Imported N record(s).` plus a skipped count when non-zero; `nexus db export-csv [--records <JSON|@file>] [--fields <a,b,c>] [--output <FILE>]` builds a `csv_export` (id 2) request, decodes the `Vec<u8>` byte array out of the response, and writes raw CSV bytes to `--output` or stdout; `nexus db eval-formula <EXPR> --fields <JSON|@file>` builds a `formula_eval` (id 3) request and pretty-prints the response JSON via `serde_json::to_string_pretty`. The inline-or-`@file` convention (`@<path>` reads from disk; otherwise the literal string passes through) lets large argument bodies live on disk without needing shell quoting. Pure-function arg builders (`build_csv_import_args` / `build_csv_export_args` / `build_eval_formula_args`) are split out from the handlers so they're testable without a runtime. `apply_view` (handler id 4) is intentionally not surfaced — its arg shape requires a base file + schema context and is exercised by the shell renderer rather than being a useful CLI today. `list` / `show <base>` are deferred pending a `com.nexus.database::list_bases` handler that does not yet exist; both would be net-new database-engine work and were ruled out of scope for this BL. The lower-level IPC-only twin of `nexus bases`, which operates over the filesystem layer (`.bases` directories); both stay. Coverage: 11 new unit tests in `commands/db.rs::tests` — `csv_import_args_serialize_to_expected_shape`, `csv_import_args_with_column_mapping_round_trips`, `csv_import_args_bad_mapping_json_returns_err`, `csv_export_args_defaults_records_and_fields`, `csv_export_args_round_trips_records_and_fields`, `eval_formula_args_serialize_to_expected_shape`, `eval_formula_args_bad_json_returns_err`, `resolve_inline_or_file_handles_at_prefix`, `resolve_inline_or_file_returns_literal_when_no_prefix`, `extract_csv_bytes_decodes_byte_array`, `extract_csv_bytes_rejects_oversized_value`. No new external deps (`tempfile` was already a dev-dep; no clap_derive extras, no new tokio features).

### BL-020: Skill REGISTRY.json Persistence ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** New [`crates/nexus-skills/src/registry_index.rs`](../../crates/nexus-skills/src/registry_index.rs) module — `RegistryIndex` / `RegistryIndexEntry` / `RegistryIndexError` mirror the PRD-13 §3.1 on-disk shape (version `"1.0"`, hand-formatted RFC3339 `last_updated`, per-skill `id` / `name` / forward-slash root-relative `path` / `version` / `tags` / `applicable_contexts` / `author` / `visibility` defaulting to `"public"`). `write_index(path, root, &reg)` is atomic: serializes to a sibling `*.json.tmp`, then `rename`s over the destination; serde / IO failures leave the destination untouched and best-effort remove the tmp file. Forward-slash path normalization joins `path.strip_prefix(root)?.components()` with `/` so the index round-trips across Windows / macOS / Linux forges. RFC3339 timestamps are hand-formatted (no `chrono` / `time` dep added) via a Howard-Hinnant civil-from-days helper, with a matching inverse for the freshness check. New cold-start path: [`SkillRegistry::load_with_index`](../../crates/nexus-skills/src/registry.rs) prefers `<root>/REGISTRY.json` when fresh and falls back to the existing directory walk on miss / staleness — staleness = any listed path missing on disk OR any `.skill.md` mtime newer than the index `last_updated`. `SkillRegistry::load`'s signature is unchanged; `entries()` is a new `(path, &Skill)` accessor used by the writer. [`SkillsCorePlugin::open`](../../crates/nexus-skills/src/core_plugin.rs) and the `reload` handler (id 5) now best-effort persist the index after a successful load; failures log at `warn` and never abort the open / reload. The plugin's handler dispatch path keeps using the in-memory `SkillRegistry` directly — `load_with_index` is a read-side optimization for external CLIs only, never a short-circuit. `.skill.md` files remain authoritative. Coverage: 10 new unit tests — 7 in `registry_index.rs` (`write_then_read_roundtrips_two_skills`, `write_uses_forward_slash_paths_on_all_platforms`, `write_is_atomic_no_partial_file_on_serde_error`, `read_missing_file_returns_io_not_found`, `version_field_is_one_dot_zero`, `last_updated_is_valid_rfc3339`, `epoch_zero_formats_as_unix_epoch`), 3 in `registry.rs` (`load_with_index_uses_index_when_fresh`, `load_with_index_falls_back_to_walk_when_missing`, `load_with_index_falls_back_when_listed_path_missing`), and 2 in `core_plugin.rs` (`open_writes_registry_json_after_load`, `reload_handler_rewrites_index`). Total `cargo test -p nexus-skills`: 42 passing (was 32).

### BL-008: Mermaid Diagram Plugin ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** New fenced-code-renderer registry — [`shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/cm/fencedCodeRegistry.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/cm/fencedCodeRegistry.ts) — owns a singleton `Map<language, FencedRenderer>` with first-match-wins duplicate guard, a per-(language, source) LRU cache (cap 64), `generation()` counter, and `onChange()` listeners that the live-preview StateField subscribes to via a `ViewPlugin` so a renderer registered after mount triggers a recompute. Public API: `api.editor.registerFencedCodeRenderer(language, renderer)` exposed via [`@nexus/extension-api` `EditorAPI`](../../packages/nexus-extension-api/src/index.ts) and wired through [`shell/src/host/PluginAPI.ts`](../../shell/src/host/PluginAPI.ts) — the disposer is auto-tracked by `PluginRegistry.trackSubscription` so plugin deactivate sweeps the registration. Live-preview integration: new `FencedCodeWidget` adjacent to `TableWidget` in [`livePreviewDecorations.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/cm/livePreviewDecorations.ts); off-cursor blocks with a registered language emit a block-replace widget that calls `renderCached` (sync hit → swap inline; miss → `<pre><code>` placeholder + async swap on resolve). On-cursor falls through to the legacy fence-line replace so source stays editable. Preview-mode integration: `marked.use({ renderer: { code } })` in [`markdownRender.ts`](../../shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/markdownRender.ts) emits `<div class="nexus-fenced-pending">` placeholders carrying the language + base64 source; the new `hydrateFencedCode(root)` helper walks them after React mounts the sanitized HTML and replaces each with the rendered widget. Mermaid plugin lives under [`shell/src/plugins/community/mermaid/`](../../shell/src/plugins/community/mermaid/) — `index.ts` registers the renderer and lazy-imports the ~150 KB mermaid library only on first render via Vite's chunked dynamic import. Default-off in `shell/src/plugins/catalog.ts` (DEFAULT_OFF_PLUGINS) so users opt in via Settings → Plugins. Coverage: 14 new unit tests in `fencedCodeRegistry.test.ts` covering register / dispose / duplicate-warn / case-insensitivity / generation / onChange / sync + async + error caching / re-register invalidation; 4 new live-preview decoration tests for FencedCodeWidget emission, on-cursor fallback, unregistered-language pass-through, and widget equality; 3 mermaid-plugin lifecycle tests. Deviation from the plan: the spec called for a community-plugin loaded via the Blob-URL community-plugin loader, but that path can't resolve `import("mermaid")` without a community-plugin bundler. The directory layout matches the spec; registration flows through the catalog as a stepping-stone — `plugin.json` is `enabled: false` so the community loader skips it. Once a community-plugin bundler lands, the catalog wiring will be deleted and the plugin will load through the standard discovery path.

### BL-018: AI Token Budget Enforcement ✅ (2026-04-28)

**Delivered:** PRD-12 §12 lands as a small library-only crate addition. New [`crates/nexus-ai/src/tokens.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/tokens.rs) defines a `TokenCounter` trait + `ApproxTokenCounter` that returns `(text.len() + 3) / 4` — the 4-chars-per-token approximation Anthropic's docs recommend for English — so no `tiktoken` / `tokenizers` dependency is pulled in. `TokenBudget::new(total, reserved)` carves out the response reservation up-front; `allocate(kind, tokens)` charges against a `ContextSourceKind` (`RagChunk` / `SystemPrompt` / `UserPrompt` / `Other`), rejecting and leaving state unchanged on overflow; `remaining` / `used` / `utilization` round out the accounting surface. `BudgetWarning::NearLimit { utilization }` fires when realised utilisation crosses the 80 % threshold; `BudgetWarning::SourceDropped { kind, tokens }` records every chunk that didn't fit. RAG-side: `rag::build_rag_prompt_budgeted(sources, &mut budget, &counter) -> (String, Vec<BudgetWarning>)` sorts sources by descending score, charges each rendered chunk under the upper-bound `Source 99: [[path]]\n<text>\n\n` template, drops the lowest-scoring chunks first when they don't fit, and surfaces the warnings. The pre-existing `build_rag_prompt` stays `pub` as a thin wrapper around it (constructs an effectively unlimited budget, discards warnings) so every existing caller (`rag::query`, `stream_ask`) keeps its byte-for-byte legacy behaviour. `AiConfig` gained `context_window: u32` (default 8192) and `reserved_response_tokens: u32` (default 1024); the existing `max_tokens` (provider request body cap on generation length) is untouched. Coverage: 10 new unit tests — 6 in `tokens.rs` (`approx_counter_returns_chars_div_4_rounded_up`, `budget_remaining_subtracts_reserved_and_used`, `budget_allocate_returns_false_when_overflow`, `budget_utilization_reports_used_over_available`, plus edge cases for zero-available utilisation and additive same-kind allocation) + 4 in `rag.rs` (`budgeted_prompt_includes_all_sources_when_under_budget`, `budgeted_prompt_drops_lowest_score_first_when_over_budget`, `budgeted_prompt_emits_near_limit_warning_at_80pct`, `budgeted_prompt_with_zero_sources_returns_legacy_default`). Out of scope per the BL-018 plan: wiring the budget into `stream_chat` / `stream_ask` provider request paths — that ships when a downstream caller needs it.

### BL-002: Typed Property Index ✅ (2026-04-18)

**Delivered:** [`crates/nexus-storage/src/search_scope.rs`](../../crates/nexus-storage/src/search_scope.rs) `prop:` scope now consumes the typed columns (`value_num`, `value_date`, `value_bool`) populated by migration 003. `ScopeFilter::Property` gained a `PropertyOp` discriminator (`Contains` / `NumCmp(CmpOp, f64)` / `DateCmp(CmpOp, i64)` / `BoolEq(bool)`) with operator parsing inside `parse_prop_body`. Supported surface:

- `prop:priority>3`, `prop:score<=7.5`, `prop:priority=3` — numeric comparison against `value_num`.
- `prop:due<2026-01-01`, `prop:due>=2026-03-01` — YYYY-MM-DD dates parsed to unix seconds and compared against `value_date`.
- `prop:draft=true` / `prop:draft=FALSE` — boolean equality against `value_bool`.
- `prop:status:done` — legacy substring match against the raw JSON `value` column (unchanged).

Typed operators dispatch to typed columns only (`… IS NOT NULL AND value_num > ?`), so a non-numeric property never accidentally matches a numeric query. Malformed tokens (unparseable numbers/dates on `>`/`<` operators, empty keys/values) fall through to plain text. Coverage: 11 new unit tests in `search_scope.rs` — 6 parser cases (num_gt, num_lte, date_lt, bool_eq, eq_numeric, contains, unparseable-fallback) + 5 filter cases (num_gt match/exclude, date_lt match, bool_eq match/exclude, contains legacy). No PRD surface changed; strictly a `nexus-storage` library improvement consumed through the existing `com.nexus.storage::search` IPC handler.

### BL-001: Daily Notes ✅ (2026-04-18)

**Delivered:** [`crates/nexus-cli/src/commands/content.rs`](../../crates/nexus-cli/src/commands/content.rs) `daily()` (wired at [`main.rs:1019`](../../crates/nexus-cli/src/main.rs)) — `nexus content daily [--date YYYY-MM-DD]` creates `notes/daily/YYYY-MM-DD.md` with YAML frontmatter (`date`, `tags: [daily]`), H1 title, and `## Tasks` / `## Notes` section stubs. Existing notes short-circuit with a path echo.
