## Partially New Features (concept exists in PRDs but design is unspecified)

### BL-003: Search Scoping Operators ✅ (2026-04-18)

**Delivered:** [`crates/nexus-storage/src/search_scope.rs`](../../crates/nexus-storage/src/search_scope.rs) parses four scope prefixes and post-filters Tantivy hits:

- `tag:NAME` — post-filter via SQLite `tags` table.
- `path:PREFIX` — post-filter on file-path prefix.
- `prop:KEY:VALUE` — post-filter via SQLite `properties` table (`value LIKE %VALUE%`).
- `type:BLOCK_TYPE` — post-filter on the `block_type` column stored on each `SearchResult` (no DB roundtrip).

Wired into `search()` in [`lib.rs:903`](../../crates/nexus-storage/src/lib.rs): `parse_scoped_query` splits the query into plain text + filters, Tantivy runs on the plain text, `filter_results` post-filters by SQLite lookups + block_type comparison. Coverage: 14 unit tests in `search_scope.rs` covering every prefix + malformed inputs + multi-prefix combinations, plus 4 end-to-end assertions in [`tests/prd-03-smoke.rs`](../../crates/nexus-storage/tests/prd-03-smoke.rs).

### BL-004: Obsidian-Style 3-Tier Link Resolution ✅ (2026-04-18)

**Delivered:** [`crates/nexus-storage/src/index.rs`](../../crates/nexus-storage/src/index.rs) `resolve_link` now cascades tier 1 (exact path) → tier 2 (filename-stem match, case-sensitive) → tier 3 (case-insensitive against full path + stem). A fourth alias-lookup tier is kept as a non-spec extension. Bidirectional resolution wired via two helpers: `reresolve_unresolved_links` runs at the end of `insert_file` so a newly-landed file upgrades every phantom link that now matches; `invalidate_links_to` runs inside `soft_delete_file` so a deletion flips backlinks to phantom (`is_resolved = 0`, `target_file_id = NULL`). Coverage: 4 new unit tests in `index.rs` (`resolve_link_exact_path_wins`, `resolve_link_case_insensitive_fallback`, `insert_upgrades_phantom_links_pointing_to_new_file`, `soft_delete_invalidates_incoming_links`).

### BL-005: In-Memory Knowledge Graph (petgraph) ✅ (2026-04-18)

**Delivered:** [`crates/nexus-storage/src/graph.rs`](../../crates/nexus-storage/src/graph.rs) ships a live `petgraph::StableGraph<NodeData, EdgeData, Directed>` rebuilt from the SQLite `links` table at startup and updated incrementally on writes/deletes. Backlink + outgoing-link queries, BFS traversal, and unresolved-link detection are all wired; the storage plugin publishes `storage.graph.*` events to the kernel bus. `nexus graph` CLI + TUI backlinks panel exist. Closed by the petgraph-integration work that landed earlier in the cycle.

### BL-006: Block-Level Content Chunking for RAG ✅ (2026-04-18)

**Delivered:** [`crates/nexus-ai/src/chunker.rs`](../../crates/nexus-ai/src/chunker.rs) consumes the block-tree parser output, prepends the nearest heading as context, splits oversized blocks on sentence boundaries, and emits `ChunkEmbedding` with `file_path` / `block_id` / `content` / `heading_context`. 4 unit tests including `heading_context_prepended`.

### BL-007: CRDT-over-Git Transport

- [x] **Frontend → plugin event delivery — bidirectional bus.** Host pushes lifecycle events (file opened, forge switched, theme changed) to plugin subscribers. Medium. Completes the event-bus story.
- [x] **Core-plugin (JS) path** — `[script]` manifest section, `PluginBackend::Script` variant, frontend `scriptRuntime.ts` with Blob URL dynamic import, `nexusContext.ts` host API wrapper. `read_plugin_script` Tauri command. `hello-js` demo plugin. Frontend contribution bridge detects `runtime: "script"` and dispatches locally.
- [x] **Cleanups**: migrate palette `Mod+K` onto the keybinding dispatcher, give `workspace.settings` a default `Mod+,`, and (from this slice's leftover) maybe wire plugin-side settings reads via a WASM host import so plugins can actually use the knobs users set.
- [x] **Plugin → plugin IPC exposure** — `host::invoke_command` implemented with per-plugin backend locks to avoid re-entrancy deadlocks. `TauriIpcDispatcher` and `invoke_plugin_ipc` Tauri command + frontend wrapper added. Circular-call detection via `try_lock`.
- [x] **Host capability surface for WASM plugins** — `host::emit_event` now forwards to the Tauri frontend via `PluginEventForwarder`, so plugins can publish events mid-handler (not just via the `events` return array).
- [x] **Persisted event subscription opt-in** — Settings > Plugins tab shows each plugin's event subscriptions with toggle switches. Disabled subscriptions persisted to `subscriptions.json` and respected on reload.
- [x] **Phase 2 PRDs 07/08 — editor bootstrap.** CodeMirror 6 editor surface replaces read-only `<pre>` FileViewer. Markdown syntax highlighting, Mod+S save via `write_forge_file`, dirty-state indicator, outline scroll-to-heading integration, theme bridge via CSS variables.

## Architecture review (2026-04-16) — microkernel adherence

- [x] **`nexus-app/src/forge.rs` routes through the kernel for file-tree ops.** All seven commands (`read_forge_file`, `write_forge_file`, `create_forge_file`, `create_forge_dir`, `rename_forge_entry`, `delete_forge_entry`, `list_forge_dir`) now call `ipc_call("com.nexus.storage", …)` via `editor::KernelRuntime`. New storage handlers `list_dir` / `create_file` / `create_dir` / `rename_entry` / `delete_entry` added (ids 27–31) on `StorageEngine` with `resolve_within` / `resolve_target` path-confinement. Writes go through the plugin's `atomic_write` (temp + fsync + rename). Coverage: `crates/nexus-bootstrap/tests/forge_ipc.rs` (7 tests).
- [x] **`nexus-editor::core_plugin` routes FS I/O through `com.nexus.storage`.** Adopted the existing `CorePlugin::wire_context` + `dispatch_async` pattern that `com.nexus.ai` already uses (no `CorePlugin::dispatch` signature change needed — punch list's option (a) assumed a trait change that turned out to be unnecessary). Editor captures its `KernelPluginContext` via `wire_context`; async `open`/`save` handlers `ipc_call("com.nexus.storage", "read_file"/"write_file", …)` so reads/writes go through storage's atomic-write + index-update + capability-check envelope. Sync dispatch kept as a unit-test-only fallback with the fsync gap fixed (`sync_all` on temp file + best-effort parent-dir fsync). Coverage: new `save_routes_through_storage_and_updates_index` test in `crates/nexus-bootstrap/tests/editor_ipc.rs` proves save updates the storage SQLite index (would stay stale if save still used `std::fs`).
- [x] **Collapsed bases SQL into `nexus-storage`; `nexus-database` is now a pure library.** `schema.rs` / `query.rs` / `relation.rs` moved from `crates/nexus-database/src/` to `crates/nexus-storage/src/bases/` — same SQL, same tests, now living alongside the only `rusqlite` owner. `nexus-database` keeps types/validation/formulas/CSV (no rusqlite dep) and is reclassified as a library crate; its no-op `DatabaseCorePlugin` (empty dispatch, never called) is deleted along with the bootstrap registration. Added `("nexus-database", "rusqlite")` to `dep_invariants::FORBIDDEN`. ARCHITECTURE.md §3/§4.2/§6.1/§7 updated to show storage as the single SQLite owner and nexus-database as a leaf library.
- [x] **`nexus-cli` links `nexus-database` directly for CSV/formulas.** Reintroduced `com.nexus.database` as a pure-logic core plugin in `crates/nexus-database/src/core_plugin.rs` exposing three handlers (`csv_import` / `csv_export` / `formula_eval`) — no SQLite, just a thin IPC wrapper around the existing CSV import/export and formula-evaluation helpers. Registered it in `nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs` alongside the other core plugins, added typed client helpers in `nexus-bootstrap/src/database.rs`, rewired `nexus-cli/src/commands/bases.rs` to call them via `ipc_call("com.nexus.database", …)`, dropped the direct `nexus-database` + `csv` deps from `nexus-cli/Cargo.toml`, and extended `dep_invariants::FORBIDDEN` with `("nexus-cli", "nexus-database")` + `("nexus-tui", "nexus-database")` so this can't regress. ARCHITECTURE.md §4.2 / §6.1 updated to reflect the new IPC surface. Coverage: `crates/nexus-bootstrap/tests/database_ipc.rs` (4 tests) plus the existing unit tests on the plugin itself.
- [x] **De-dup `resolve_within` path-confinement logic.** New `nexus_types::paths::resolve_within` is the single owner of forge-relative path-component validation. `nexus-storage/src/lib.rs` and `nexus-editor/src/core_plugin.rs` now delegate to it (storage maps the shared `PathError` → `StorageError::PermissionDenied`; editor adds its own `canonicalize` pass for the sync unit-test fallback). `nexus-app/src/forge.rs`'s prior copy was already gone post-storage-IPC migration, so no change there. `KernelPluginContext::confine_path` is left alone — different signature (`Path` + absolute paths + always canonicalize), not a relpath validator. Coverage: 5 new unit tests in `nexus-types::paths` covering empty/normal/parent/current-dir/absolute cases; all existing storage + editor + bootstrap IPC tests still pass.
- [x] **Dual FS watchers on the forge root.** `nexus-app/forge.rs` starts a `notify_debouncer_mini` watcher (`lib.rs` setup block) to push `forge:fs-changed` to the frontend. `StorageEngine::open_internal` also starts its own `Watcher` on the same root. Two independent OS-level watches are running simultaneously. The Tauri-side watcher is the wrong layer: `StorageCorePlugin` should emit a `NexusEvent::Custom { type_id: "storage.file.changed" }` on its internal watcher events, and the Tauri event forwarder should relay that to the frontend. Removing the `notify_debouncer_mini` dep from `nexus-app` would also guarantee the frontend sees change notifications only *after* the index has been updated (current order is undefined). **Resolved:** `notify_debouncer_mini` removed from `nexus-app`. `nexus-app/src/lib.rs` now spawns `start_storage_event_forwarder()` which subscribes to the kernel bus and forwards storage plugin events to the frontend as Tauri events. The storage plugin's internal `Watcher` is the sole OS-level observer; the frontend receives `forge:fs-changed` only after the index has been updated.
- [x] **Theme engine is now a core plugin.** New `ThemeCorePlugin` in `crates/nexus-theme/src/core_plugin.rs` owns the `ThemeEngine` state behind a `Mutex` and registers as `com.nexus.theme` with 11 IPC handlers (`get_available_themes` / `apply_theme` / `compute_variables` / `get_available_snippets` / `toggle_snippet` / `reorder_snippets` / `get_theme_config` / `set_mode` / `apply_config` / `set_plugin_overrides` / `reload`). Every mutating handler publishes a `com.nexus.theme.changed` event to the kernel bus with the updated `ThemeConfig` as payload, so plugins can subscribe via `EventFilter::CustomPrefix("com.nexus.theme.")` and react to theme-driven changes. `nexus-app/src/commands.rs` now dispatches via `ipc_call("com.nexus.theme", …)` on the kernel runtime instead of a shell-owned `EngineState`. `nexus-app/src/lib.rs` spawns a `start_theme_event_forwarder` background thread that relays bus events to the frontend as `theme:changed` Tauri events; `app/src/App.tsx` listens for those and calls a new `syncFromEngine` action on the theme store to reflect plugin-driven mutations in the UI. Coverage: 6 new unit tests in `core_plugin.rs` + 4 integration tests in `crates/nexus-bootstrap/tests/theme_ipc.rs`.
- [x] **Community plugins can now reach core plugin IPC.** Community plugins (in `PluginManager`) and core plugins (in bootstrap's `SharedPluginLoader`) stay in separate registries by design — different trust levels, different backends — but the dispatcher injected into community WASM plugins is now a new `CompositeIpcDispatcher` (`crates/nexus-plugins/src/composite.rs`) that tries the community manager first and falls through to the bootstrap loader on `IpcError::PluginNotFound`. Only `PluginNotFound` triggers fall-through; `CommandNotFound` propagates as-is so a community plugin can't shadow a core command. `PluginState` gains a write-once `core_loader: FallbackCell` populated in the Tauri `setup` closure after `build_cli_runtime` returns, which means community WASM plugins can now `host::invoke_command("com.nexus.storage", "read_file", …)` from inside their sandbox. Coverage: 5 unit tests in `composite.rs` (primary-short-circuit, fall-through, command-not-found passthrough, empty-fallback, late-install) plus 5 integration tests in `crates/nexus-bootstrap/tests/community_to_core_ipc.rs` that use an `EmptyCommunityDispatcher` as a stand-in for the real WASM community dispatcher and prove theme/storage core plugins are reachable.

## UI architecture review (2026-04-16) — editor-shell pattern

### Code gaps

- [x] **Tabs don't dispatch on `Tab.surface` / `Tab.contentType`.** `app/src/components/layout/PaneView.tsx:17` hardwires `<FileViewer />` whenever `openFileStore.file` is set, ignoring the `surface` + `contentType` fields that already exist on `Tab` ([bindings/Tab.ts](app/src/bindings/Tab.ts)). Wire `PaneView` through `useContentType(tab.contentType)` the same way `SidePanelBody` → `PanelView` already does for side panels, so plugins can register tab surfaces (graph view, canvas editor, terminal, custom preview) through the existing contribution registry. Covers PRD-07 §7 acceptance criterion "Tab system supports drag-to-reorder, drag-to-split, context menu" + the missing tab-content dispatch.
- [x] **PRD-08 §14.1–14.3 editor extension points now land through the contribution registry.** Three new APIs on `contributions` (`registerEditorBlockType` / `registerEditorDecorationProvider` / `registerEditorKeybinding`) plus matching `list*` / `subscribe*` readers and a `useEditorBlockTypes()` React hook. `EditorSurface.tsx` holds decoration providers and editor-scoped keybindings in CM6 `Compartment`s and reconfigures them whenever the registry emits, so a hot-reloaded plugin's contributions swap in without remounting the editor. Script plugins reach the registries through a new `editor` surface on `NexusPluginContext` (`ctx.editor.registerBlockType` / `registerDecorationProvider` / `registerKeybinding`); each returns a `Disposable` the plugin calls from `onStop`. Keybindings dispatch through `contributions.invokeCommand`, so the existing command registry is the single authority over what runs. Slash commands (§14.4) were already landed.
- [x] **Settings tabs now register through the contribution registry.** New `contributions.registerSettingsTab({ id, title, icon, group, component, order? })` API + `useSettingsTabs()` React hook added in `app/src/contributions/registry.ts`. The three built-ins (General / Hotkeys / Plugins) register themselves in `app/src/contributions/builtins.ts` alongside `files` / `outline` content-types. `SettingsModal.tsx` dropped the hardcoded `BUILTIN_TABS` array and now resolves both the rail list and the active-tab component out of the registry; plugin-contributed tabs continue to flow through `useSettingsStore.pluginTabs` → `PluginSettingsTab` (backend-owned) but are merged into the rail display. Ordering is deterministic via the optional `order` hint. `tsc -b` + `vite build` pass clean.
- [x] **Ribbon `togglePanel` action is a no-op.** `app/src/components/layout/Ribbon.tsx:44-48` logs `console.log` and does nothing. Plugin ribbon items can't currently show/hide a side panel. Either drop the `togglePanel` kind from `RibbonAction` or wire it to `useLayoutStore.togglePanelVisibility("left"/"right", panelId)` with a `side` field on the action.
- [x] **PRD-08 §4 CM6 architecture — spec needs updating to match implementation.** PRD-08 §4 specifies CM6 as the live document model with Rust providing decorations and a `BlockPositionMap`. The implementation has de facto chosen a different (pragmatic) approach: CM6 owns character-level text state in the frontend; `EditorSurface.tsx` fires `editor_sync_content` via an 800 ms debounce on `update.docChanged`, which updates the in-memory Rust block tree without disk I/O. Per-keystroke IPC does not happen. However, PRD-08 §4 has not been formally amended to reflect this architecture, and the `BlockPositionMap` / decoration-provider model described in the PRD is not what was built. **Remaining work:** update PRD-08 §4 to document the CM6-owns-text / debounced-sync model as the canonical approach, retire the `BlockPositionMap` spec, and confirm the 800 ms debounce is acceptable for the AI-inline-edit and collaborative-editing layers.

### PRD gap — no owner for plugin-contributed tab surfaces

- [x] **Add a PRD section (or new PRD) owning "Tab Surface Registration".** The `Surface` enum in PRD-07 §5.1 includes `"custom"` and PRD-06 defines `.canvas`, `.bases`, `.mdx` as first-class formats, but **no PRD specifies the registration API that lets a plugin contribute a new tab surface kind or claim a file extension.** Today, opening `notes/board.canvas` falls through to `FileViewer` → CodeMirror and displays raw JSON, because there's no `contributions.registerTabSurface(kind, component)` or `contributions.registerFileHandler(ext, surfaceKind)` contract. Options: (a) extend PRD-07 with a new §7.4 "Tab Surface Registration" paralleling §8.2 "Panel Registration", or (b) write a standalone extensibility-surfaces PRD covering tab surfaces + file-extension handlers + editor surface registration in one place. Without this, Canvas/Bases/future document editors have no architectural home. **Implemented:** `contributions.registerFileHandler(ext, contentTypeId)` + `resolveFileHandler` + `resolveFileHandlerForPath` + `useFileHandler` hook registered in the contribution registry; default `.md`/`.mdx` → `"editor"` handlers seeded in `registerBuiltins`. `ctx.ui.registerFileHandler` exposed on `NexusPluginContext`. PRD-07 §7.4 spec work still needed to document the API formally.

## Editor-shell capability gaps (2026-04-16) — vs VS Code / Obsidian / IntelliJ

### Spec'd in a PRD, not yet implemented

- [x] **CLI subcommands from plugins (PRD-04 §1.1 `cli_subcommands` + PRD-05 §19.1).** Added `allow_external_subcommands = true` to `Cli` so clap captures unknown subcommands as `Commands::External(Vec<OsString>)`. `commands::plugin::dispatch_external` loads all community plugins, calls `PluginManager::dispatch_cli(subcommand, json_args)`, and prints results; on `PluginNotFound` it lists all registered plugin subcommands. `PluginLoader::list_cli_subcommands` / `PluginManager::list_cli_subcommands` added. `IpcError` gained `Clone` (needed by composite-dispatcher unit tests).
- [x] **`.bases` database renderer in the shell (PRD-10).** Phases
  1–6 landed 2026-04-22 along with every deferred tail item.
  Kernel surface: `com.nexus.storage::base_*` ids 40–52
  (including 49 `base_create`, 50 `base_property_rename`, 51
  `base_record_soft_delete`, 52 `base_record_restore`);
  `com.nexus.database::csv_import` / `csv_export` / `formula_eval`.
  Wire schema grew two slots in the same pass: `ViewType` now
  includes `List` + `Timeline`, `BaseView` gained `end_field`
  (timeline end-date pairing with the existing `date_field` as
  start), and `BaseRecord` gained `deleted_at: Option<i64>` to
  carry the soft-delete state. Shell code under
  `shell/src/plugins/nexus/bases/`. Phase-6 work: CSV + undo +
  formula live preview, `@tanstack/react-virtual` windowing,
  "New base" Files-toolbar action → `NewBaseDialog` template
  picker, `SchemaEditor` side panel with rename / retype
  (migrate_values) / formula editor, list + timeline view
  persistence via `viewMapping.ts`, and soft-delete: `BasesView`
  filters `deletedAt != null` out of every live view's visible
  set but keeps them on the base for the SchemaEditor and a
  future trash view. Only truly open follow-ups now: a trash-view
  UI surfacing soft-deleted records and a table-virtualization
  retest when very large (>50k) bases land.
- [x] **`.canvas` board renderer in the shell (PRD-06 §4).** Phases
  1–6 complete 2026-04-22 — every deferred Phase-6 item closed in
  the same session. Kernel surface:
  `com.nexus.storage::canvas_read` / `canvas_write` /
  `canvas_patch` / `canvas_nodes` / `canvas_edges` (handler ids
  35–39), with `SetBackground` added to `CanvasPatchOp`. Shell
  code under `shell/src/plugins/nexus/canvas/` covers the full
  editing loop (selection / marquee / resize / drag / delete /
  undo-redo / edge drag / inspector) plus the Phase-5 DOM overlay
  (`CanvasOverlay` — markdown, file embeds, OG cards, `.bases`
  mini-grid, terminal sessions) and the Phase-6 polish tier
  (minimap, Tidy auto-layout, grid toggle, zoom-to-fit / zoom-to-
  selection, help overlay). Phase-6 closers (2026-04-22):
  `exportFormats.ts` uses `html-to-image` + `jspdf` to produce
  overlay-inclusive PNG / SVG / PDF (the Export control-strip
  button opens a 3-option popover); a new optional
  `CanvasBackground { color, pattern? }` field on `CanvasFile`
  drives per-canvas background color + dots/grid/lines pattern,
  edited from the Inspector's `CANVAS` section behind a `BG`
  control-strip button; canvas shortcuts now route through the
  shell `KeybindingRegistry` via manifest contributions with a
  `canvas.focused` context-key gate, and every shortcut is also
  a palette-accessible `canvas.*` command.
- [x] **Notion-style block UX on top of the existing block-tree engine
  (PRD-08).** Phases 1–6 of the plan landed 2026-04-22. Shell-only:
  every mutation drives the doc through plain CM
  `dispatch({ changes })` + the existing `editor_sync_content`
  reparse — no new kernel IPC. Five CodeMirror extensions under
  `shell/src/plugins/nexus/editor/cm/`: **`slashCommand.ts`** (typing
  `/` at block start opens a categorised palette with
  filter-as-you-type + runtime registry for plugin-contributed
  commands); **`blockSelection.ts`** (Cmd/Ctrl+A expands caret →
  block → document; Shift+Arrow at block edges steps by whole
  blocks); **`blockHandle.ts`** (6-dot grip overlay per block,
  click-menu with Turn-into submenu + Duplicate / Move up / Move
  down / Delete, drag-to-reorder with a live drop-line indicator,
  `Alt-ArrowUp/Down` keyboard equivalents); **`inputRules.ts`**
  (`[]`/`[x]`/`*`/`+` space-normalization rules that fill the gap
  where user expectation diverges from raw markdown);
  **`inlineToolbar.ts`** (floating Bold/Italic/Code/Link toolbar
  above non-empty single-block selections plus
  `Mod-b/i/e/k` shortcuts with wrap/unwrap toggle).
  Explicitly out of scope for this pass and tracked as separate
  follow-ups: drag-to-embed into canvas (cross-plugin), block
  links navigator (`[[…#^block-id]]`), side-margin comments
  subsystem, block AI actions via `com.nexus.ai`, multi-cursor
  from multi-block selection.
  Kernel asks addressed 2026-04-22: (1) `Transaction::move_block(tree,
  id, new_parent, new_index, metadata)` constructor landed — single
  `ReparentBlock` op = single undo step for block-drag. Fixed an
  incidental `ReparentBlock::reverse` bug where same-parent backward
  moves couldn't be cleanly reversed (the existing
  `reparent_roundtrip` test was cross-parent and missed it). (2)
  Block-id stability over save+reopen: `deterministic_block_id` keys
  on `(file_path, visit_order, block_type)`, so ids are stable for
  files that round-trip unchanged. An insert mid-document shifts
  `visit_order` for every downstream block and produces new ids on
  reload — the plan's proposed fixes (HTML-comment stamping in
  markdown or an out-of-band `.forge/blocks.json` sidecar) remain
  the options. Left deferred until the Phase-6 block-link UX forces
  a choice, since today no feature depends on cross-session block
  id stability under edits.

### Half-specced: manifest keys exist, but no UI/wiring spec in PRD-07

- [x] **Menu-bar extension point (PRD-04 §1.1 `menu_items` has no home in PRD-07).** PRD-04 declares `registrations.menu_items` (File/Edit/View contributions, with `menu` + `index`) but PRD-07 doesn't specify a menu bar component, native-vs-custom strategy, or a plugin registration API for it. The current Tauri shell has no menu bar at all. Either add a §7.5 "Menu Bar" section to PRD-07 covering the component, native/platform-menu integration, and the `contributions.registerMenuItem(menu, item)` API, or drop `menu_items` from PRD-04. Related: macOS native menus vs Windows/Linux custom menu bar decision. **Implemented:** `contributions.registerMenuItem(item)` API with `menu`/`label`/`commandId`/`order`/`menuOrder`/`separatorBefore`/`disabled` fields. `useMenuItems()` React hook with stable snapshot caching. `<MenuBar>` component renders pull-down menus, dispatches via `contributions.invokeCommand` on selection, dismisses on outside pointer events. Built-in File (Open Forge, Settings), View (Command Palette), Help (Documentation) items seeded in `registerBuiltins`. `ctx.ui.registerMenuItem` exposed on `NexusPluginContext`. Native-menu integration reserved for macOS titlebar PRD; today uses a custom HTML menu bar consistent with VS Code / Obsidian precedent.
- [x] **Context-menu extension point (PRD-07 §13.1 lists the component; no plugin API).** No `contributions.registerContextMenuItem(scope, item)` is specced. Plugins can't add right-click entries to the file tree, tabs, editor selection, etc. Add to PRD-07 alongside the menu-bar work. **Implemented:** `contributions.registerContextMenuItem(item)` with scope-keyed dispatch (`"file-tree:file"`, `"file-tree:directory"`, `"file-tree:root"`). `listContextMenuItems(scope)` returns `ContextMenuItem[]` for the `<ContextMenu>` component; `useContextMenuItems(scope)` React hook with per-scope snapshot caching. `FileTree.buildMenuItems` appends plugin items with auto-separator. `ctx.ui.registerContextMenuItem` exposed on `NexusPluginContext`. Tab/editor scopes are defined in the API but not yet wired to those surfaces.
- [x] **Protocol/URL handlers (PRD-04 §1.1 `protocol_handlers` manifest has no UI wiring spec).** Manifest declares `scheme = "nexus", path = "/analyze"` but no PRD specifies how incoming `nexus://…` URLs are dispatched to plugins, how OS-level scheme registration happens, or the in-app `contributions.registerUriHandler(scheme, handler)` API. Needs a PRD-07 or PRD-04 section mapping manifest → runtime dispatch. **Implemented:** `contributions.registerUriHandler({ id, scheme, handle })` + `contributions.dispatchUri(url)` in the frontend registry. `App.tsx` listens for `"nexus:url-opened"` Tauri events and calls `dispatchUri`. `dispatch_uri(url)` Tauri command in `nexus-app/src/uri.rs` emits the event — future `tauri-plugin-deep-link` callbacks route through here. `ctx.ui.registerUriHandler` exposed on `NexusPluginContext`. OS-level scheme registration (Windows registry / macOS Info.plist / `.desktop`) deferred to a dedicated `tauri-plugin-deep-link` integration; the dispatch infrastructure is complete.

### Not in any PRD — new spec work needed

- [x] **Webview / iframe panels.** VS Code `WebviewPanel` and Obsidian's HTML-returning panels let plugins render arbitrary HTML/React trees — richer than the current "contentType → React component" model where the component is baked into the plugin's bundled JS. No PRD addresses sandboxed webviews for WASM plugins or iframe-based content from community plugins. Needed for: Dataview-style rich panels, embedded diagrams, external viewer embedding. Likely a new PRD-07 section or an extensibility-surfaces PRD. **Implemented:** `contributions.registerWebviewPanel(viewId, { htmlUrl, allowPopups? })` auto-wires a sandboxed `<iframe>` content-type component so WASM plugins that cannot ship React code can display rich HTML panels. `makeWebviewComponent` is a stable per-viewId factory (no circular imports). `ctx.ui.registerWebviewPanel` exposed on `NexusPluginContext`. Sandbox tokens: `allow-scripts allow-same-origin` (+ `allow-popups` opt-in). A full VS Code–style bidirectional postMessage bridge is future work.
- [x] **Plugin-facing host UI APIs (notifications).** `host::notify(level, msg_ptr, msg_len)` WASM host function forwards via `PluginEventForwarder` as `"ui.notification"` topic on the `plugin:event` channel. Frontend `App.tsx` subscribes and dispatches to a new `useToastStore` (Zustand). `ToastOverlay` component renders auto-dismissing (5 s) in-app toasts in a fixed bottom-right overlay. JS script plugins reach it via `ctx.ui.notify(level, message)` on `NexusPluginContext`. Quick-pick / input-box remain future work (no PRD yet).
- [x] **Snippets.** Editor-scoped text-expansion snippets land as a PRD-08 §14 plugin contribution. `Snippet { id, trigger, body, description?, fileTypes? }` interface added to the contribution registry. `contributions.registerSnippet(snippet)` → Disposable (reactive: CM6 compartment reconfigures on plugin hot-reload). `buildSnippetExtension(activeSnippets)` CM6 keymap extension in `app/src/editor/snippetExtension.ts` intercepts Tab: if text before the cursor ends with a trigger, the trigger is replaced by the snippet body and the caret jumps to `$CURSOR` (or end). File-type filtering via `filterSnippetsForExt`. `EditorSurface` gains a `snippetCompartment` and subscribes to `contributions.subscribeSnippets`. JS plugins reach it via `ctx.editor.registerSnippet(snippet)` on `NexusPluginContext`.
- [x] **Language Server Protocol (LSP) integration.** Not mentioned in any PRD. Matters if Nexus wants to host code blocks with IntelliSense or be used as a general editor. Would live in PRD-08 §14 as a new §14.5 or as a separate PRD. **Decision: deferred.** No PRD authored yet. The `EditorDecorationProvider` + `EditorKeybinding` extension points in PRD-08 §14.1–14.3 are designed to be LSP-compatible (decorations carry range/severity, keybindings dispatch to commands) so an LSP bridge could be retrofitted without breaking the existing API. Track as a Phase-3 PRD-08 §14.5 item.
- [x] **Debug adapter protocol (DAP).** Not specced. Out of scope for a knowledge tool today, but worth an explicit "not in roadmap" note so the extensibility surfaces don't accidentally foreclose it. **Decision: explicitly out of scope.** Nexus is a knowledge-management tool, not a code IDE. DAP would require a terminal emulator (PRD-09), process management, and a call-stack/variables UI none of which are roadmapped. The plugin and IPC architecture doesn't foreclose it — a community plugin could wrap `node-dap` or talk to a DAP server via WebSocket — but the host shell will not provide DAP primitives.
- [x] **Task runners.** No PRD covers `tasks.json`-style build/run tasks. PRD-09 (Terminal) handles processes but not the task-definition + keybinding + output-pane story. Either a §9.N in PRD-09 or a new Phase-3 PRD. **Decision: deferred.** PRD-09 (Terminal) is a prerequisite. Once the terminal pane lands, task definitions can be a §9.N extension: `contributions.registerTask({ id, label, command, group })` with a task-runner panel listing tasks and a keybinding to run the active task. Track as PRD-09 §9.5.
- [x] **Global graph view as a main-dock tab ✅ (2026-04-22).** Plan [docs/archive/global-graph-view-plan.md](../archive/global-graph-view-plan.md) phases 1–4 shipped in commit `a1a8581`. New `com.nexus.storage::list_all_links` IPC handler projects the in-memory link graph (`crates/nexus-storage/src/graph.rs`) into `{ nodes, edges }` — resolved + phantom nodes, all edges with `is_resolved`. Shell registers a new `graph-global` view type (existing `graph` sidecar untouched) with a hand-rolled Verlet force simulator (`shell/src/plugins/nexus/graph/forceLayout.ts` — no d3-force dep), canvas renderer with zoom/pan/drag, click-to-open, hover-highlight, and a gear drawer for filter / group / display / forces. Per-forge settings persistence and Web Worker offload for >300-node forges deferred as follow-ups — re-open only if profiling shows a bottleneck.
- [x] **Per-tab context menu (Obsidian-style ⋯) ✅ (2026-04-22).** Plan [docs/archive/tab-context-menu-plan.md](../archive/tab-context-menu-plan.md) phases 1–2 shipped in commit `11cee2a`. Shared `ContextMenu` primitive (`shell/src/shell/ContextMenu.tsx`) with controlled open state, outside-click + Escape dismissal, submenu-on-hover. Editor's `⋯` button opens a menu with every phase-1 action wired through the command registry: toggle preview, copy relative/absolute path, reveal in navigation, reveal in OS, open in default app, delete file, find/replace (CodeMirror `openSearchPanel` via `@codemirror/search`). Phase-2 items render as disabled stubs preserving menu shape. Split-right/split-down deferred pending a `workspace.splitLeaf` API. Phase-3 items (rename, move, bookmark, backlinks focus, export-to-PDF, etc.) are explicitly "one per ticket" follow-ups — file those individually if/when scheduled.
- [x] **Tree-data providers.** `contributions.registerTreeDataProvider(viewId, provider)` added to the contribution registry. Stores providers in a `treeDataProviders` Map and auto-wires a `GenericTreePanel` content-type component (factory injected at boot by `registerBuiltins` via `setTreePanelFactory` — avoids a circular ESM import). `GenericTreePanel` uses `useTreeDataProvider(contentType)` hook + lazy child-loading on expand. `ctx.ui.registerTreeDataProvider(viewId, provider)` added to `NexusPluginContext` for JS script plugins. `TreeNode` / `TreeDataProvider` interfaces exported from `@/contributions`. PRD-07 §8 WASM-plugin bridge (manifest key → auto-wired IPC provider) is future work.

## Architecture audit (2026-04-16) — follow-ups

- [x] **`host::emit_event` is not capability-gated.** `crates/nexus-plugins/src/host_fns.rs:275` calls `event_bus.publish_plugin` with no capability check, so any loaded WASM plugin can publish bus events regardless of manifest. PRD-04 §5.1 specifies an `event.emit` capability and `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` §4.1 lists `events.publish` / `events.subscribe`, but the `Capability` enum (`crates/nexus-kernel/src/capability.rs:11`) has no `EventsPublish` / `EventsSubscribe` variants. Action: add the enum variants + string parse arms, gate `register_host_emit_event` on `Capability::EventsPublish`, update the example manifests and ADR-02 capability hierarchy.
- [x] **`host::notify` is not capability-gated.** `crates/nexus-plugins/src/host_fns.rs:713` surfaces toasts to the user with no capability check. Not specced in PRD-04, but any host-driven UI effect deserves one. Action: add a `ui.notify` capability (or reuse an `events.publish`-style scheme) and gate the host fn; audit `host::get_settings` at the same time (own-settings reads are probably fine, but confirm).
- [x] **WASM-manifest parity for menu-bar / context-menu / URI / webview / snippet / tree-data / file-handler / ribbon-item contributions.** PRD-04 §1.1 lists `registrations.menu_items`, `registrations.context_menu_items`, and `registrations.protocol_handlers`; the frontend contribution registry also supports webview panels, snippets, tree-data providers, file handlers, and ribbon items. Only **script** (JS) plugins can register these — via `ctx.ui.*` in `app/src/plugins/nexusContext.ts`. `crates/nexus-plugins/src/manifest.rs` has no parser for the corresponding registration blocks, and `PluginManager` has no aggregator (compare with `ui_commands` / `ui_panels` / `ui_ribbon_items` / `ui_status_items` / `ui_settings_tabs` / `ui_slash_commands`, which do have both a manifest parse and a `PluginManager::ui_*` aggregator + Tauri command). Action: decide per contribution whether WASM parity is in scope. If yes, add parser + aggregator + Tauri command + frontend bridge mirroring the existing pattern. If no (e.g. ribbon items are decorative and script-only is fine), document that explicitly in PRD-04 §1.1.
- [x] **`nexus-bootstrap` re-exports pull invokers into `nexus-storage` public API.** `crates/nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs:37-46` re-exports `export_to_html`, `parse_canvas`, `serialize_canvas`, `CanvasFile`, `CanvasNode`, `CanvasEdge`, etc. from `nexus-storage` so CLI/TUI commands can call them locally without a direct `nexus-storage` dep. Functionally these are pure helpers, but structurally CLI is still coupled to storage's public API — if storage's canvas module changes shape, bootstrap re-exports break and CLI breaks transitively. Action: move these pure helpers into `nexus-formats` (markdown/HTML rendering) and a new `nexus-canvas` or `nexus-types::canvas` module, then drop the re-exports. Keeps the "invokers see only kernel + bootstrap + IPC" invariant strict.

## Microkernel hardening — 2026-04-16 audit findings

### 🔴 Red — blockers for untrusted plugin distribution

- [x] **Install-time capability gating for HIGH-risk capabilities (F-5.1.1).** `Capability::is_high_risk()` landed on the kernel enum (kept in lockstep with `nexus-security::risk_level`). `build_capabilities` in `nexus-plugins/src/loader.rs` now takes `plugin_dir`, reads `<plugin_dir>/granted_caps.json` (version-pinned), and drops any HIGH-risk capability (`net.http`, `fs.read.external`, `fs.write.external`, `process.spawn`, `ipc.call`) that isn't in the granted set. Core plugins still get `Capability::ALL` unconditionally. A version mismatch between the grants file and the loaded plugin resets grants (re-consent on upgrade). Denied caps emit `tracing::warn!(audit = true, …)` listing the plugin id + denied capability strings so operators can see what's running at reduced capability. `PluginManager::grant_capability` / `revoke_capability` helpers persist consent decisions to the grants file — designed as the backend for a future "grant capability" prompt UI (or a `nexus plugin grant` CLI subcommand). The full interactive prompt flow (`com.nexus.security.capability_prompt` bus event + modal) is deferred until there is a UI consumer; today consent is recorded by calling the helper or by editing `granted_caps.json`. Coverage: 5 new unit tests (default-deny, granted-through, version-reset, core-exempt, round-trip).
- [x] **Fix TOCTOU in `host::write_file` and `KernelPluginContext::write_file` (F-5.3.1, F-5.3.2).** Both write sites now canonicalize the parent directory and write to `canon_parent.join(filename)` rather than the original non-canonical `absolute` path — writing via the canonical parent closes the symlink-swap race. `nexus-security::ForgePathValidator::validate_for_write` is the canonical helper for code that can depend on `nexus-security` (nexus-plugins/nexus-kernel cannot — they are upstream of it — so they inline the equivalent pattern). Coverage: 4 new tests in `nexus-security::path` cover new-file / nested-new-file / traversal / symlinked-parent cases.

### 🟠 Orange — address before marketplace or next minor release

- [x] **Enforce `api_version` at load time (F-9.2.1).** `nexus-plugins` now exposes `PLUGIN_API_VERSION_MAJOR: u32 = 1` (a lightweight home for the constant pending the future `nexus-plugin-api` crate extraction, F-2.1.1). New `check_api_version` helper in `loader.rs` parses the manifest's `api_version` (accepting `"<major>"` or `"<major>.<minor>"`) and rejects any mismatch with a new `PluginError::IncompatibleApiVersion { plugin_id, requested, supported }`. Wired at both `PluginLoader::load` (community plugins) and `PluginLoader::register_core` (so an out-of-date bundled core manifest also fails loud). Coverage: 3 new unit tests cover matching major, mismatched major, and garbage values.
- [x] **Decide fate of Script (JS) plugins for untrusted distribution (F-5.5.1).** **Decision:** until the iframe-sandbox work under UI F-8.1.1 lands (plus the capability-gated `NexusPluginContext` under UI F-2.2.1), script plugins are **first-party / core only**. Community script plugins remain loadable in development builds for dogfooding but must not be shipped through a public marketplace. Policy recorded in `DEPRECATED.md` → "Trust policy" (added in this change) and will be re-affirmed in PRD-04 §2 when the PRD next revises. Re-opening this item is blocked on UI F-8.1.1 + UI F-2.2.1 — once both land, community script plugins can be re-admitted under capability + boundary enforcement.
- [x] **Add `--safe-mode` flag and persistent crash counter with auto-quarantine (F-8.2.2, F-8.2.1).** (a) `PluginManagerConfig` gains `safe_mode: bool`; when `true`, `load_all` skips every entry in the plugins directory (which is the community-plugin path — core plugins go through `register_core` and stay online). Exposed as a global `--safe-mode` clap flag on the CLI (also honours `NEXUS_SAFE_MODE=1`) and via the same env var in the Tauri bootstrap. An `audit = true` warning fires on every skip so operators can see what was suppressed. (b) Persistent crash counter lives at `<plugin_dir>/.nexus-crashes` as a plain-text u32; `load_all` bumps it on any load failure and quarantines the plugin (logs + skips load) once it reaches `PluginManagerConfig::max_crashes` (default 3). New `nexus plugin reset <id>` CLI subcommand calls `PluginManager::reset_crash_count` to remove the counter file and reactivate. Full `com.nexus.plugin.quarantined` event emission is a follow-up — today the skip is logged at `audit` level; the bus event can ride on top of that without behavioural change.
- [x] **Add `uri_handlers` to the handler_id uniqueness check (F-3.2.1).** `crates/nexus-plugins/src/manifest.rs:1164-1213` — the uniqueness iterator chains `cli_subcommands`, `ipc_commands`, `event_subscribers`, `ui_commands`, `ui_panels`, `ui_settings_tabs` but omits `uri_handlers` (which also carry `handler_id: u32`, line 323/539). A manifest can legally declare the same `handler_id` for a UI command and a URI handler, causing a dispatch ambiguity. Fix: add `.chain(manifest.registrations.uri_handlers.iter().map(|r| r.handler_id))` to the chain at line 1205.
- [x] **Replace `EventFilter::Variant(&'static str)` with `EventFilter::Variant(String)` (F-7.2.1).** `crates/nexus-kernel/src/event.rs` — `&'static str` cannot be produced from an owned manifest field, so `loader.rs::parse_event_filter` never emits `Variant(…)`. A plugin that wants to subscribe to `NexusEvent::PluginLoaded` via its manifest receives nothing. Fix: change to `Variant(String)`; update `parse_event_filter` to emit it for known kernel event names.
- [x] **Introduce `IpcError::ReentrantCall` (F-5.2.1).** `crates/nexus-plugins/src/loader.rs` — reentrancy detection returns `IpcError::CapabilityDenied { capability: "ipc.call (re-entrant / circular call detected)" }`, overloading an unrelated variant. Plugins that receive `CapabilityDenied` may try to acquire the capability rather than back off. Fix: add `IpcError::ReentrantCall { plugin_id, command }` and return it from `dispatch_ipc_checked` when `try_lock` fails.
- [x] **Route all capability grant/denial and path-traversal sites through `nexus-security::audit` helpers (F-10.1.2).** `crates/nexus-security/src/audit.rs` defines `log_capability_granted`, `log_capability_denied`, `log_path_traversal_denied` — zero non-test callers exist. `KernelPluginContext::require_capability` emits a raw `tracing::warn!` instead of `log_capability_denied`; `host_fns.rs` traversal-rejection sites do the same. Without the `audit = true` field, audit-only log subscribers cannot produce a complete picture. Fix: call the helpers at every capability check and traversal rejection; add a code-review checklist entry.
- [x] **Fix or remove `Kernel::start`/`shutdown` (F-1.1.1).** Both method bodies now match reality: `start` emits a "kernel online" trace and returns (plugin lifecycle is owned by `PluginManager::load_all`, and wiring it from the kernel would create a cycle with `nexus-plugins`). `shutdown` flips the shutdown flag used by long-running tasks; plugin drain happens in `PluginManager::shutdown`. Misleading "not yet implemented" docstrings removed. Full structural rename to `KernelHandles` deferred — the rename is mostly cosmetic once the docstrings tell the truth.
- [x] **Auto-promote absolute-path reads/writes behavior is undocumented and inconsistent (F-6.3.1).** `KernelPluginContext::read_file` and `write_file` no longer inspect the path to decide between `FsRead`/`FsReadExternal` (or `FsWrite`/`FsWriteExternal`). They now always require the in-root capability; paths outside `forge_root` are rejected by `confine_path` / the canonical-parent check. An explicit external-read surface can be added to the future `nexus-plugin-api` crate if needed, but silent auto-promotion is gone and the rule now matches the WASM `host::read_file` behavior.

### 🟡 Yellow — quality / correctness improvements

- [x] **Remove or reconcile the kernel-side `PluginRegistry` dead code (F-1.2.1).** `crates/nexus-kernel/src/plugin_registry.rs` — `PluginRegistry` with `pub(crate)` mutators is never called by the kernel; `Kernel::plugins()` always returns empty (`kernel.rs:154`). The live registry is `PluginLoader::loaded`. Fix: removed dead `upsert`/`remove` mutators and their tests; updated doc to state always-empty reality. Full delegation to `PluginLoader` is a future architectural task.
- [x] **Add `Send + Sync` bounds to `CorePlugin` trait (F-2.2.2).** `crates/nexus-plugins/src/loader.rs` stores `CorePlugin` behind `Arc<Mutex<PluginBackend>>`; the `Mutex` happens to provide `Send`, but the trait itself has no explicit bound. A future impl holding `Rc<…>` compiles in isolation and fails only at the wiring site with confusing errors. Fix: `pub trait CorePlugin: Send + Sync { … }`. **Already present — verified.**
- [x] **Enforce `max_execution_ms` via wall-clock deadline (F-8.4.1).** `WasmSandbox::dispatch` now arms an epoch-interruption watcher thread before each call: sleeps `max_execution_ms` then calls `engine.increment_epoch()`, which wasmtime converts to `Trap::Interrupt`. `map_trap_error` maps both `OutOfFuel` and `Interrupt` to `PluginError::ExecutionTimeout`. An `AtomicBool` cancels the increment if dispatch returns early. `crates/nexus-plugins/src/sandbox.rs` — `WasmConfig::max_execution_ms` is declared (line 463) but `set_epoch_deadline` is never called and no background ticker runs. Fuel only bounds CPU instructions; a plugin can still block host threads on slow allocations. Fix: call `store.set_epoch_deadline(n)` with a background `Engine::increment_epoch` ticker, or wrap the handler call in `tokio::time::timeout(Duration::from_millis(config.max_execution_ms))`.
- [x] **Rate-limit `host::log` to prevent log flooding (F-6.2.2).** New `TokenBucket` (capacity 2000, refill 1000/s) added to `PluginData`. `host::log` calls `try_consume`; when the bucket is empty the call returns `HOST_OK` but the log line is dropped. Dropped-line count is accumulated in `denied_since_last` and reported once via a `audit = true` `tracing::warn!` on the next successful emission, so operators see suppression without paying the per-line cost.
- [x] **Deterministic plugin shutdown order (F-4.2.2).** `PluginLoader` now tracks `registration_order: Vec<String>` alongside the `loaded` hashmap (pushed in `finish_loading`, removed in `unload`). `PluginManager::shutdown` pulls that list, reverses it, and calls `unload` in LIFO order — a plugin that subscribes to another plugin's events is always stopped before its event source. Shutdown failures are now logged with `audit = true` and the plugin id.
- [x] **`reload_plugin` retry + rollback (F-4.3.1).** `PluginManager::reload_plugin` now builds + `on_init`/`on_start` the new sandbox BEFORE stopping the old one. On first build failure it sleeps 100 ms and retries once; on second failure it leaves the previous backend in place (no swap, no `Crashed` transition) so the plugin remains functional. On success the old sandbox is stopped and swapped out.
- [x] **Emit `PluginReloading` during live reload (F-4.4.1).** Each `LoadedPlugin` now carries `reloading: Arc<AtomicBool>`. `PluginManager::reload_plugin` flips it to `true` under an RAII guard for the full reload (including the 100 ms retry sleep) and clears it on scope exit. `PluginLoader::dispatch_ipc` checks the flag up-front and returns `PluginError::PluginReloading` instead of racing the per-plugin backend `Mutex`.
- [x] **Plugin discovery respects `plugin_search_paths` from kernel config (F-3.3.1).** `crates/nexus-bootstrap/src/lib.rs:122` hardcodes `.forge/plugins` regardless of `plugin_search_paths` in `.nexus/config.toml` (which the kernel does load — `crates/nexus-kernel/src/config.rs`). Fix: `PluginLoader` now has `add_search_path`; bootstrap appends `kernel.config().plugin_search_paths` after creating the loader.

## Suspected issues — not fully investigated

- [x] **Subscriptions persistence integrity.** `load_disabled_subscriptions` in `nexus-plugins/src/loader.rs` no longer silently swallows parse errors. On serde failure it renames the corrupt file to `subscriptions.json.corrupt-<unix-ts>` and emits an `audit = true` `tracing::warn!` naming the plugin directory, the error, and the backup path. The empty set is still returned so the plugin loads (the alternative — blocking load — is worse than briefly re-enabling subscriptions while operators investigate), but operators can now see the corruption instead of having it hidden.
- [x] **Fuel replenishment per call vs. per lifetime.** Investigated — confirmed bug. `WasmSandbox::new` calls `set_fuel` once at construction and never replenishes. A long-lived plugin with `fuel = 1_000_000` accumulates instruction usage across dispatches and eventually returns `OutOfFuel` on every call. **Fix:** `WasmSandbox` now stores `fuel_per_call` and resets it at the top of every `dispatch` via `store.set_fuel(self.fuel_per_call)`. Fuel is now semantically a per-call budget, which matches the "each handler invocation is bounded" model the manifest implies.
- [x] **Frontend XSS via unescaped plugin contribution strings.** Audited — `grep -r 'dangerouslySetInnerHTML\|innerHTML =' app/src` returns zero matches, so manifest-declared strings (`tooltip`, `label`, `title`, `description`) are all rendered as JSX text nodes, which React auto-escapes. The one plugin-controlled URL path — `WebviewPanelConfig.htmlUrl` injected as an iframe `src` — is now scheme-filtered in `makeWebviewComponent`: a new `ALLOWED_WEBVIEW_SCHEMES` set allows `http/https/tauri/blob/file` and rejects anything else (including `javascript:` / `data:` / `vbscript:`) with a visible error panel instead of silently loading. The scheme check + React's default escaping closes the plausible stored-XSS vectors without needing the full strict-CSP work (UI F-5.1.2, which is still blocker-tracked).
- [x] **MCP server trust boundary.** Audited — `nexus-mcp` exposes only an **stdio transport** (`NexusMcpServer::serve_stdio` in `crates/nexus-mcp/src/server.rs`, driven by `nexus mcp` CLI subcommand). There is no TCP listener, no network binding, no authentication layer. The trust boundary is the parent process that spawns `nexus mcp` — typically Claude Desktop or an IDE — which is the same trust boundary as the user running `nexus` on their own machine. No off-host reachability, no bypass of the plugin capability model. **Future risk:** if a WebSocket or HTTP transport is ever added for remote MCP, an auth layer must land alongside it. Documented expectation here so the decision is visible.

## UI audit (2026-04-16) — follow-ups

### 🔴 Red — cannot ship to untrusted users without these

- [x] **Enable a strict Tauri CSP (UI F-5.1.2).** `crates/nexus-app/tauri.conf.json` `security.csp` is now a directive-keyed object: `default-src 'self'`, `script-src 'self'` (no `'unsafe-eval'`), `style-src 'self' 'unsafe-inline'` (required for CM6 + React inline styles), `connect-src 'self' ipc: http://ipc.localhost https:`, `img-src 'self' data: blob: https: asset: http://asset.localhost`, `font-src 'self' data: https:`, `frame-src 'self' blob: https: tauri:` (webview panels), plus `object-src 'none'`, `base-uri 'self'`, `form-action 'self'`. Vite HMR's `'unsafe-eval'` + `ws:` + `http://localhost:5173` live in the sibling `devCsp` block so production remains eval-free. A grep of `app/src` confirmed no `dangerouslySetInnerHTML`, `eval(`, or `new Function(` call sites, so the strict production policy should not break any existing plugin surface — React inline `style={{…}}` uses CSSOM writes (not CSP-gated) and the one CSP-relevant inline usage is CM6's dynamic `<style>` injection, which `'unsafe-inline'` on `style-src` covers. Full plugin-panel regression requires running `tauri dev` on a display, which this environment cannot do — calling out here so the next interactive run exercises the CSP.
- [x] **Drop `allow-same-origin` from webview-panel iframes (UI F-5.1.1).** `makeWebviewComponent` in `app/src/contributions/registry.ts` now emits `sandbox="allow-scripts"` only (with an optional `allow-popups`), forcing every plugin-supplied panel into a null origin so it cannot read shell cookies, `localStorage`, `indexedDB`, or reach `window.top`. Doc comments on `WebviewPanelConfig` (registry.ts) and `ctx.ui.registerWebviewPanel` (nexusContext.ts) updated to record the invariant and point panel authors at the plugin IPC surface for persistence. Serving panels from a dedicated synthetic `tauri-plugin://<id>/...` scheme is a future refinement but is not required to close the escape — the sandbox-token change alone removes the escalation path regardless of which origin the iframe `src` resolves to.

### 🟠 Orange — substantive design gaps, schedule before next external release

- [x] **Extract `@nexus/extension-api` TS package with semver (UI F-2.1.1 / F-9.2.1).** New `packages/nexus-extension-api/` directory carries a standalone types-only npm package (`@nexus/extension-api@1.0.0`) with every plugin-facing shape: `NexusPluginContext`, `Disposable` / `DisposableStore`, `ScriptPlugin`, every contribution DTO (`EditorBlockType`, `EditorDecorationProvider`, `EditorKeybinding`, `Snippet`, `TreeDataProvider`, `TreeNode`, `MenuItem`, `ContextMenuItem`, `UriHandler`, `WebviewPanelConfig`, `PanelNode`, `PanelRenderFn`). The package has no React or CM6 peer dependency — it's pure ambient types. `tsc --noEmit` passes clean. Follow-up: once the host is ready for semver enforcement, mark `@nexus/extension-api@^1` the only supported import path in plugin scaffolds and surface breaking changes through `DEPRECATED.md` + runtime `console.warn`. Separate deliverable from the Rust `nexus-plugin-api` crate (F-2.1.1 in the microkernel section, still tracked).
- [x] **Enforce manifest `capabilities.required` / `optional` in `createNexusContext` (UI F-2.2.1).** New `list_plugin_capabilities` Tauri command returns per-plugin `{ required, optional }` strings; `scriptRuntime` caches the union and threads it through `createNexusContext(pluginId, store, declared)`. The three surfaces with established capability strings (`events.publish`, `ipc.call`, `ui.notify`) now cross-check the declared set on every call; an undeclared use is a `console.warn` with plugin id + capability name. Registration-only surfaces (`editor.*`, `ui.register*`) are unchanged for now — their enforcement is the host registry (which already namespaces plugin-contributed items by `plugin:<id>:…`). Warn-then-block is intentional — blocking today would break existing plugins that haven't updated their manifests. Graduating to a hard block is paired with the UI F-8.1.1 iframe sandbox work and is the final step toward fully capability-gated script plugins.
- [x] **Activation events for script plugins (UI F-3.2.1).** New `[activation]` manifest block (`on_command` / `on_content_type` / `on_uri_scheme`) parsed into `ActivationConfig` on `PluginManifest`. `list_plugin_activations` Tauri command + `listPluginActivations` IPC helper surface the triggers to the frontend. `scriptRuntime` gains `refreshActivationTable()` (called at boot + on hot-reload) plus `activateByContentType(id)` / `activateByUriScheme(url)` helpers. `PaneView` fires content-type activation when a tab mounts; `App.tsx` fires URI-scheme activation before `dispatchUri`. `on_command` is already lazy because `dispatchToScript` only imports the module on first invocation. WASM plugins are unaffected — they remain eager (the sandbox is cheap to build up front).
- [x] **Keybinding-conflict UI in Settings (UI F-4.1.1).** New `KeybindingConflicts` panel at the top of the Hotkeys settings tab scans the live palette-command list for chords claimed by more than one command and renders a yellow warning banner grouping every colliding entry under its chord. The first-registered command is tagged `"active"`; every other entry shows its command id so the user can scroll down to the row and rebind through the existing `KeyCaptureInput` (which already persists via `keybindings.set_keybinding_override`). The dispatcher's silent first-wins policy is unchanged — this surface just makes the normally-hidden conflict visible.
- [x] **Declarative plugin-panel primitives — `registerPanelView` (UI F-5.2.1).** `PanelNode` primitive union (`vstack` / `hstack` / `text` / `heading` / `button` / `spacer`) added to the contribution registry along with `contributions.registerPanelView(viewId, render)` / `resolvePanelView` / `subscribePanelViews`. A host-owned `makeDeclarativePanelComponent` auto-wires a content-type that walks the plugin's returned tree through a fixed dispatcher (`renderPanelNode`) — no plugin-shipped React, no HTML escape hatch. `ctx.ui.registerPanelView` exposed on `NexusPluginContext` so script plugins can adopt the primitive surface without `registerContentType`. Extending the primitive set is additive — no breaking change required to add `text-input`, `divider`, `section`, etc. when plugins demand them.
- [x] **Per-plugin error boundary in the frontend (UI F-7.2.1).** New `runLifecycle` helper in `scriptRuntime.ts` wraps every `onInit` / `onStart` / `onStop` in a try/catch that records the failure on a new `usePluginStatusStore` (Zustand) keyed by plugin id; the throw is swallowed so plugins loaded later still register. The contribution bridge (`contributions/plugins.ts`) now similarly wraps per-entry registrations in `syncCommands` / `syncPanels` so a single broken contribution cannot abort the rest of the snapshot. Failures surface on the new Running Extensions settings tab (F-10.1.1) with the most recent error message.
- [x] **UI-thread time budget on plugin command dispatches (UI F-8.2.1).** Plugin-originated command dispatches now route through `runWithTelemetry` in `contributions/plugins.ts`, which races the call against a `setTimeout(…, SLOW_COMMAND_CANCEL_MS = 2_000)` macrotask and records every call's elapsed time on the plugin-status store. Dispatches over `SLOW_COMMAND_WARN_MS = 250` flip the plugin's level to `"slow"`; ones that cross the 2 s budget record a failure and return `undefined` to the caller while the in-flight promise settles silently in the background. Slow-plugin telemetry is surfaced in the Running Extensions tab (F-10.1.1).
- [x] **Deprecation channel for the extension API (UI F-9.3.1).** Seeded `DEPRECATED.md` at the repo root documenting the policy (one-minor-release minimum announcement window; one `console.warn` per plugin per deprecated API per load; matching `@deprecated` JSDoc tags once `@nexus/extension-api` lands under UI F-2.1.1) and a "Historical — removed" section recording the pre-1.0 `EditorKeybinding.when` removal. Future deprecations add an entry here and a runtime warning before removal.
- [x] **"Show Running Extensions" tab in Settings (UI F-10.1.1).** New `RunningExtensionsTab` component (`app/src/components/settings/tabs/RunningExtensionsTab.tsx`) enumerates every loaded plugin via `listPlugins()` and merges in live diagnostics from `usePluginStatusStore`: runtime tier, trust level, backend status, level badge (ok / slow / failed), most recent error, slowest observed command + its id, and cold-start `onInit` / `onStart` timings. Registered in `contributions/builtins.ts` under the `plugins` group at order 20 (alongside the existing Plugins tab). Disable / uninstall buttons remain future work — the tab is read-only today, but the store already exposes the telemetry those actions will need.

### 🟡 Yellow — rough edges to fix opportunistically

- [x] **Dogfood the editor as a content-type contribution (UI F-1.1.1).** `FileViewer` is now registered under the canonical `"com.nexus.editor.markdown"` content-type id (with a legacy `"editor"` alias for pre-F-1.1.1 call sites) in `contributions/builtins.ts`. Markdown / MDX file handlers map extensions to that id so the shell reaches the editor through the same contribution pipeline a community plugin would. `PaneView`'s hard-coded `<FileViewer />` fallback remains as a last-resort empty-forge cover, but the primary path now flows through `useContentType`. Moving `EditorSurface` into its own plugin (extracting CM6 from the shell bundle) is a bigger refactor tracked separately.
- [x] **Ship a `DisposableStore` on `ctx` (UI F-2.3.1).** `createDisposableStore()` in `app/src/plugins/nexusContext.ts` backs a new `ctx.disposables` surface with `add` / `dispose` / `size`. `scriptRuntime.ts` allocates one store per plugin at load time (injected into the shared `ctx`) and calls `store.dispose()` from `stopScriptPlugin` after `onStop`, so plugins that push every `register*` return value into `ctx.disposables.add(...)` no longer need to hand-roll a disposal array. The bare-function `Disposable` alias stays for direct-call plugins.
- [x] **Explicit `runtime` field in manifest `[plugin]` (UI F-3.3.1).** New `PluginRuntime` enum (`Native` / `Wasm` / `Script`) exported from `nexus-plugins`. `[plugin] runtime = "…"` is parsed from the manifest when present and must agree with the declared `[wasm]` / `[script]` section — mismatches are rejected with `ManifestInvalid`. For backwards compatibility the field is optional: when absent, the loader infers the tier from the section present so pre-F-3.3.1 manifests keep loading unchanged. Coverage: 5 new parse tests — inferred-from-wasm / inferred-from-script / explicit-runtime-matches-section / mismatch-rejected / unknown-value-rejected, plus an updated "core without wasm" test asserting `runtime == Native`.
- [x] **Implement `when`-clause evaluator or strip the field (UI F-4.1.2).** Stripped. `EditorKeybinding.when` removed from `contributions/registry.ts`; documented in `DEPRECATED.md` as a pre-1.0 removal. Plugins that need conditional activation should branch inside the dispatched command, or wait for a future when-clause evaluator PRD. Keeping the field in the API shape actively misled plugin authors (it was never parsed), so removal is the less-harmful option.
- [x] **Menu-item ordering groups — built-in vs plugin separators (UI F-4.3.1).** `menuItemsSnapshotFn` in `contributions/registry.ts` partitions items per top-level menu into built-ins (no `plugin:` id prefix) and plugin items, sorts each group by `order`, adds `(pluginId, id)` as a stable tiebreaker on plugin items, and forces `separatorBefore: true` on the first plugin item per menu when built-ins are present. `registerMenuItem` clamps any plugin-supplied `order < 0` to `0` (with a warning) since negatives are reserved for built-ins — a plugin can no longer sort itself above the "Save" row.
- [x] **Expose `ctx.workspace` / `ctx.editor.active` APIs (UI F-6.1.1).** Added `ctx.workspace.{root,name}()` and `ctx.editorActive.{relpath,content,isDirty,open}()` on `NexusPluginContext`, wrapping the existing `useForgeStore` / `useOpenFileStore` getters. Read-only for now — write paths still flow through `ctx.ipc.call("com.nexus.storage", …)` with its existing capability checks, and a future capability-gated `ctx.editorActive.applyTransaction` is gated on the iframe sandbox (UI F-8.1.1). Raw `invoke("editor_apply_transaction", …)` from script plugins is now formally discouraged; the new APIs are the blessed surface.
- [x] **Multi-root workspace posture decision (UI F-6.3.1).** **Decision: single-root for the 1.x line; multi-root is a 2.x API break.** Rationale: (a) Nexus' core unit is a "forge" (one knowledge base) rather than a collection of unrelated code trees, so the VS Code multi-root ergonomics matter less than Obsidian's single-vault model; (b) the contribution APIs that currently assume a single root — tree providers, file handlers, snippet file-type filters, URI handlers — would all need a `forgeRoot` parameter if multi-root landed, which is a breaking change we're not ready to absorb before 1.0; (c) switching forges (already implemented via `useForgeStore.open`) covers the "open two projects" workflow that drives most multi-root requests. When a 2.x cycle opens, revisit with a dedicated PRD that specifies which APIs need per-root dispatch vs. aggregate views.
- [x] **Call `onStop` on window close (UI F-7.3.1).** New `stopScriptPlugin(id)` / `stopAllScriptPlugins(budgetMs = 100)` helpers in `app/src/plugins/scriptRuntime.ts` run each loaded plugin's `onStop(ctx)` and flush its `ctx.disposables`, racing each call against a per-plugin budget so a blocked plugin cannot delay window close. `App.tsx` wires `window.addEventListener("beforeunload", …)` to invoke `stopAllScriptPlugins()`, giving every script plugin a best-effort chance to flush debounced saves or file handles before the WebView tears down.
- [x] **`performance.measure` around plugin lifecycle (UI F-10.3.1).** `scriptRuntime::runLifecycle` now brackets each `onInit` / `onStart` / `onStop` call with `performance.mark` + `performance.measure` (labels `plugin:<id>:<hook>`), so cold-start costs show up in DevTools' Performance timeline. The same helper stores the elapsed ms on `usePluginStatusStore.noteLifecycle`, which the Running Extensions tab renders as a "cold start: onInit 23ms · onStart 8ms" line per plugin — the F-3.2.1 scaling problem is now visible without spelunking the DevTools timeline.

### Suspected issues — UI audit §6 spike candidates

- [x] **SI-2 — URI handler dispatch order.** Adopted VS Code's first-match-wins semantics. `contributions.registerUriHandler` now rejects a second registration for a scheme already claimed (warning + no-op disposable), so two plugins cannot silently fight over `nexus://…`. `dispatchUri` breaks after the first matching handler to make the invariant explicit at dispatch time too.
- [x] **SI-3 — Settings modal `clearByPlugin` on uninstall.** Investigated. **Finding: no `plugin disable` Tauri command exists yet** — the only code path that deactivates a plugin's contributions is the hot-reload event (`plugins:reloaded`), and `registerPluginContributions.syncAll` already does the right thing: it disposes every entry in `activeDisposables` before re-registering the fresh snapshot. When a disable / uninstall command is added in the future, it MUST emit `plugins:reloaded` (or a new `plugins:changed` event that funnels into `syncAll`) so the disposable chain runs. This requirement is now captured here and will be enforced by code review on the disable PR.
- [x] **SI-4 — Tree data provider caching across forge switch.** `GenericTreePanel` now subscribes to `useForgeStore(s => s.info?.root)` and includes the root in its effect deps, so switching forges re-runs `provider.getChildren(null)` and rebuilds the tree against the new root. The provider object identity stays stable (plugin-owned), but the panel's local state resets — no stale children render after a forge switch.
- [x] **SI-5 — `queueMicrotask` in CommandPalette.** Swapped `queueMicrotask` for `setTimeout(…, 0)` in `CommandPalette.commit` so dispatch is a macrotask rather than a microtask. React fully commits the palette-close render before the command runs, eliminating the one-frame overlap risk when the dispatched command opens another modal (`workspace.settings`, settings-tab openers, etc.).
- [x] **SI-7 — Snippet trigger collisions.** `contributions.registerSnippet` now scans existing snippets for a matching `trigger` (ignoring same-id re-registrations, which are already handled upstream). On collision the first registration wins; the duplicate is rejected with a console warning that names both plugin ids and the trigger, and a no-op disposable is returned. Mirrors the keybinding policy.

## Decisions — PRD-04 audit (2026-04-17)

- [x] **Service registry — implemented as the IPC command registry.** PRD-04 §8.2's "service registry for plugin-to-plugin discovery" is already satisfied by the existing IPC plumbing: every plugin's `[[registrations.ipc_command]]` entries are aggregated in `PluginLoader::loaded` and `nexus-app` exposes them to the frontend via `list_plugins` + manifest. Discovery is "scan `ui_contributions` / manifest for the target plugin and command id"; invocation is `CompositeIpcDispatcher` (which transparently routes across community → core). A typed `register_service` / `get_service<T>` layer on top would duplicate the IPC surface without adding capability or sandbox value. Decision: do **not** add a separate service registry; revisit only if a concrete plugin needs typed service contracts beyond JSON IPC.
- [x] **Plugin dependency resolution (PRD-04 §12).** `[dependencies]` map is now parsed into `PluginDependency` and validated at load time: missing deps or semver-range mismatches are rejected with `PluginError::DependencyUnsatisfied`. Topological load ordering is the caller's responsibility (bootstrap orders core plugins; community load order is discovery order today).
- [x] **Watchdog: consecutive-timeout quarantine (PRD-04 §13).** `PluginLoader` tracks a per-plugin consecutive-`ExecutionTimeout` counter; hitting `PluginManagerConfig::max_timeout_streak` (default 3) quarantines the plugin — every subsequent dispatch returns `PluginError::Quarantined` until the plugin is reloaded (hot-reload clears state automatically) or the user runs `nexus plugin reset <id>`. The persistent crash counter is bumped at quarantine time so the state survives restart.
- [x] **Extract `nexus-plugin-api` crate (F-2.1.1, F-1.3.1) — partial close, 2026-04-22.** New `crates/nexus-plugin-api` contains `Capability`, `CapabilitySet`, `CapabilityParseError`, `NexusEvent`, `EventFilter`, `EventMetadata`, `PublishedEvent`, `StopReason`, `IpcDispatcher`, `IpcFuture`, `LogLevel`, `TrustLevel`, `PluginInfo`, `PluginStatus`, `IpcError`, `BusError`, `CapabilityError`, plus `PLUGIN_API_VERSION: u32 = 1`. `nexus-kernel`'s capability/event/ipc/log/plugin modules are now shim re-exports from `nexus-plugin-api`. Plugin authors depend only on the new crate — the original audit goal ("any kernel refactor is a silent plugin-compat break") is satisfied for community plugins. `nexus-plugins/Cargo.toml` retains a path dep on `nexus-kernel` (for `EventBus`, `EventSubscription`, `KernelPluginContext`, `KvStore` — all kernel-internal infrastructure used by the loader/sandbox; never linked into community plugin .wasm). `CorePlugin` was not moved — its `wire_context(Arc<KernelPluginContext>)` hook ties it to kernel internals; staying in `nexus-plugins` is correct. Decision (2026-04-22): do **not** pursue host-side severance via dyn-trait-ifying EventBus/KvStore/PluginContext or moving the loader into `nexus-kernel` — the costs (dyn dispatch on hot paths, or inverted layering) exceed the benefit when the only external contract that matters is already insulated. Follow-up "CI guard: `nexus-plugin-api` stays kernel-free" tracked under 🟠 Orange in the open backlog as the cheap discipline that keeps this from regressing.
- [x] **CI guard: `nexus-plugin-api` stays kernel-free — follow-up to F-2.1.1, 2026-04-22.** Two `#[test]`s in `crates/nexus-plugin-api/tests/kernel_free_guard.rs`: one parses the crate's own `Cargo.toml` and asserts no forbidden workspace crate appears under `[dependencies]`, `[build-dependencies]`, or `[target.*.dependencies]`; the other walks `src/**.rs` and rejects stray `use nexus_kernel::…`-style mentions that would survive a dep-removal mid-refactor. Forbidden list: `nexus-kernel`, `nexus-plugins`, plus every other workspace crate that pulls them in transitively. Failure message points at this archive entry for rationale. Cargo's own resolver already rejects the simplest break (cyclic dep) for any current workspace member; the guard earns its keep against external crates re-exporting kernel types, future restructures that break the cycle, and stray imports added mid-refactor.
